# **Quick Search Method**

The purpose of using tags is to facilitate searching for specific combinations of topics. You can search any combination using the following regular expression:

Tags:(.\*)?*Topic1*(.\*)?*Topic2*(.\*)?*Topic3*...

To use it you just have to follow these steps:

1. Press **Ctrl \+ H** or click **Edit** \> **Find and Replace**.  
2. Next to "**Find**", type the expression and click the **Match using regular expressions** option.  
3. Now use the regular expression described above, replacing *Topic1, Topic2,* etc. with the topics of your choosing which can be found in the Glossary section.

Note: This search method is *not* case sensitive, but you have to mind the order of the topics, making sure you place them in alphabetical order.

**Examples:**

1. Alphabetical order:  
   1. Tags:(.\*)?Age(.\*)?Ash \- will work.  
   2. Tags:(.\*)?Ash(.\*)?Age \- will *not* work.

   

2. Case insensitive:  
   1. Tags:(.\*)?Last War(.\*)?Surge \- will work.  
   2. Tags:(.\*)?last war(.\*)?surge \- will work.

   

3. Space before or after the tags:  
   1. Tags:(.\*)?Last War(.\*)?Surge \- will work.  
   2. Tags:(.\*)?Last War (.\*)?Surge \- will not work.  
   3. Tags:(.\*)? Last War(.\*)?Surge \- will not work.

   

4. The amount of topics is *not* important:  
   1. Tags:(.\*)?Ash(.\*)?Mew(.\*)?Pokemon Biology(.\*)?Wild Pokemon \- will work.  
   2. Tags:(.\*)?Ash \- will work.

# **Questions**

## **Q.1. On who is responsible for the Jynxs’ transfiguration.**

- ## *Tags: Articuno, Feather, Haukea, Legendary Birds*

Just wanted to clear up a quick misconception\! Articuno doesn’t bestow a Feather to the Jynx \- that’s Haukea manifesting her own Feather and using it to catalyze the transformation.

## **Q.2. Do all Champions/Future Champions meet Moltres?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Chinatsu, Legendary Birds, Moltres*

Yep, in general Champions only meet Chinatsu. If I remember right, no Champion had met Moltres in centuries.

## **Q.3. Comparison between the Will of Fire concept (Naruto-verse) and Chinatsu’s duty.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Chinatsu, Indigo, League*

Sort of \- Chinatsu is also connected to the Champion’s office for another reason besides offering wisdom. If an Indigo Champion were to go mad or disrespect the authority of their office, who better to put an end to them?

## **Q.4. A young Larvitar’s destructive ability to eat and break stone is matched against a young Rhyhorn’s armor. What emerges as the victor?**

- ## *Tags: Larvitar, Rhyhorn, Pokemon Battle*

Larvitar’s bites would probably be effective at damaging the armor, but Rhyhorn is probably going to figure the game out real quick.

## **Q.5. So does this make Larvitar a major predator?**

- ## *Tags: Geodude, Larvitar, Pokemon Behaviour, Tyranitar*

I see a lone Larvitar as more of a scavenger or picking off weaker Pokémon like young Geodude, while ones with their parents just dig into whatever mama Tyranitar murders.

## **Q.6. Is Mt. Silver as isolated in Traveler as the games?**

- ## *Tags: Conference, Indigo, Indigo Plateau, Mt. Silver, Silver Town*

It’s fairly isolated, but has both the Pokémon League Village and Silver Town nearby. They’re sparsely populated outside of Conferences, however. The only regular human presence on and around Mt. Silver is Indigo Plateau, which is built onto the side.

## **Q.7. Is the shrine \[Chinatsu’s\] built into the Mt. \[Mt. Silver\]?**

- ## *Tags: Chinatsu, Indigo, Indigo Plateau, League, Mt. Silver, Wild Pokemon*

Yep. The League maintains various tunnels for their use. The wild Pokémon are too afraid of Chinatsu to try and infringe on them.

## **Q.8. Is Melmetal a mythical Pokemon Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Melmetal, Mythical Pokemon, Pokemon Biology*

It’s been a while since I visited that lore, but if I remember correctly I had Melmetal as Aura-forged human constructs that were recently discovered. Subject to change, of course\!

## **Q.9. It was mentioned early on that Seadra could learn to levitate after extensive training, I'm guessing it's done through their latent draconic power?**

- ## *Tags: Dragon type, Seadra*

Yep, that’s right. Seadra levitate through their latent draconic power, although it’s quite difficult.

## **Q.10. What do you define aura-forged pokemon to be?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Distortion, Sinnoh, Spiritomb*

And in general you have certain Aura-forged Pokémon created all over the world. When looking at their qualities, you have to realize that their qualities are defined by what their creators needed from them. Guardians, weapons, partners, laborers...there’s a massive range of them. Some are designed with the ability to reproduce to better fulfill their role, while others were denied that power for various reasons. Can you imagine if Spiritomb were capable of easily reproducing? Sinnoh would be a Distorted nightmare.

## **Q.11. Do common people know about this type of aura-forged pokemon? \[see question 10\]**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Spiritomb*

People don’t know they were created by Aura (and some of these Pokémon are still mostly hidden such as Spiritomb) but they know of many of these Pokémon.

## **Q.12. On Infernus’ evolution.**

- ## *Tags: Evolution, Infernus, Magmarizer, Moltres, Technology*

I will say Infernus didn’t get a real power boost from Moltres’ influence on his evolution. I’m not a fan of blatant power ups haha. He’s more or less as strong as he would be if he’d evolved through a Magmarizer. What the experience did leave him with, however, was knowledge and comprehension that’ll help him down the line.

## **Q.13. Does Sabrina not know \[about Ash dying\]?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Death, Psychic, Sabrina*


Sabrina knows \- most powerful psychics will be able to tell that something is at the very least not right with Ash.

## **Q.14. Could it be argued that humans are technically Pokemon?**

- ## *Tags: Human Biology, Meta, Pokemon Biology*


In most continuities, I think yes. In Traveler, that’ll be a no.

## **Q.15. Where are the legendary golems in the strength tree? Are they at a similar level as genesect?**

- ## *Tags: Genesect, Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon, Legendary Titans, Pokemon Battle*


They’re roughly around the level of the Birds, although I don’t want to give too much info on them yet.

## **Q.16. Doesn’t Traveler Lance have a red Gyrados?**

- ## *Tags: Gyrados, Lake of Rage, Lance, Mewtwo, Team Rocket*


Yep, due to the Rockets being mostly broken up by Mewtwo’s temper tantrum, they never went forward with their evolution experiments at the Lake of Rage. Lance just has a normal boring blue Gyarados.

## **Q.17. How many Rockets were there before and after the \[Rocket\] war? How many remain free?**

- ## *Tags: Archer, Ariana, Hoenn, League, Mewtwo, Proton, Rocket War, Team Rocket*


Actual, uniformed Rocket grunts and operatives? A few thousand. Research teams, criminal links, smugglers, and the Rocket network measured in the tens of thousands. Plenty were wiped out by Mewtwo and the League. I’d say there’s something like 1-2,000 Rockets split between the factions in Hoenn, though they’re recruiting as much as possible and making forays into the criminal underworld and poaching rings (exploiting many former links that Pierce organized). 

Proton and Archer are free. Petrel is still in prison, as is Ariana.

## **Q.18. Infernus grunts, right?**

- ## *Tags: Infernus, Pokemon Behaviour*


Snarls, grunts, and roars mostly.

## **Q.19. On Grey’s perspective about battles.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Grey, Pokemon Battle*


He and Ash are basically on the same page where it’s more about the right \[fight\] than the win. Not that either like losing \- they hate it \- but both are in it for the competition instead of just winning.

## **Q.20. If Micheal and Grey had a field battle who would win? By that I mean everyone with each other.**

- ## *Tags: Conference, Grey, Michael, Pokemon Battle*


If you had just their Conference teams they faced Ash with...I'd say it'd be close. I'd lean towards Grey, simply because he's used to hunting down powerful trainers. Michael's team I see as more of an army \- they fight well together and compensate for each other's weaknesses, but Grey's team is designed to be as lethal as possible. He excels in taking down single powerful trainers, whereas Michael is who I would want on my side if I had to take down hundreds of trainers.

## **Q.21. On the topic of Lance, do we know how old he actually is? Traveler info and Recollection stories are contradicting each other.**

- ## *Tags: Age, Champion, Lance, Master Trainer*


Lance is...26? 27, maybe? To be honest I lost the notes I had with his exact age and have just had him categorized as mid-20s. I know he was a Master at 14, Champion at 15 or 16? Can't remember which. He'd been Champion for roughly ten years when Traveler first began, so he's been Champion for a little over 11 years now. That puts him at 26ish. I'll see if I can't dig through my notes and find the exact accurate notes.

## **Q.22. On the southern continent.**

- ## *Tags: Location, Sinnoh, Southern Continent*


There's significantly more to the Southern Continent. I figure the northern cap isn't too far north from Sinnoh.

## **Q.23. Out of curiosity, is Hoenn in line with the Equator?**

- ## *Tags: Hoenn, Location, Southern Continent*


Roughly. I imagine it to be roughly in line with the equator. Perhaps a little north? The Southern Continent is enormous.

## **Q.24. On the official Traveler world map.**

- ## *Tags: Johto, Kanto, Location, Sinnoh, Southern Continent*


Also, keep in mind the proportions for some areas are slightly off. In my mind Sinnoh is much bigger, nearly the size of both Kanto and Johto. I'll edit that in the future, along with the Southern Continent to make it look a little more realistic. That long, smooth strait in the southwest of the Southern Continent is intentional, btw\!

## **Q.25. How hard would it be to take over Viridian Gym when Giovanni is killed?**

- ## *Tags: Giovanni, Indigo, League, Viridian Gym*


Kind of a mess because the League was extremely paranoid about everything to do with the Viridian Gym and figuring out the extent of the corruption and rooting it out.

## **Q.26. Who is the \[Viridian\] gym leader now though?**

- ## *Tags: Giovanni, Indigo, Karen, League, Viridian Gym, Will*


Still having Karen as the substitute for now, but Will shifts in and out once he's back on his feet. They have other League members as well t\[o\] take some of the strain off.

## **Q.27. As things are now\[chapter 51\], how would Ash stack up against Michael?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Conference, Indigo, Michael, Orre, Pokemon Battle*


That's a hard question \[redacted\] and it does kind of come down to the context of the fight. Michael hasn't been resting on his laurels after the Conference down in Orre, but he's definitely specializing to be more like Grey with his team \- less emphasis on individual development and more on members of the team working with one another to maximize effectiveness and compensate for each other's weaknesses. He's training soldiers, not warriors. Ash's team is steadily growing in individual strength, and I think they'd be at least equal to most of Grey's team (minus Jolteon) in one-on-one combat since that's not what Michael is focusing his energy on. If you threw six of Michael's pokemon at six of Ash's, though, it would be a really bloody battle. Ash's team is strong enough to do some major damage, but I think Michael would pick Ash apart through superior teamwork.

## **Q.28. Was it possible for Ash to beat Michael?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Air Lens, Champion, Infernus, Jolteon, Michael, Pokemon Battle*


I'd say that it was possible, but I think it would've been a 1-in-100 shot. Ash would've had to do everything absolutely perfectly, which was extremely tough to do because Michael had way more pokemon than he did and had basically seen every trick Ash had except for Air Lens \- and we saw how effective that was. Without Air Lens and Infernus, Michael would have done serious damage with Jolteon, which was Champion-level.

## **Q.29. Can you tell us all of Oak's team?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Arcanine, Blastoise, Charizard, Dragonite, Exeggutor, Gyarados, Pikachu, Professor Oak, Tauros, Venusaur*


Yep, Oak does have Ash's canon Pikachu at the Corral with him. It's kind of his buddy since most of his other teammates are either living a distance from the Corral or would completely tear the house up.

Tauros, Exeggutor, Arcanine, Charizard, Venusaur, Blastoise, Dragonite, Gyarados, and Alakazam. Maybe a few others, but these are the important ones that made up the core of his team.

## **Q.30. How did Infernus get that far ahead? The exp\[ierence\] from Michael?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Infernus, Michael, Pokemon Behaviour*


Mostly just because he's a broken fighter haha. Even before you factor in his stamina, techniques, and skill at battle you have to consider his devastating, absolutely OP combo of Teleport/Hug that can take down most fighters easily.

And yes, the enthusiasm is definitely a big factor.

## **Q.31. What was its \[Blaine’s Magmar\] rank in its prime?**

- ## *Tags: Blaine, Champion, Magmar*


I'd say B+, so average Champion-level.

## **Q.32. Can you please elaborate on threat levels and how those threats are measured?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Agatha, Champion, Elite Four, Glacia, Grey, Lorelei, Master Trainer, Nomad, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Trainer, Threat Level*


Here's a rough breakdown of the threat-levels.

H: Champion-level threats. Basically someone you'd want to have the entire Elite Four plus ACE Trainers to take down safely.

AAA: High-level Masters. Think Agatha, Glacia, Lorelei, etc. Powerful, experienced Masters. You'd probably want two Elite Four \+ ACE Trainer backup.

AA: Master-level. This is the most common level of Nomadic Masters. They're extremely formidable, but tend to have holes in their teams that can be safely exploited by a prepared team.

A:  Elite trainers like George Grey. Potentially devastating if they run rampant, but not nearly impossible to take down cleanly like a Master.

## **Q.33. What tier is Ash \[around chapter 51\]? in AA?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Legendary Pokemon, Pokemon Battle, Threat Level*


Ash is currently considered by the League to be in A. He's got a few powerhouses and is strong across the board, but more experienced trainers wouldn't have much trouble taking him down in groups. They'd be able to pick him apart due to his inexperience if he didn't have support. In reality, I think they'd treat him more like AA or even S due to his unique ties to the League and, more importantly, his links to the Legends. They don't know exactly what he could do if he went rogue, but they don't want to take chances.

## **Q.34. How far down the list does Steven fall \[in the tier list\] if you take away Metagross?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Metagross, Pokemon Battle, Steven, Threat Level*


Without Metagross I'd say Steven falls to S-tier. He'd be at the top of it, but Metagross is an instrumental part of his team. He'd still be a nightmare to fight, but Metagross does a lot of his offense and softens up (or wipes) the other team. A lot of his other teammates are based around endurance and outlasting the weakened opponents.

Honestly, the rest of Steven's team is more than capable of handling most Masters fairly easily. The biggest issue of losing Metagross would be against Champion-level teams where he's instrumental. Metagross is usually good for taking down their cornerstones and then another teammate, or at least mostly taking them down.

## **Q.35. On Jacqueline Durand’s thead level.**

- ## *Tags: Elite Four, Jacqueline Durand, Karen, Threat Level, Will*


And \[redacted\] \[redacted\] is right. Jacqueline Durand is basically on the level of inexperienced Elite Four members like Will and Karen. In a straight fight she's much more dangerous than they are, however. It's one of the situations where tier lists don't perfectly capture the full picture.

## **Q.36. On the King Under the Mountain participating in regulated matches.**

- ## *Tags: Bruno, King Under the Mountain, Pokemon Battle*


Technically there's nothing stopping Bruiser\[Bruno\] from using the King (other than the problem of actually fitting him in the stadium) but he would never use him in a regulated match. Bruno has too strong of an honor code for that.

## **Q.37. On the King Under the Mountain against a distortion user.**

- ## *Tags: Curse, Destiny Bond, Ghost type, King Under the Mountain, Pokemon Battle*


Yep, ghosts are excellent for taking down overwhelming conventional fighters like that.  
I'd say it might take several Destiny Bonds and Curses to bring the King down \- it's massive enough that it would require a lot more Distortional energy to bring him down.

## **Q.38. On Jon and Amelia being \[around chapter 51\] on Giovanni’s level.**

- ## *Tags: Amelia, Giovanni, Jonathan, Pokemon Battle*


Yep, it's easy to forget that they're pretty powerful in their own right. I mean, in a real fight Giovanni would tear them apart. But in a regulated match they're on roughly even terms.

## **Q.39. On Misty’s level.**

- ## *Tags: Cerulean Gym, Misty, Pokemon Battle, Sensational Sisters*


I put Misty on the level of the Sisters at this point \[around chapter 51\]. We haven't seen her in ages but she has the resources of the Cerulean Gym, training, and plenty of pokemon of her own. She's at least low Gym Leader-level with her personal team.

## **Q.40. Why did you never teach her \[Oz\] teleport as well?**

- ## *Tags: Infernus, Flash, Oz, Teleport*


Mostly it comes down to Oz not having the endurance. It's rough even on Infernus, and she just doesn't have his stamina. I think it would drain her too quickly at this point. She's better off favoring dodges and using things like Flash to overwhelm and disorient a pokemon's aim than teleporting away. Infernus has been a stamina monster from the beginning.

## **Q.41. Wouldn't using it cover and increase her stamina? \[see question 40\]**

- ## *Tags: Dazed, Infernus, Lucario, Oz, Pokemon Battle, Teleport*


It would, but not by a noticeable margin. It might take her from 1-2 times per battle to 2-3, maybe 4\. She wouldn't be able to hop around like Dazed can. Even Infernus uses it mostly as an opening tactic to close distance or desperate defensive moves, like against Lucario.

## **Q.42. Does that mean they \[Exeggutor’s eggs\] are separate entities?**

- ## *Tags: Exeggutor, Pokemon Biology, Psychic type*


Yeah, the most logical solution to me is that they're individuals, but are mentally linked in order to create a hive mind organism. That would probably amplify their psychic abilities as well \- alone I can see them being ridiculously weak.

## **Q.43. On Fairy types.**

- ## *Tags: Alola, Clefable, Fairy type, Galar, Gary, Kalos*


Quick point that's not really a spoiler so much as making people aware of my stance on Fairy-types: Gary's Clefable is not technically a Fairy-type at this moment. You have to go to areas like Kalos, Alola, and Galar for that...at the moment.

## **Q.44. Is Torrent just salty that Clair’s Kingdra used Attract?**

- ## *Tags: Attract, Clair, Kingdra, Pokemon Battle, Torrent*


Pretty much. Nobody was really happy about how that ended, but Torrent is taking it extremely personally. He's been dreaming of this fight and had a chance at an honorable loss or victory yanked away from him.

## **Q.45. So he \[Torrent\] now views Clair’s Kingdra as beneath honor and now would never consider her as a partner?**

- ## *Tags: Clair, Kingdra, Torrent*


I wouldn't say it's that extreme \- I think a rematch would do them both good, though.

## **Q.46. What happens when Ash dies and most of his team outlive him?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Champion, Infernus, Lugia, Moltres, Pokemon Behaviour, Torrent*


A lot of the others I won't spoil, but Torrent goes to Lugia to act as its Champion (like the talking Slowking at Shamouti), and Infernus makes a beeline for the Fire Stone to reclaim it. He fights Moltres for eternity, slowly growing stronger over the centuries until he's able to push past Moltres and reclaim the Fire Orb, then burns the whole world.

Okay, can't confirm the last part, but he'll at least go after the Fire Orb when there are no mundane challenges left.

## **Q.47. What would Infernus do when he’s done all he can?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Infernus, Pokemon Behaviour*


That's something even Infernus wouldn't know. Probably end up getting himself killed on purpose by taking on something way stronger than him.

## **Q.48. We already know that Traveler's got space travel. How far off are we from FTL travel? Any chance we get space odyssey pokemon regions?**

- ## *Tags: Flying type, Space, Rayquaza*


Honestly, the biggest problem is that Rayquaza makes a habit of blasting the space shuttles and satellites out of the sky. Plus a bunch of flying-types take it as a personal challenge to shoot man-made things down. Most of the world isn't very hospitable.

## **Q.49. Comparison between Torrent and Clair’s Kingdra.**

- ## *Tags: Clair, Kingdra, Strength, Torrent*


\[Redacted\] 100% on point. They're at similar levels (Clair's is overall more powerful) but they basically took two different specializations.

## **Q.50. What would it take for a Pokecenter to part with a Chansey?**

- ## *Tags: Chansey, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Center*


A big part would depend on if the Chansey wanted to leave or not. If it did, nobody's stopping them.

## **Q.51. How are Pokecenters not robbed more frequently?**

- ## *Tags: Chansey, League, Pokemon Center*


Let's just say that the League doesn't take kindly to their Pokemon Centers getting attacked. Also, now I'm just imagining various pokemon stealing Chansey eggs to raise them as their own so they can have healers lol.

## **Q.52. On the advantages of organized crime.**

- ## *Tags: Crime, League, Psychic type*


And yep, I wouldn't want to be a criminal without a greater organization. One League psychic scanning brains out in the wilderness would be enough to get you captured.

## **Q.53. How hard would it be to get a trainer license in Traveler if some kid just turned up at Viridian with a pidgey, spearow and poliwhirl and nothing else?**

- ## *Tags: Gym, League, Pokemon Trainer*


Extremely easy. There's some certification tests, but the League WANTS as many trainers as possible. It's the backbone of the economy and an excellent way to naturally develop people with teams that can later find work in industry, law enforcement, etc.

## **Q.54. Do trainers in Traveler get starting funds when they become a trainer?**

- ## *Tags: League, Pokemon Trainer*


I did a horrible job of fleshing out the starting process of being a trainer in a beginning, but the League has a vested interest in making sure the beginning trainers have at least some resources. They want them to succeed and want to ensure pokemon are well-taken care of.

## **Q.55. On the League’s power structure.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Elite Four, League*


The League is the governing body. It's an interesting system in that they're very, very involved in many ways but extremely hands off in others. The Champion is essentially a military dictator with practically unlimited authority. What balances are in place are basically making sure the Champion and Elite Four are of good moral fiber through a series of psychic checks. In practice, the League allows the various territories and cities to govern themselves so long as they abide by the League's laws, but they come down like a hammer when they need to.

## **Q.56. On whether it’s necessary to bond with your Pokemon to reach a high combat level.**

- ## *Tags: League, Master Trainer, Pokemon Behaviour, Team Rocket*


Yep. To reach a high level you have to have some kind of cooperation with your team. They have to like and respect you \- even if they fight out of fear, it's going to hamper them. They can reach Master-level, but it's extremely rare. There's nothing stopping a pokemon from snapping and killing their trainer, and it's hideously easy. There's a reason that the Rockets invested so heavily in breaking down their pokemon for the most part.

## **Q.57. On Giovanni caring for things other than himself.**

- ## *Tags: Giovanni*


One thing to keep in mind with Giovanni is that he did care for things, but in an extremely selfish, narcissistic way. His love is basically seeing things as an extension of himself, as treasured possessions that belong only to him. It's a shallow thing.

## **Q.58. Would the training under a Gravity attack and getting healed with Heal Pulse be applicable in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Gravity, Heal Pulse*


I don't think so. It might work for a bit, but I think you'd get extremely diminishing returns. I see Heal Pulse as a quick-and-dirty way to numb pain and promote some recovery. It'll keep you in fighting condition, but if you use it over and over again the body is going to be utterly exhausted. Plus I think spending a lot of time under Gravity could be rough on a pokemon's system. It could be used as a sporadic regimen, but I wouldn't rely on it.

## **Q.59. In Traveler-verse is pokemon referee a separate profession or is it done by gym trainers?**

- ## *Tags: Conference, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Gym, Pokemon Trainer*


And good question, I haven't really thought about it. I'd say that it can be both \- for big things like Conferences the League probably has ones that they hire, but in Gym battles it's likely that a Gym trainer is just trained to do it.

## **Q.60. People who don't start from say Oak, where do their pokemon go when they have a full team already?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Care, Pokemon Trainer, Professor Oak*


I imagine that there are plenty of other League and private facilities that look after excess Pokemon.

## **Q.61. How does one become a Gym Leader? Like do you have to overthrow the current Leader or does it have to be passed on?**

- ## *Tags: Elite Four, Gym Leader, League*


It's an appointed position. It's not like the Elite Four where a challenger can potentially dethrone you and take your spot. Gym Leaders take care of the League's work on a local level, so they need to be individuals who can be trusted with a high degree of autonomy. You see it passed down through families frequently, but it's definitely not hereditary. Anyone acting as a Gym Leader has to meet the League's requirements.

## **Q.62. In E4 whoever wins gets the spot immediately? Or is there some mentorship period to learn about other aspects of the job/check if the candidate isn't a psycho?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Conference, Elite Four*


Not immediately. They wouldn't be made acting members of the Elite Four until they'd been heavily screened and gone through a mentorship period to prepare for the role, but it's pretty rare that any Conference Champions actually take down one of the Elite Four anyways. What normally happens is that promising Conference Champions lose against the Elite Four and are inducted as Elite Four trainees. Promising candidates are also approached outside Conferences. After a while, they can choose to make a challenge or slot in when a current Elite Four member leaves.

## **Q.63. On whether other Legendary Birds replicate Articuno/Haukea’s relationship.**

- ## *Tags: Articuno, Champion, Haukea, Legendary Birds, Moltres*


FYI for everyone, Haukea is entirely unique. Moltres has a fair number of mortal Champions \- it likes to invest. Articuno's only Champion is Haukea.

## **Q.64. On what caused Zapdos to leave at the end of The Storm.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Mewtwo, Zapdos*


If you're talking about Zapdos, then basically Mewtwo's mental struggle against it while he was still hampered by his power-limiting armor was what grounded it and caused it to roost. But Ash got it to leave of his own volition.

## **Q.65. On Mewtwo’s impact on the behaviour of Zapdos.**

- ## *Tags: Mewtwo, Pokemon Behaviour, Zapdos*


It was sort of a situation where everything would've been fine without Mewtwo...which kind of describes most of the plot, now that I think about it. Basically Mewtwo discovered Zapdos while it was passing through as normal, attacked it mentally, then Zapdos was exhausted and decided to sleep for a little while to recover.

## **Q.66. On what is the Dark World.**

- ## *Tags: Dark World, Indigo, Rota*


The Dark World is the region north of Indigo and Rota, surrounded by huge walls of mountains where a lot of stuff gets weird.

## **Q.69. Say I got a Venusaur, what would be the advantages of teaching him solar or hyper beam?**

## **Q.70. So because of Lance the cape is associated with championship, while in reality it's a Wataru thing. So he basically ties the clan to the position?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Drake, Lance, Wataru Clan* 


It's actually been associated with the Champion's position for centuries now, but it had its origins in the many, many Drakes that achieved the Champion's position. As political powerhouse warlords trained from birth (not to mention easy access to some of the most powerful pokemon around) they had a disproportionate number of Champions counted in their ranks, especially in the old days before training advanced to where it is now. As time went on more and more Champions naturally took up a cloak or mantle, and eventually it became part of the tradition.

## **Q.71. That \[previous question\] still makes me wonder if that had an effect on the Hoenn League. They also have a Champion's Cape, in the exact inverted colors of Lance's.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Ever Grande, Indigo, Lance, League*


I do see the Ever Grande League Champion having an official cape/mantle they wear for ceremonial purposes, but it's not a constant thing like Lance's. The other Leagues modeled the League system off Indigo, so it would make sense for them to take elements from that.

## **Q.75. How do trainers catch Abra and other teleporters? Wouldn't they be able to teleport when they're released after being caught?**

- ## *Tags: League, Pokemon Trainer, Psychic type, Wild Pokemon*


Sure, basically the League has a ton of psychics posted throughout the wilderness to generally keep an eye on wild pokemon, trainers, and to know when to reach out to help others. It's just a good tool. It's very easy for them to sense distress, and they'll often check in on it. I don't want to go in too much detail yet.

## **Q.77. How strong is the Shamouti Slowking compared to say Lance's Dragonite or Chinatsu?**

- ## *Tags: Chinatsu, Chosen One Prophecy, Dragonite, Shamouti, Slowking*


Shamouti Slowking is kind of in an interesting place compared to Chinatsu. On paper, it has the ability to be an incredibly powerful opponent \- basically able to use its psychic abilities and control over the ocean to an incredible scale we haven't seen elsewhere. But Chinatsu would probably beat it despite that. Slowking is more of a mentor or loremaster, meant to oversee the Prophecy and guide heroes. Chinatsu is a warrior through and through.

- ## *Tags: Chinatsu, Champion, Mamoru, Moltres, Will-O-Wisps*

If you took her ability to decompose into Will-o-Wisps away from her, Mamoru might have a chance, but that would just leave her a glass cannon who could still feasibly burn right through his armor.

## **Q.79. Just looked at tiers in FAQ. Does it mean that Chandelure was the strongest of Grey's pokemon (not Hydreigon)?**

- ## *Tags: Chandelure, Hydreigon*


Different strengths, I'd say. If you want something taken down physically, go for Hydreigon. Chandelure is more for nasty things like Infernus that are almost impossible to take down conventionally. Chandelure definitely has the edge on Hydreigon because of how reckless and aggressive it is. It would walk right into traps.

- ## *Tags: Jolteon, Michael*

## **Q.81. Can Ditto transform into a ghost in The Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Ditto, Galarian Corsola, Gengar, Ghost type, Pokemon Biology*


I'd say it depends on the ghost since Ditto requires some kind of DNA to latch onto. Galarian Corsola, yes. Trevenant,  yes. Gengar? No. Ditto needs something to work with, so if a ghost uses something entirely inorganic it's a hard counter to Ditto. But Ditto in Traveler (experienced ones at least) are also capable of storing DNA for later use, although it degrades over time.

## **Q.82. What happens if it transforms into Mew?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Darkrai, Ditto, Mew, Mewtwo*


Ditto's transformation into Mew would be like Mew's transformation into Darkrai. Probably fairly powerful (but like, Alakazam level) but with complete inexperience with the limited psychic powers it could access.

Plus, it depends on how efficient Mew is at cleaning up the DNA it leaves behind...it can't be too good because Mewtwo is a thing, but I think Mew would be either a little too intrigued for Ditto's own good or slightly offended.

## **Q.84. During Brave Bird, is it the feathers that burn, an energy cloak that burns or a bunch of matter materialised from energy that burns?**

- ## *Tags: Brave Bird, Hyper Beam*

I see it as less actual flames \- to a point, anyway \- than it is a sort of aura that results from the pokemon's power. One of the harder questions to answer, and it's subject to change as I think about it more.

## **Q.85. It was discussed here, and you also wrote it clearly in the story that the Pokenav was a fairly new thing. Will Ash be getting an upgrade technology wise? Like an updated Pokedex or Xtransreciever or something?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, PokeDex, PokeNav, Stone Family, Technology*


Ash will most likely be getting a new technology upgrade, but it's most likely going to be an upgraded PokeNav since he's so close to the Stones. He already has the national dex upgrade.

## **Q.86. Did the Pokemon come into existence naturally through evolution by itself? Or did Mew assist this at some point and then let it go on by itself afterwards?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Evolution, Legendary Pokemon, Mew*


Good question\! Essentially life began as it did in our universe over the course of millions and millions and millions of years. Everything was fairly standard other than the fact that the Legendaries existed \- basically, life would constantly get reset due to the Legends rampaging uncontrolled. The planet was just too unstable for life to flourish. Single-celled, microscopic, and smaller, more adaptable forms of life would survive just fine and grow back and evolve in new ways, but then a big Legendary event would take place every few thousand years and completely mess everything up. The planet was just inhospitable to advanced life. As the Guardian of Life, Mew was very, very bored and frustrated by this arrangement. It gave life the kickstart it needed and basically engineered the progenitors of pokemon, which would be hardy and tough enough to survive Legendary clashes (or at least give them a chance to escape). Mew basically created them, dumped them all over the planet, and let things proceed naturally after that. That's not the whole story, but it's enough for now.

So yeah, it's basically both. Mew basically provided the foundation that would be able to survive the inhospitable earth, but otherwise evolution proceeds as normal. This is the rough version, at least. I could go into more detail but I'd rather save that for a later time.

## **Q.87. On Plume’s speed.**

- ## *Tags: Flying type, Plume*


Before I went to work I figured I'd pop in here and address the discussion real quick. Honestly, I don't want to jump to assigning actual numbers to Plume because I'm not knowledgeable enough about aerodynamics and the physics involved to handle it like I do with certain biological questions. Basically, we'll just stick to that she's really, really fast and can at minimum break the sound barrier pretty easily haha. I have an idea of her speed that I use for travel purposes, but I don't feel comfortable assigning exact numbers to it\!

## **Q.88. All this wondering about the regions has me wonder how people travel between them? Ships? Planes? Trains? Which is the most used?**

- ## *Tags: Dark World, Ranger Union, Region, Sinnoh, Technology, Teleport, Wild Pokemon*


Interregional travel can be pretty complicated. Ferries exist between nearby regions, but it can be dangerous to take them out on the open sea. Trains and planes used to be very common and popular (there was a train network around the edges of the Dark World and through the Ranger Union, which was formerly a Sinnoan territory) but were very expensive and had to be constantly repaired. A single disgruntled wild pokemon could tear huge portions of the railroad up, so it was extremely resource intensive \- wild pokemon (much more aggressive than the ones in the League regions) had to be bribed, huge numbers of trainers had to be committed, and it was still down pretty frequently. Nowadays with how training has advanced, psychic 'taxi' services exist to teleport in several jumps between regions, or you can fly there with certain services. Teleportation is most common, and with the advent of matter-energy conversion technology (aka pokeballs and storage compartments we see in Traveler) the train networks and roads have fallen into relative disrepair. Their main use was always shipping cargo (it's easy for individuals to get around on pokemon) and when you can just put tons and tons of material in a lightweight 'pokeball', it's much easier to just have a psychic teleport a bunch of those to their destination. Cheap and extremely efficient.

## **Q.89. Is there a reason people can’t be sent via Pokéball technology?**

- ## *Tags: Technology*


Good question\! There's several reasons that will later be explained in-story, but the most important one is that humans are pretty flimsy and fragile compared to pokemon. We aren't robust, and our bodies and minds don't handle the conversion particularly well. It won't kill you, but repeated attempts...well, you might wish you were dead. It takes a toll.

## **Q.90. If it's not too spoilery, why are those mountains in the middle of the Dark World not shadowed? Are they above whatever miasma permeates the place?**

- ## *Tags: Dark World*


Unlike most of the map, that's something that doesn't have a reason behind it haha. The mountains should be black as well, but the map software I used didn't color it. It's an oversight on my part. That said, they do mark something significant.

## **Q.91. Would you be able to say how strong Volcarona is considered in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Bug type, Dragonite, Fire type, Pseudo Legendary, Salamence, Volcarona*


Volcarona are somewhat seen as pseudolegendaries like Dragonite and Salamence. Very rare and powerful and with a major cultural influence on their region. In battle, I think that they're a little more vulnerable than a dragon but with more elemental powers. Also, they're excellent against psychics.

## **Q.92. Do all Leagues have ACE trainers? Or are they different in every region?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, ASTRE Trainer, Galar, Kalos, National League, NOBLE Trainer, SEEK Trainer, Unova*


That's right, ACE is standard for the National League with various specialized groups under that umbrella. Kalos has ASTRE, Unova has SEEK, Galar has NOBLE.

## **Q.93. Do the national league regions speak the same language?**

- ## *Tags: Galar, Hoenn, Kalos, Language, League, National League, Sinnoh, Unova, Unown*


The National League does speak the same  official language, since all of the humans in that area have a common origin. There's a lot of regional dialects and stuff, but as communication has improved and ties grew closer, the differences have been smoothed out so long as you don't go to an isolated area. Sinnoh's full of villages and towns in hidden away mountain valleys that barely ever see visitors, so you're a lot more likely to have communication gaps there \- in general, the farther you get from a main city in Sinnoh the less you'll be able to understand anyone. Hoenn's archipelago is similar, but the mainland has been connected through trade to Indigo for so long that there was a lot of common ground. Unova, Kalos, Galar, etc. have different languages from the National League's. I'm no linguist, but since their written languages are all based on the Unown I imagine it would be very easy for them to communicate in writing between different cultures, and possibly have similar phonetics? I'm not sure about that, but I do feel it's easier for different cultures to communicate and bridge gaps since they all have a similar written alphabet. Hard to say for certain.

- ## *Tags: Psychic type, Unown*


Now I just imagine all the Unown's psychic cries just sounding like a text-to-speech device when there's multiples of the same letters like that.

## **Q.96. How is pollution in other regions?**

- ## *Tags: Alola, Galar, Johto, Kalos, Kanto, Pollution, Region, Rustboro City, Sinnoh, Technology, Unova*


And pollution kind of varies from region to region. Unova and Kanto are probably the worst due to being heavily industrialized, but it's much, much better than it was in the past due to technological advancements. It definitely doesn't hurt that wild pokemon get absolutely pissed and start wrecking things when pollution and human influence gets too disruptive. Hoenn is really, really good on the pollution front outside of Rustboro, while Sinnoh, Johto, Kalos, and Galar are all pretty good at handling it. Alola is barely habitated compared to the others, so it only has a few pollution hotspots.

## **Q.97. On Hoenn’s climate.**

- ## *Tags: Hoenn, Legendary Pokemon, Region*


Yep, definitely a north South American or Caribbean feel. Very tropical. Of course, its pristine environment is partly responsible to the angry Legends that nuke civilization every few thousand years haha.

## **Q.98. About the language thing in FAQ, how would basing all the regions language on Unown work if Unown aren't native to all the post Sinnoh regions? \[see question 93\]**

- ## *Tags: Greenfield, Region, Ruins of Alph, Sevii Islands, Sinnoh, Unown*


My current thinking is that Unown were once fairly widespread, scattered all over the place in caches. It's only over thousands of years that they aggregated into massive hordes like the one we saw in Greenfield \- they were intentionally collected and sealed away in protected areas like the Ruins of Alph and the Sevii Islands so that their power would be unreachable. Isolated caches are still found in modern day, but it's usually only four or five Unown that weren't discovered and added to the hoards.

## **Q.99. Do you carry momentum during teleportation?**

- ## *Tags: Physics, Psychic type, Teleport*


Psychics and teleportation are hard to pin down, but my current thinking is that momentum can be kept depending on the skill of a psychic. Most psychics aren't capable of it, and those that tend to be psychic-types that wouldn't get much use out of keeping momentum since they tend to be more stationary fighters. That's my current thinking, anyways.

## **Q.100. On Gallade’s potential psychic specialization.**

- ## *Tags: Gallade, Psychic type*


Yep, I'd say Gallade is the optimal one for that technique \[described in the answer to question 99\]. It's just not worth training most psychics in, but it would be incredible in a Gallade's hands.

## **Q.101. Which of the teams \[Aqua or Magma\] will be the oldest?**

- ## *Tags: Archie, Crime, Hoenn, League, National League, Southern Continent, Team Aqua, Team Magma*


Aqua and Magma are roughly the same age, but they're really just organizations that mobilized and organized preexisting movements. Magma drew heavily on industrial, pro-human, and real estate groups due to their mission to create new land for humanity to settle. They have MASSIVE financial backing from various groups. In the Traveler world, it's almost impossible to expand beyond the major regions. The world outside of civilized regions is basically a massive death trap full of pokemon unused to humanity and not particularly interested in sharing their territory. Expansion is possible, but it progresses at a snail's pace and can be wrecked at any point if there's a diplomatic issue with the local pokemon. There's a reason the Southern Continent is basically empty and that the frontier regions are unable to really thrive. Magma's mission is to avert the issue entirely by producing new land without current pokemon inhabitants, allowing humanity a chance to grow beyond the core regions.

Aqua is basically the opposite. They're drawn from the Hoenn archipelago, which is incredibly isolated and traditional. Archie basically just organized them as a protective force to make up the difference against rampant poachers and criminals hiding out in the archipelago. Due to how young the Hoenn League is (and their comparative lack of development compared to the other National League regions) the League completely lacks the manpower to effectively patrol the archipelago and stick mostly to the mainland and major centers. That left a void for Archie to fill, and things basically progressed from there.

## **Q.102. \[Does\] the Magma land creation involves island creation, similar to the contemporary efforts in the South China Sea? How does that affect the seafloor pokemon? Archie's just the local hegemon, and his (and Aqua's) interest in Kyogre is presumably more inspired by culture than pragmatic desires?**

- ## *Tags: Archie, Kyogre, Team Aqua, Team Magma, Wild Pokemon*


Yep, that's their current 'proof of concept'. They've been doing work on that for some time now, although they're running into exactly the problems you mentioned. They have to work with local pokemon (who usually want bribes), it's an expensive process, and there's always pokemon that do decide to say screw it and attack or harass them anyways.

And yeah, Archie as a local hegemon is a good way to look at it. Very charismatic, offers hope, and provides a sense of unity that the humans of the archipelago haven't had in centuries.

## **Q.103. Why bother making new land when it amounts to the same issues \- maybe it comes down to the laws the Ever Grande League has in place?**

- ## *Tags: Ever Grande, League*


And yep, the Ever Grande League is extremely protective of the archipelago. They can't practically patrol and control it, but they make up for it by fiercely protecting it when they can. It's part of the treaty that got the islanders into the League in the first place \- it's basically a protected zone.

## **Q.104. What’re your thoughts on which Pokémon get Teleport, and what exactly Gravity is?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Dazed, Gardevoir, Gravity, Hypno, Metagross, Psychic type, Steven, Teleport*


Honestly, I'd give Teleport to most psychic pokemon (and ones that have psychic potential) since it seemed to be ubiquitous in Gen I. However, the big difference is how effective they are at it. Even powerful psychics like Dazed might only be good for short jumps, and even then it's exhausting. Very few pokemon are actually GOOD at teleportation. There's a reason pokemon like Gardevoir and Alakazam are overrepresented in the Teleportation Squads I've shown so far. They have a natural affinity for space manipulation, while other pokemon like Hypno have natural affinities for mental and emotional manipulation. Metagross, as mentioned in the Steven training chapters, is a natural at physical manipulation (psychic barriers, producing and manipulating force, etc). Metagross can teleport, but it's very difficult for them since their talents lie elsewhere, plus their huge mass makes it significantly more difficult and draining to control. Hope that explains some of my thoughts on it.

As for Gravity, that's a tough one. For most pokemon, I imagine them to basically perform the simplistic version of the technique in which they use their psychic abilities to simulate increased weight \- basically dragging things down somewhat passively with their abilities. Others are a little more clever and use a small fraction of the energy to make a pokemon THINK their weight has been increased massively, thus influencing their behavior. In general, I think Metagross uses it more as a single-target technique in order to yank fliers out of the sky.

## **Q.105. Would pokemon be able to affect spacetime to actually simulate increased gravity on the battlefield? Or would that be too energy intensive?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Gravity, Psychic type*


Plausible, but exhausting. I think you'd see that as almost an artform amongst psychics, a sign of true talent and training \- all you really need is to use psychic power to weight things down in a fight. But something like an ancient Alakazam would probably take pride in performing genuine space-time manipulation to mimic the effect simply to demonstrate its mastery. That's ridiculously rare, though. When you're a powerful enough psychic that truly understands your power, it starts opening doors.

## **Q.106. Mew and Mewtwo are comparatively weak among Legendaries\!?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Legendary Pokemon, Mew, Mewtwo, Sabrina*


In the grand scheme of things, yes. But they're about as powerful as it gets for the Legends that actively intervene in mortal affairs. The others are just too far above it. And yep, that's right. That was Sabrina's Alakazam \- I modeled the technique off of what Mewtwo and Mew did in the First Movie with their psychic bubbles. Figured it would be really cool to explore in more detail in that fight haha.

## **Q.107. Dazed's Clone was using something like the psychic bubble right? Is it possible for her to do the same or was that only possible as a result of Mewtwo's genetic modification and empowering mortal psychics?**

- ## *Tags: Dazed, Metagross, Mewtwo, Psychic type*


Technically Dazed could do it, but it wouldn't be worth the trouble. It would take extensive training to get that technique down, and she doesn't really have the capacity for it. Metagross probably could, but Metagross also wouldn't be creative enough to use it as anything but a battering ram. Dazed's clone was only able to use it effectively because she was channeling Mewtwo's ambient power to enhance her abilities.

## **Q.108. Does Dazed have an ability to grab projectile attacks and fling them back on their user without them blowing up in the process? It'd sure even the score between her and Torrent, for example, if she could grab one of his dragon pulses and huck it back at him.**

- ## *Tags: Dazed, Dragon Pulse, Torrent*


Things always get tricky with projectile attacks like Dragon Pulse haha. I think she could do it, and we will see something along those lines in the future...

## **Q.109. To be honest I kinda get the feeling Ash is training Dazed more like an Alakazam would. Beyond Hypnosis and Dream Eater there's not much showing in her mental arts.**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Ash, Dazed, Dream Eater, Hoenn, Hypno, Hypnosis, Psychic type*


Yep, and a big part of combat is 'Just because you can, doesn't mean you should'. There are plenty of cool, effective techniques they can learn that just aren't going to be as effective as fighting with simpler, more practical options. Some things are possible, but sometimes it's better to go with the easy, reliable way of doing things. And \[redacted\] yep, that's going to be a big part of her development going forward. Ash has realized already that he's neglected that side of her. She's probably in the top 1% of Hypno for generating force and raw power, but she's lagging behind in the mental skills. Rounding her out will be a major part of her Hoenn arc.

## **Q.110. The question that's been keeping me up at night is whether the clearly best written characters in pokemon, Sordward and Shielbert, exist in the Traveler universe. Do this dynamic duo reign supreme in Galar? Is their lore morally complex and deep?**

- ## *Tags: Galar, Shielbert, Sordward*


I can confirm that they exist \[redacted\] and will have an interesting part to play in the VERY FAR future, but I won't get into the specifics just yet.

## **Q.111. What is the reasoning behind the normal animal descriptions for some pokemon? For example, Grey calls Amelia's Raichu a 'rat' in his battle against her. Are 'normal' animal names extant in the Traveler verse as a sort of general word for some broader types of pokemon? Kind of like a more vulgar species name? (vulgar in the low sense, not the obscene) Would it be uncommon for someone to be called, say, a 'Unovan dog' or whatnot?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Language*


Basically terms like that are used to refer to categories of physiologically similar pokemon. It's a general term. When I'm writing from Ash's POV I tend to try and keep to more 'scientific' sounding names like canine, feline, etc.

## **Q.112. Why does Erika not care about her territory?**

- ## *Tags: Celadon City, Erika, Gym Leader, Gym Trainer, Indigo, League, Surge, Team Rocket*


On the battling front, Erika is more than competent enough to qualify as a Gym Leader (and she meets the physical requirements as well). The physical requirements aren't too demanding, honestly, it's mostly just making sure you're capable of keeping up in a fight. She's definitely not in as good of shape as, say, Surge but she can run and has stamina. The biggest problem with Erika is that she's a perfectly acceptable Gym Leader in peace time \- she's very well-connected and competent in the administrative part \- but served EXTREMELY poorly in times of crisis. She's a manager, not a hunter. She was content to sit back and let the police handle things, usually making appearances as muscle and using her Gym Trainers as force amplifiers, and wasn't nearly as aggressive in hunting down criminal elements as she should have been. She did the bare minimum and figured the League and police would be able to handle the rest. Without that hunter mentality and aggression the other Gym Leaders have, the sprawling metropolis of Celadon was easy for Rockets to establish a presence in and spread corruption. She was too passive and content to let others do the heavy lifting, and without going full Sabrina or Surge Celadon was the perfect environment for the Rockets to trench themselves in.

For her current position, let's just say 'thin ice' isn't fragile enough.

I see Erika as someone who needed direct pressure constantly applied \- without it, she was more than happy to just stick to her regular duties and wait for the storm to blow over.

## **Q.113. How does one challenge for a gym leader position? \[...\] Does the champion have the option to leave entirely, or displace one of their elites, depending on preference?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Conference, Drake, Elite Four, Gym Leader, Hoenn, League, Michael, Steven*


I'll start with Elite Four first since that's simpler: If you win a Conference, you have the option of challenging the Elite Four. Even if you fail to defeat any (the normal result) like Michael, you'll still generally be approached by the League to join as an Elite Four trainee or other League position if they think you're of sound mind and good moral character. Even if you do win a challenge, that's how you start out. After a training period (usually of at least one year) you have the option to challenge the Elite Four again. You can supplant the highest ranked member that you defeat, and the Elite Four members above you are shifted down.

For Champions, if you defeat the Champion you go through a training period before taking your position. The former Champion has the option of becoming the highest ranked member of the Elite Four (like Drake in Hoenn after Steven's victory) or leaving entirely. Most choose to leave \- by the time a worthy challenger comes along they're normally tired of the duty.

Now for Gym Leaders: Normally, you have to go through League training and join as a Gym Trainer, then potentially make your way up to the minor Gym Leader position, then eventually you can challenge for the true Gym Leader position. That's the normal process. Occasionally, the League will appoint a talented trainer they have faith in to an empty spot, but they are given a high degree of oversight. They have to be careful when handling powerful, more experienced trainers \- you don't want to shove someone overqualified into a minor Gym Leader role or they'll get bored and leave. It's rare, however, and the League prefers to draw from their own ranks.

## **Q.114. If you win a conference, can you challenge the elite four whenever you want?**

- ## *Tags: Conference, Elite Four, League*


No, I figure there's a set period after the Conference is over that you can challenge the Elite Four the first time. After that, unless you join the League, you have to win a Conference all over again or be invited to rechallenge them by the League.

## **Q.115. How's the typical training for an Elite Four trainee?**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Elite Four, Karen, Master Trainer, Will*


Typical training is definitely more similar to what Karen and Will got. They're basically official members of the Elite Four in all but name \- it's very nice to have additional Master or near-Master trainers to draw on \- and are being trained to handle their duties and hone their teams. Usually they'll be paired up with members of the current Elite Four that have similar specialties \- Karen with Agatha, for example.

## **Q.116. What is the overall job of gym leaders, E4 and champions?**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Champion, Elite Four, Gym, Gym Leader, Hoenn, League, Ranger, SPECTRE Corps, Wild Pokemon*


Gym Leaders: Manage a specific territory. On paper they have practically unlimited power to administer and enforce laws, but in practice they work closely with local authorities. They're the ultimate authority in their territory, however. They are based out of the major cities of each territory and provide support and oversight to Rangers, League personnel, and the minor Gyms.

Elite Four: The Champion's hands. They tend to take over a certain duty related to their specialties \- Agatha handled the criminal underworld of Indigo, as well as handling the SPECTRE program \- but rarely have a list of official duties other than 'do what the Champion asks'. The commonalities tend to be training other League forces, especially Gym Leaders. It's a very flexible position.

Champion: Protect the region from internal and external threats. Essentially a benevolent military dictator, checked by literally hundreds of psychics before they can assume the role \- with how much power Champions wield, it's essential to ensure they are of good character. In practice, however, they tend to be very hands off in civil matters and allow local authorities to regulate themselves so long as they abide by the League's laws. One of the biggest responsibilities of the Champion \- and the League as a whole \- is managing relations with the wild pokemon of a region, which often involves making sure feeding stations are well supplied, Rangers provide support to wild pokemon to defend them (otherwise wild pokemon start defending themselves, and that gets ugly really quick), and keeping wild pokemon settled and happy.

## **Q.117. Does evolution grant the Pokemon extra lifetime or vice versa?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Bug type, Human Biology, Pokemon Biology*


It does depend on the pokemon, but I think on average evolution will extend a pokemon's life. I imagine many pokemon like somewhere around the natural lifespan of a human (60-80) while you have many bug-types that die sooner (30-50 years) and many, many, many pokemon that can live for centuries or indefinitely depending on their natural environment.

## **Q.118. How do friendship evolutions work in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology*


Friendship evolutions tend to be characteristics of social pokemon. They are linked to positive emotions which often come from being healthy and accepted \- or high \- in a hierarchy. It's basically a sign that they're growing well and succeeding.

## **Q.119. Was there an answer from Elf about Volt Tackle and whether it was exclusive to the Pikachu line?**

- ## *Tags: Electivire, Pikachu, Pokemon Biology, Volt Tackle*


Volt Tackle, for now, is not restricted to the Pikachu line but it tends to be one of their signatures \- their small bodies are ideal for it, and makes it far more efficient for them to use than something like Electivire.

## **Q.120. So the psychological requirements of evolution are pretty much like what Bruiser faces, right?**

- ## *Tags: Bruiser, Machoke, Pokemon Biology*


Yep, Bruiser's really trapped himself. He needs to embrace his power and lose that fear. I think his gentle nature is something that makes him an essential part of the team, but it's hampering him in this instance. A more aggressive Machoke would have evolved already in his body.

## **Q.121. How does one proceed with the E4 challenge? Do you battle each of them right after another (like in games) or it's one battle a day or something like that?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Elite Four, Master Trainer, Pokemon Battle*


The Elite Four challenge is a slow and grueling process. We can throw the first chapter's idea of it away as early installment weirdness haha. It's essentially one battle per three days (assuming you make it past the first battle) in order to give your team proper time to recover. Those battles are intense and grueling, and even a Champion wouldn't be able to just battle their way through the Elite Four with a team of 6\. It's impossible when it comes to Master-level combat.

## **Q.122. Do primary typings exist in the Traveler-verse? Is it that it's down the individual? Like One sneasel is more ice type then dark and another is more dark than ice? Is it the same for all like in their pokedex entries? Or does the concept of primary type not exist at all?**

- ## *Tags: Clair, Dragon type, Kingdra, Pokemon Biology, Torrent, Water type*


Types are basically just a description of a species' attributes \- I think you can view their primary type as more of their core, if that makes any sense, but it depends on the species. You're going to generally see variance in different pokemon of the same species due to learning different techniques and being exposed to different teachers (in either the wild or a trained pokemon). A good example of this was in \[the\] last chapter \[chapter 52\] with Torrent and Clair's Kingdra, which are roughly on the same level but have basically specialized in different ways. Torrent is far more focused on water-type techniques while Clair's Kingdra focuses on the dragon-type. It's just due to their different training and experiences.

## **Q.123. Where does Alola fall on the timeline in Traveler? Has the league been established? On that note too, how are ultra beasts treated in your canon? Are they on the same level as the legendaries, or are they trainable?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Alola, Ash, Sinnoh, Ultra Beasts*


The way I'm treating it is that each region in the anime equates to one year of traveling. So by the time anime Ash got to Sinnoh, for example, I would have Ash as 14\. By Alola he'd be 17, so it's still a very long way off. That's just a general rule, however, and I do change certain parts up on occasion. Ultra Beasts aren't something I've developed quite enough to get into yet \[by 2020.04.27\] \- they exist in some form, but I'm still working on my plans for them haha.

## **Q.124. Are you going to deal with the Orange Islands? Or is that just gone?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Orange Islands, Region*


Nah, with how long Traveler will already be I'm trying to mostly stick to the main regions. There's a chance we might see Ash visit the Orange Islands again for a chapter, but there's not a plan for it currently in the works.

## **Q.125. Would it be spoilers to ask what Michael's main team was?**

- ## *Tags: Claydol, Jolteon, Michael, Pokemon Battle*


Michael was unique in that he very frequently swapped his team out in order to help purify and build bonds with them. Plus, when they did get injured it was serious and required much more time off. So he cycled a lot of his team, but Jolteon was a constant and he really liked Claydol as well for its defensive abilities.

## **Q.126. Does he \[Lance\] see any justice in a system like that \[Galar being controlled by Macro Cosmos\]? Does he tolerate it? Loathe it?**

- ## *Tags: Lance, Galar, Indigo, League, Macro Cosmos, Region*


Admittedly I'm not familiar enough with Galar to give a definite answer, so this is subject to change. My current interpretation has Galar as extremely isolationist, with little contact with other regions. There's trade, but it's fairly limited. Galar is largely self-sufficient and only has nominal ties to other Leagues for reasons we'll dive into later. Knowing Lance, I think he's mostly just neutral to it. Probably not a fan of the heavily corporate and political nature of its tournament system, but he largely just ignores them. That would probably be what rankles him most. Lance is an egalitarian, and I think he wants as many people competing as possible.

## **Q.127. What will your take on the Klinklang line be?**

- ## *Tags: Claydol, Klinklang, Pokemon Biology, Spiritomb*


I haven't put too much thought into them to be honest. I definitely consider them to be \[more\] biological than an artificial construct like Claydol or Spiritomb, albeit a very oddly shaped one. Unfortunately I haven't really come up with any special lore for them haha.

## **Q.128. Is Torrent \[around chapter 52\] at/near the level of Mamoru due to the teachings of Suicune?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Mamoru, Suicune, Torrent*


Nope, not even close. Torrent is where Mamoru was approximately nine centuries ago when he was taking his first steps into the power.

## **Q.129. How long can a Kingdra live?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Kingdra, Pokemon Biology*


Kingdra can live \~200 years in their natural environment. They're very passive in the wild, rarely venturing out of their nests other than to hunt or search for mates.

## **Q.130. Torrent's gonna head out for Lugia after Ash passes right? Is he gonna get a lifespan extension like Slowking?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Champion, Concept, Legendary Pokemon, Lugia, Pokemon Biology, Torrent*


For the most part, pokemon bonded to Legends as their mortal Champions are immortal, tied to the Concept itself. They're immortal until they leave their Legend's service. There are exceptions.

## **Q.131. How are Banette created in Traveler? Does an existing ghost inject some of their essence \- like a curse \- into an old doll to just make them?**

- ## *Tags: Banette, Ghost type, Pokemon Biology*


Pretty much. Strictly speaking, the Banette don't have to pick an old doll or abandoned toy. But that's how the first Banette reproduced, and so it's a bit of a compulsion for them to find something old and worn out and abandoned and take it for their corporeal form.

## **Q.132. Is there a demarcation between where a ghost is a Banette or, say, a Rotom possessing an appliance? Both are ghosts inhabiting different man-made things. What's the fundamental difference? Can they leave their things and still be considered Banette?**

- ## *Tags: Banette, Distortion, Ghost type, Pokemon Biology, Rotom, Shuppet*


Shuppet are what I imagine to be proto-Banette, or Banette without corporeal forms. It's due to their 'bodies' being too badly damaged, regressing, or being forced out of their possessed item for whatever reason. You also see Banette capable of just forcing out a little of their Distortion, creating a new Shuppet that will seek out something to possess. They definitely prefer a physical form to bind themselves too. It makes anchoring themselves in the material world significantly easier.

Rotom are fairly unique in that they're significantly more flexible than most other ghosts. Most ghosts become incredibly attached, tethered, and potentially bound to their item. If that item is somehow destroyed \- very difficult when a ghost is possessing it \- it can seriously damage or even shatter them. Rotom are special in that they can easily flow from one form to the other, never growing too attached.

## **Q.133. On the Rota governing body.**

- ## *Tags: Indigo League, League, Rota*


Yep, it's actual royalty. Most of their laws come from the League, though, so in practice the Queen doesn't have much to do other than take a central part in their culture.

## **Q.134. Besides attempting to enslave Ho-Oh somehow, what did Pokelantis do to deserve its destruction again?**

- ## *Tags: Ho-Oh, Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon, Pokelantis*


Basically, Pokelantis tried to control Ho-Oh for its own ends back in the very, very olden days. It was one of the scant few civilizations that managed to eke out an existence before the Birds were sealed. They pretty much got what I like to call 'the Lawrence III treatment' with their city washed away in a sea of flame.

## **Q.135. Does this mean Sylveon just don’t exist in Kanto?**

- ## *Tags: Fairy type, Pokemon Biology, Sylveon*


Pretty much \- Fairies can't easily sustain themselves outside of those regions. Although there has been a source of Fairy-type energy shown in the last few chapters \[around chapter 52\]. I don't think anyone caught it, though.

## **Q.136. … \[What’s\] the average pay of an Elite 4 or Champion? Is it like a sports person's or like the head of state's pay?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Elite Four, League*


So, Champions have a very nice salary. Figure it ranges roughly from an equivalent of $800,000 to $1,000,000 per year, with Elite Four being maybe 80-90% of that depending on seniority. It's generous compensation, but that being said there are absolutely professional battlers and Contest Champions who probably make a fair bit more. 

Of course, a lot of the allure of being Champion doesn't come from the money. It's nice, and definitely enough to keep you comfortable (especially since the League covers living expenses and offers a generous budget for high-ranking League members) but anyone with the capability of making Champion isn't likely to be as focused on the money. The real benefits are the power and authority that come with it, particularly the resources that being a League member opens up.

## **Q.137. On the Unown’s power.**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Pokemon Biology, Psychic type, Spencer, Unown* 


Another thing to take into account is how many Unown you're dealing with. If it's just a tiny group, it'll barely make you any stronger than an ordinary psychic. A decent collection like what Spencer found puts you at an average-tier Legend, while if you went around the universe collecting Unown you'd be able to crush most normal Legends with ease.

I picture them similar to the Geth from Mass Effect. Essentially exponentially more useful and powerful the more you collect.

## **Q.138. Do you pretty much accept every move listed as something they \[Pokemon\] can learn?**

- ## *Tags: Meta, Pokemon Biology, TM*


Yep, but TM moves tend to be much more difficult to learn there’s a reason they aren’t normally taught.

## **Q.139. Are you going to incorporate the Gen 8 learnsets and new moves?**

- ## *Tags: Meta, Pokemon Biology*


Yes.

## **Q.140. What's your policy on what moves pokemon can learn? Do you go by the books and if they can't learn them in the games they can't learn them in Traveler? We know that's not entirely true given Plume trying to master Aeroblast and whatnot, but would Infernus be able to learn Blast Burn, or Eruption? Would Dazed be able to master Miracle Eye? Would Plume be able to learn Shadow Claw?**

- ## *Tags: Aeroblast, Pokemon Biology, Pokemon Move, Psychic type, TM*


Pokémon can learn any moves they can learn in canon. If they can learn it in any game it can be learned. There is wiggle room \- like Aeroblast \- and with psychics they can theoretically learn any psychic technique, but it goes back to the specialties we talked about a while back. They’d have a much harder time using certain techniques that they aren’t attuned to.

## **Q.141. What's the in-universe explanation as to how well Pokemon understand human language?**

- ## *Tags: Language*


There’s several more complex reasons which the story will delve into eventually, but for now a sufficient explanation is that it’s an extension of a Pokémon’s innate psychic sensitivity that lets them pick up basic information, emotions, etc. from humans and Pokémon they interact with. It’s not quite comprehending language \- that comes with time \- but they’re able to glean basic information and meaning from hatching. Infant Pokémon are better at working with simpler instructions since they don’t understand words as well.

## **Q.142. How come Pokémon understand each other despite the fact that they don’t even say the same thing?**

- ## *Tags: Language, Meta, Pokemon Biology*


Well, in Traveler it’s not like the anime where they say their names. They make general roars, grunts, etc. It’s just like with humans where they can pick up each other’s basic meaning and intentions, but a lot of it is also nonverbal communication like body language. So Pokémon have more sophisticated means of communication, electric signals, pheromones, telepathy, etc.

## **Q.143. Bruno vs Koga hand to hand, who wins?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Bruno, Koga*


Bruno for sure due to Aura. Without Aura, I’d say Koga would have the advantage if he had the element of surprise, but Bruno is just a beast. His bulk and skill would be a major advantage.

## **Q.144. On whether Koga knows about Aura.**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Bruno, Cynthia, Koga*


He probably knows of it due to his long friendship with Bruno, but I don’t think he’d use it. While he loves training, it takes years of additional effort. Like Cynthia said, for most people it’s just not really worth the effort. It’s difficult and a long, long journey for oftentimes little payoff.

## **Q.145. On the risk of a coup happening.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Elite Four, Gym Leader, Gym Trainer, League*


As to answer the coup question...not really. In the past it was slightly more of a concern, but these days the League is incredibly stable. Gym Trainers, even if they managed to beat their Leader, would just be deposed by the League. A Champion could theoretically be ousted by the Elite Four if they went rogue, but in practice there are enough safeguards in place that it wouldn’t be necessary on either side. The League had issues with that on occasion in the early days \- and we’ll learn more about those struggles fairly soon \- but the structure and hierarchy have been set up to preserve the League as a strong, stable institution.

## **Q.146. But in Erika's case \[around chapter 51\], where she's on the thinnest ice that sneasel could produce?**

- ## *Tags: Erika, Gym Leader, Gym Trainer, League*


You still won’t see a coup. It’s the Leagues responsibility to handle these things \- all the Gym Trainers can do is reach out to the League to raise attention to it. It’s a very strict hierarchy and division of powers, although the League is content to give Gym Leaders a lot of autonomy and try not to step in unless necessary.

## **Q.147. On why a lot of the Fossil Pokemon are Rock type.**

- ## *Tags: Aerodactyl, Ditto, Dragon type, Fossil Pokemon, Pokemon Biology, Rock type*


And yeah, that’s a big chunk of it \[redacted\] . I’m sort of going with the route of finding degraded DNA samples. However, since many fossil Pokémon are derived from rock-types they also tend to have fairly protected soft tissue that is shielded from the elements. With how robust Pokémon are, their cells and DNA take a little longer to degrade anyway. It’s heavily degraded and needs some extra ‘kick’ to be properly preserved for so long, but it gives scientists significantly more to work with. In the beginnings of Cinnabar’s research, they patched the DNA with samples from other similar, related species. Dragons featured heavily in Aerodactyl’s reconstruction, for example. It allowed for functional Pokémon to be recreated, but the biggest leap in the technology involved the first appearance of Ditto less than two decades ago, whose cells were naturally adapted to reconstruct and amplify DNA to extents scientists never thought possible.

## **Q.148. Salamence for example? \[see question 147\]**

- ## *Tags: Aerodactyl, Fossil Pokemon, Salamence*


Yep, I imagine Salamence would be drawn on for Aerodactyl.

## **Q.149.TBH seeing how quite a few gyms are hereditary I can see there being a contractual agreement between the gym leader families and the league from the early days that keep alot of incompetent leaders in charge.**

- ## *Tags: Gym Leader, League*


One thing involves in each of those contracts was a competency requirement \- it wasn’t as enforced as frequently in the old days when stability was key (and the League needed those local connections) but nowadays pretty much each Gym Leader from those families is forced to be competent. One benefit of a stabler, modern world.

## **Q.150. What's Alola's relationship with Kanto?**

- ## *Tags: Alola, Kanto, National League, Southern Continent*


Pretty positive. Alola’s another one of the gates to the Southern Continent and the National League has given it a lot of support over the years to help develop it.

## **Q.151. Do you have a ranking for Gary's team's strength, strongest to weakest?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Arcanine, Ash, Blastoise, Gary, Pokemon Battle*


Gary ironically has a more well balanced team than Ash (in that they’re roughly equal in fights). There are some like Blastoise, Alakazam, and Arcanine that are more useful in general, but they’re roughly at the same level of strength. He’s geared them more to cover individual roles.

## **Q.152. Can you comment on his\[Gary’s\] Pidgeot? Is it just getting bad matchups against Plume and stronger than it appears?**

- ## *Tags: Dragon type, Flying type, Gary, Pidgeot, Plume, Pokemon Battle*


Plume is kind of Gary’s Pidgeot’s worst possible matchup. He’s a lightning bruiser \- hits hard, can tank hits few other non-dragon fliers can, and is way faster than most other fliers. Plume is his weak point. She’s faster and more maneuverable, and can hit almost as hard. Gary’s Pidgeot can outmuscle most dragons in the sky, although they have other abilities to draw on that can give them the edge if used correctly.

## **Q.153. Other than the team we saw in the last chapter \[chapter 51\] does he \[Gary\] have any other Pokemon knocking about?**

- ## *Tags: Gary, Golem*


He does, but the full list is in one of my notebooks somewhere haha. I know Golem is on there and roughly five to six more.

## **Q.154. What was the team of Champion Uther and E4 Matthias(the one Agatha dethroned)?**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Champion, Matthias, Master Trainer, Normal type, Pallet Town, Pokemon Starter, Professor Oak, Raticate, Snorlax, Uther*


Admittedly, I haven’t 100% pinned down my timeline for the war to specifics, so this is subject to change. As of this second, Oak challenged them shortly before the war \- it's one of the reasons he was able to secure the funding for Pallet Town. They knew nothing was going to get through him. Of course, that’s another reason he had a few vocal detractors \- he’d proven his strength and was perceived as a coward for being unwilling to use it.

I have the teams for Matthias and Uther somewhere, but I don’t remember them exactly. From what I do remember, Uther was an extremely powerful Normal Master with a Raticate starter and a Snorlax cornerstone.
