## **Q.159. Is Air Lens limited to the Magmar line or can other Fire-types learn it too? And in a hypothetical scenario where Infernus didn't know Air Lens how many of Ash's team would he defeat?**

- ## *Tags: Air Lens, Ash, Fire type, Jolteon, Magcargo, Magmar, Pokemon Battle*


Other fire-types can learn it, but generally only ones like Magmar or Magcargo. It’s significantly easier when you’re already putting out crazy heat. As for that, I think Jolteon would’ve made it through at least 2 of Ash’s team \- Ash would’ve figured out a way to beat it, but it would be costly.

## **Q.162. How are relations between Unova and the rest of the regions? Are they incredibly tense, or has the younger generation basically forgotten about the war?**

- ## *Tags: Alder, Indigo, Last War, League, National League, Kalos, Unova*


Relations between Unova, Kalos, and the Indigo League are pretty warm nowadays. The older generations still hold a bit of a grudge, but it helps that Unova’s fascist government during the  Last War was completely shut down and replaced with a new government. Alder led a coup with his group of idealistic revolutionaries and played an essential part in capturing important Unovan officials as they tried to escape, plus opened up several major gaps in the defenses that allowed the National League to make it a relatively bloodless assault.

Kalos is more complicated, but that’s for another day.

## **Q.165. Were the longer periods of rest cause the fights were that brutal? Or cause of medical reasons like Orre not being fully developed (or this being before they discovered ditto cells)? \[see question 125\]**

- ## *Tags: Ditto, Michael, Orre, Pokemon Biology, Technology*


Both\! The fights were life and death so many more extreme injuries popped up. Orre lacks the same infrastructure, so unless Michael was in a major city medical care was limited to potions and other items. It was also before they discovered Ditto cells as well \- they first appeared a little over 10 years before Traveler began, so it had only just begun to spread to Orre by Michael’s time.

## **Q.174. Have you thought about how Conference brackets are set up?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Conference, Pokemon Trainer*


A bit, although it’s not an area of specialty for me. But yeah, it’s not 100% random. Trainers who got all 8 main badges (and 7, 6, so on) were weighted to face trainers who had a higher percentage of badges gained through facing minor gyms (aka, the trainers who had to go through Preliminary rounds in order to enter). Look at how relatively easy Ash’s early fights were. The trainers he faced were still competent, but it wasn’t until he reached the Top 16 that he faced a real threat.

## **Q.175. On the League scouting trainers.**

- ## *Tags: Gym Leader, League, Metagross, Pokemon Trainer, Pallet Town*


Yeah, and there is a big bureaucracy in the League that handles a lot of the processing...or one Metagross lol. But Gym Leaders definitely highlight trainers with potential. All the Pallet trainers were noted.

## **Q.176. What are time-zone differences like between the regions?**

- ## *Tags: Evolution,  Lightning Bolt, Oz, Pokemon Biology*


Yep, there’s a massive difference. The energy contained in a natural lightning bolt is insane \- Oz can generate pretty powerful blasts, but they’re just pale imitations.

For simplicity’s sake, the Pokémon World has the same length year as our world does.

## **Q.183. On Clair.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Clair, Lance, Master Trainer, Wataru Clan*


Admittedly, one thing to remember is that Clair is being shown from her family who know her too well and that colors their opinion of her as a trainer (particularly Lance, who’s personally disappointed by her stagnation since he wants a good fight). Beating Clair is still an achievement, and that fight would’ve been much, much more difficult without Ash doing his research on her. It’s really at the Master-level of opponents where her flaws are most noticeable.

## **Q.184. How would a total war scenario look like regarding the trainers? Would all of them be conscripted barring powerful ones that could refuse like Oak did?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Last War, League, Ranger, Technology, Wild Pokemon*


There won’t be another war for at least a century (when the people affected by the Last War have passed on and those experiences are lost) due to the ridiculous amounts of devastation left by clashes between civilizations that had advanced in training and technology \- with every trainer capable of carrying a small army, the damage was ridiculous. But, hypothetically, if one did occur then the League would stick with their normal forces (Rangers, ACE, perhaps working with local wild Pokémon). You wouldn’t see conscriptions unless it was an overwhelming force or the region itself was being threatened.

## **Q.185. What's the possible explanation as to how we don't have a bunch of centuries old Rhydon running around?**

- ## *Tags: Indigo, Mamoru, Rhydon*


There are 10-15 Rhydon in Indigo that have lived for centuries, but they frequently get into fights and kill each other. Mamoru also has a habit of culling them every few centuries when a few will band together and try to kill him.

## **Q.186. Where are Mount Gold/Silver compared to each other roughly?**

If I remember my plans correctly, Mt. Gold is roughly halfway between Blackthorn and Mt. Silver. It’s tucked away between larger mountains and difficult to pick out details from the air.

## **Q.187. I know that Mt. Coronet is considered the tallest mountain range in the pokemon world and is pretty perilous, but would Mount Silver be considered the more dangerous of the two mountains?**

- ## *Tags: Mt. Coronet, Mt. Silver*


I’d say it’s a pick your poison scenario. Mt. Silver is a very blunt kind of danger with harsh weather and strong Pokémon. Mt. Coronet is the danger of the unknown when you stray from the path.

## **Q.188. Weren't there horrifically powerful ghosts in Mt Coronet?**

## **Q.190. Are Dusknoir hostile to those who walk into their crypts automatically?**

- ## *Tags: Dusknoir, Ghost type, Pokemon Behaviour*


They will usually manifest ahead of you and warn you off. If you try to advance, they attack ruthlessly. They won’t draw it out or torture you, but you will die.

## **Q.191. What ghost types would draw your death out?**

- ## *Tags: Dusknoir, Ghost type, Pokemon Behaviour*


Chandelure.

## **Q.192. On the League’s judicial branch.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, League, Psychic type*


Basically there’s a vast court system outside of the League’s command structure. It’s created and supported by the League, but the Champion tends to not have direct control of it. Additionally, psychics are heavily involved to determine guilt. There’s less of a legal process (though it is present) for serious and violent crimes and more about a dozen psychics digging through your head to confirm guilt, then those psychics are cross referenced by other psychics. It’s a little nightmarish for our world and would never happen. But in a world where psychics are common, defenses against them are essentially nonexistent, and the foundations of the justice system are built upon psychics existing...

## **Q.193. What is the procedure to get a permission for restricted Pokemon? Do you have to notify the League, and can you even use it in regulated battles before?**

Yeah, you have to reach out to the League. Usually a Gym Leader, and they’ll assess you. Sometimes you have to have certain certifications or pass tests

Champions have the authority to do whatever they want when it comes to training, basically.

## **Q.200. What's the population of the Traveler-verse? By League if possible.**

- ## *Tags: Frontier Regions, Hoenn, Kanto, Orre, Population, Unova* 


Hard to pin down exact numbers. I’d say the main regions tend to hold 50-100 million. Somewhere like Hoenn is on the lower end of that while Kanto and Unova are on the higher end. Frontier regions have maybe 1-2 million. Orre has something like 10 million. All in all, I’d say there’s only around a billion humans worldwide.

This is a little embarrassing but I just checked my notes and my number was a little off. That \~1 billion number was from a while back. Basically the population is a little under 2/3 of the numbers I gave above.

## **Q.201. How serious is power creep? Like, obviously there were big jumps with TMs and Pokeballs. But other than that, what's it like?**

- ## *Tags: Technology, TM*


Major power creep over the last centuries due to more peace and time to train and progression in science, but the biggest appeared with TMs and Pokeballs (pokeballs being the largest due to eliminating many of the logistical problems associated with raising multiple Pokémon). TMs appeared less than twenty years ago and instantly changed the battle circuit. Power creep is pretty much stagnant at this point, with only innovations like multiple use TMs becoming more accessible. It’s mostly leveled off at this point.

## **Q.202. On Super Speed’s origins.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Lance, Super Speed*


If I remember right, Super Speed is Ash’s design. Inspired by Lance’s emphasis on speed and maneuverability, but not created by Lance.

## **Q.203. Other people have probably made similar things, correct?**

- ## *Tags: Agility, Pidgeot*


Yes, there are plenty of speed boosting techniques, just not in that same regard. It’s not terribly practical for things other than Pidgeot of\[or\] other incredibly fast fliers \- otherwise it’s usually best to enhance other aspects. Agility does the job perfectly well most of the time.

## **Q.208. How has Orre's ecosystem recovered after the events of xd?**

- ## *Tags: Orre*


Orre’s still a blasted wasteland, but the oases have continued to expand. The main reason pokemon have fled the region in the past is due to hostile human presence, particularly those that would capture and exploit them for gang wars and the like. Some oases have been redevastated as Orre descends more and more into anarchy, but Duking has been able to protect several as well and those have thrived. It’s done a lot in terms of restoring the human/Pokémon relationship in the region.

## **Q.212. Do gym leaders have to specialize in one pokemon type? If they do, can they change the gym type if they become a leader?**

- ## *Tags: Gym, Gym Leader*


Gyms tend to have a historical basis for a certain type specialty, but there isn’t a required type. Most trainers on that level tend to be specialists, however. ## **Q.213. Do you have a preferred last name for Agatha?**

## **Q.214. What is Kanto's Square Footage?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Dark World, Kanto, Location, Plume, Region, Sinnoh*


Most regions are the size of an average sized US western state \- I don’t give exact numbers, but 50-70000 square miles. That tends to be several hundred miles across and up and down, which Plume can very, very easily cover in a day even at a reduced speed that Ash can take. On long trips without much need for maneuvering she can fly faster as well.

Flying to Sinnoh isn’t a super casual trip \- mostly due to having to fly around the Dark World \- but with Plume flying quickly she can easily make it with Ash in about two days. It would be faster to make teleportation jumps with a ferry service, but plenty of trainers choose to fly.

## **Q.215. What concept could Genesect represent?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Genesect, Giovanni, Legendary Pokemon, Metagross, Mewtwo, Steven*


Unova is fun. For Genesect, each will basically be on the level of Steven’s Metagross minus psychic abilities. They’re essential what Giovanni should have done: powerful, reliably produced, controllable super soldiers. Not Legends, but their modifications make them extremely formidable. They’re force multipliers rather than nukes such as Mewtwo. They’re reliable.

## **Q.216. You said Genesect were reliably made but how reliably were they made?**

- ## *Tags: Genesect*


They’re extremely limited in number due to limitations on the number of specimens they can get to perform the process on, the process of augmenting Genesect killing nearly 3/4 of the attempts until it was more fine tuned, and the biggest factor comes down to cost. It’s ridiculously expensive to clone, it’s ridiculously expensive to augment them, and it’s ridiculously expensive to maintain and keep Genesect alive and healthy. They’re extremely resource intensive.

## **Q.217. Back with Mewtwo, it was mentioned that he had some trouble grasping dark types were harder to grasp at with his powers. - ## *Tags: Absol, Alakazam, Darkrai, Karen, Legendary Pokemon, Mega Evolution, Mewtwo, Suicune, Psychic type*

In practice it’s like a massive psychic awareness, but it’s different in that it’s innately tied to the universe. Psychic abilities stand out as flashes, so it was able to sense Alakazam’s intentions and attempt.

Yeah, Lance has an edge over Cynthia but they’re basically even. ## **Q.222. What's the differences between the various poisons used by pokemon? Like is Nidoking's venom different from a Seviper or Tentacruel and is Seviper and Arbok venom the same or Garbador and Muk sludge etc.? Can Weezing produce different types of poison gas?**

## **Q.223. What did Michael do differently from Wes? Does Micheal keep his full team on him at all times or in orre does he fight fully lethal "go for the trainers"?**

- ## *Tags: Ardos, Citadark Isle, Eldes, Greevil, Michael, Rui, Wes*

Michael left them to die in Citadark. Eldes, when Ardos and Greevil we’re preparing to go back to their old ways, killed them.

## **Q.224. Do gym leaders use their true teams on challengers when they are no longer rookies or have participated in a League Conference? Or both? And speaking of the Conference there were mentions of repeat competitors. So are Badges earned in one season valid for only tha Conference of the same year or is it earned once,lifetime qualifications situation?**

- ## *Tags: Blaine, Conference, Giovanni, Gym Badges, Gym Leader, Sabrina*


It’s essentially up to the Gym Leader’s discretion. In general they match their teams to their opponent. You’ll have a few \- such as Sabrina, Blaine, and Giovanni \- who always fight at a higher level. They’re the gatekeepers to the Conference. But Gym Leaders ten\[d\]s to fight around their opponents level \- people with no badges get newer or inexperienced opponents, while they gradually scale up. 

Against someone who’s competed in a Conference, they’ll generally fight higher. They get access to an opponent’s records when they sign into the Gym and can tailor their approach. 

Badges only apply per season.

## **Q.225. On the Indigo Conference’s bracket.**

- ## *Tags: Conference, Indigo Conference, Gym Badges, Pokemon Trainer*


Yep, for trainers that didn’t get all 8 main badges they had to go through admission rounds to whittle the numbers down for the actual Conference.

## **Q.226. When do the admission rounds happen? \[see question 225\]**

- ## *Tags: Conference, Indigo*


The weeks before.

## **Q.227. What's the information regarding pseudo-legendaries and how "special" they are compared to normal Pokemon?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Dragonite, Master Trainer, Metagross, Michael, Pierce, Pokemon Battle, Princess, Pseudo Legendary, Salamence*


Pseudo-legendaries are naturally powerful Pokémon. As wild Pokémon they’ll tend to be unmatched and claim a status as apex predators. At the lower and middle tiers of battle they’re pretty much unstoppable due to their natural advantages. Just look at Pierce’s Metagross. 

It’s at the higher tiers where things get more difficult. As Pokémon start reaching their true potential and pack an arsenal of techniques and a much higher level of skill and technique, a pseudo-legendary starts to find competition (which can be difficult for them since they’ve overwhelmed everything at early levels). I think pseudo-legendaries will be dangerous opponents at any level, but other Pokémon are more than capable of surpassing them at higher levels. It’s only a handful of even pseudo-legendaries that could even hope to challenge a team on Ash’s or Michael’s level. Other than true Masters, Ash’s main team members would absolutely obliterate almost any pseudo-Legendary he came across. Plus look at his battle with Michael \- he managed to take down Dragonite and Salamence on equal footing. Are they strong? Definitely. They have natural advantages, but it doesn’t stop normal Pokémon from reaching that level. The absolutely insane examples of the Dragonite Trio, Metagross, and Princess are stellar examples of their species, brought to that level by their trainers.

## **Q.228. On whether Michael fought Mewtwo.**

- ## *Tags: Giovanni, Mewtwo, Michael, Pokemon Trainer*


Michael fought Giovanni before Mewtwo was brought in. It took a while before Mewtwo could regulate his power enough to ‘safely’ fight normal trainers.

## **Q.229. Aside from Lucario/Riolu other Pokemon can learn Aura Sphere. Is the reason the same as Lucario, that they have an innate ability to control aura as well?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Aura Sphere, Lucario, Riolu*


In Traveler, Aura Sphere is more a raw expression of Aura. It’s a commonality to many Pokémon and humans who know of Aura \- either through extensive self-reflection or because their species have communities that pass down knowledge of Aura \- because it’s simple yet effective. It’s a physical manifestation of a desire or need to attack.

## **Q.232. On Aura.**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Bruno, Cynthia*


In Traveler, Aura is essentially self expression. It’s using a part of yourself and expressing it physically into the world. Bruno has dedicated his life to training and combat, and as a result he can fortify his body to superhuman levels. Cynthia seeks knowledge and spent her life working with her team, so she has Aura abilities enhancing those aspects of her character. 

But everyone has aspects intrinsic to humanity: Fear, Love, Anger, etc. as a result, there tends to be a core set of common abilities that almost anyone can use.

## **Q.239. So this just popped into my head. Can a Jigglypuff or etc's Sing be controlled enough to selectively put to sleep opponents without affecting others in hearing range? And can it be recorded to put others to sleep?**

- ## *Tags: Jigglypuff, Sing*


Good question\! That definitely depends. I see Sing as having a psychic component that makes it more effective, which can be controlled by a skilled Jigglypuff. It’s fairly difficult, however, and requires a lot of focus to not just ‘broadcast’.

And I think Sing without the psychic influence is just a very soothing sound. It’s probably relaxing and could put you to sleep if you were already relaxed, but it wouldn’t be able to calm down a Pokémon pumped up with adrenaline.

## **Q.240. What's the difference between mental arts and physical manipulation?**

- ## *Tags: Psychic type*


Mental arts involve manipulation of emotions, thoughts, and perceptions via psychic influence. Physical manipulation is the projection and creation of force, barriers, and finer methods of manipulating matter, energy, and force.

## **Q.241. Can psychic pokemon be good at both mental art and physical manipulation?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Dazed, Espeon, Gardevoir, Psychic type*


Yep. Just look at Dazed, whose species specializes in mental arts yet she’s incredibly powerful with physical manipulation through extensive training. Alakazam and several other species (Espeon and Gardevoir for example) are also good at both.

## **Q.242. Why do we need Bob to teleport Ash, when he can take help from Dazed?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Ash, Bob, Dazed, Mewtwo, Psychic type, Teleport*


Dazed isn’t really capable of long range teleportation. She could do a few miles at best (without being juiced up on Mewtwo’s power, which she wants to avoid for obvious reasons haha). Even most Alakazam have to do jumps for cross-region travel. Members of the Teleportation Squad are incredibly specialized in teleporting and are capable of jumping across entire regions by themselves in a single teleport.

## **Q.243. Can it\[Sabrina’s Alakazam\] teleport long range?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Metagross, Psychic type, Sabrina, Steven*


Yep. Sabrina’s Alakazam is basically a Master of All when it comes to psychic abilities. It’s got similar physical abilities to a powerful Metagross (not Steven’s, of course), excellent mental abilities, and great space-time manipulation.

## **Q.244. Has anyone ever tried to build a mecha for a Rotom to possess? Is that legal for a regulated match? In fact, can Rotom possessed appliances be stored in pokeballs and used for matches?**

- ## *Tags: Cynthia, Ghost type, League, National League, Rotom, Spiritomb*

There hasn’t been a ton of research into them, although I can definitely see powerful bodies being built for them by the League once they reach that point. Rotom in appliances can be used for matches \- I figure if something as awful as Cynthia’s Spiritomb can be used a Rotom can be as well haha.

## **Q.247. On the Dark World’s inaccessibility.**

## **Q.249. Can Humans travel to outer space?**

- ## *Tags: Technology*


Humans can go to outer space and have sent satellites up, but they have a fairly low success rate \- quite a few tend to be mysteriously destroyed.

## **Q.250. What happens to the feather when the bearer dies?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Feather, Haukea, Lance, Legendary Birds, Moltres*


In general, the Feather will dissipate unless the Bird desires it to be passed on to a new bearer. Tani’s Feather faded away when she died, Lance’s would most likely do the same (unless he died as Champion, in which case Moltres would likely desire for the Feather to be picked up by someone new and the covenant renewed). Haukea’s would remain in the world, but anyone who picked it up would regret it.

## **Q.251. On why Blast Burn is frequently taught using a TM.**

- ## *Tags: Blast Burn, Fire type, Master Trainer, Technology, TM*


I will say that a proper Blast Burn has an element of technique and control to it that is VERY difficult for a fire-type to discover and master on their own. There are several ‘forms’ of Blast Burn, each acting as a stage that preps the fire-type for the next until eventually you arrive at the final product. There’s a reason it’s a Master-level technique.

## **Q.252. Presumably Jonathan was at the very first stage, then? \[see question 251\]**

- ## *Tags: Blast Burn, Fire type, Jonathan*


Yep. Jonathan walked away with a very powerful technique, but he doesn’t have the full product yet.

## **Q.253. So could a Torkoal learn Blast Burn?**

- ## *Tags: Blast Burn, Fire type*


In Traveler, pretty much any fire-type can learn Blast Burn. Raw power helps, but it’s only one piece of the puzzle. I see it being restricted to starters as purely a game mechanic.

## **Q.254. Can any nota\[b\]le non fire types learn it\[Blast Burn\]? Does groudon have access to bb\[Blast Burn\] potentially?**

- ## *Tags: Blast Burn, Fire type, Groudon, Legendary Pokemon, Weather Trio*


Technically a non fire-type could learn it, but it would be extraordinarily difficult. They also lack the innate resistance to heat and flame that a fire-type does, so it would be damaging to them in most cases. As for Groudon, it and the rest of the Weather Trio are in the boat where they don’t need techniques.

## **Q.255. Would any fire types be able to use Blast Burn naturally?**

- ## *Tags: Blast Burn, Fire type*


Nah, Blast Burn absolutely requires a great deal of experience and skill to wield, although some Pokémon might have an easier time learning it. 

## **Q.256. If Magnus doesn't know how to do it \[Blast Burn\], I'll eat Ash's hat.**

- ## *Tags: Blast Burn, Fire type, Magnus*


Magnus does know it\!

## **Q.257. How prevalent is cannibalism in the pokemon world? Do mothers eat there eggs in desperate times? Do ariados females eat their mates?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology*


It happens, but generally only out of necessity unless a Pokémon is very, very disturbed...at which point other wild Pokémon will probably gang up to kill it anyways.

## **Q.258. So Pierce’s Umbreon, did it eat other Umbreons? Is it that disturbed?**

- ## *Tags: Pierce, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology, Umbreon*


It probably would if it needed to in order to survive, but in general it preferred killing to those acts.

## **Q.259. What about Precipice Blades or Origin Pulse or Dragon Ascent? Are those exceptions? \[see question 254\]**

- ## *Tags: Dragon Ascent, Legendary Pokemon, Origin Pulse, Precipice Blades, Weather Trio*


Sort of. In Traveler, their\[Weather Trio’s\] techniques are more along the lines of them just focusing their attention for a moment rather than just letting their power emanate out.

## **Q.260. How would you describe rare candies in Traveler verse? I know Gary made a joke about Ash's team being injected with them so are they like steroids?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Gary, Last War, Pokemon Biology, Rare Candy*


Pretty much. I imagine them being used for physical enhancement, although best used in small doses to prevent physiological dependencies and complications. Additionally, using them can lead to a Pokémon losing coordination due to rapid growth of muscle (and sometimes size in general). Few high tier trainers use it for these reasons, as well as it being very much a crutch. Without natural growth, the Pokémon possess less skill and tend to have weaker abilities. 

They’re basically nonexistent in the modern day outside of medical purposes. Rare candies originated in the years prior to the Last War, and were heavily abused by governments during the war in order to maintain any edge they could.

## **Q.261. So they're \[Rare Candies are\] essentially steroids? \[see question 260\]**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Biology, Rare Candy*


Basically lol...but with super Pokémon science\! 

## **Q.262. Does Bruiser have a belt around his waist and how is the belt around his neck tied, like the knot behind is back or do they hang down on his front?**

- ## *Tags: Bruiser, Machoke*


So Bruiser wears the standard Machoke power save belt around his waist. The black belt is tied around his neck loosely with the knot in front.

## **Q.263. Are there any limitations to the move Mimic? Will a Mightyena exhaust itself when copying a Draco Meteor or something?**

- ## *Tags: Draco Meteor, Mightyena, Mimic, Pokemon Biology* 


Oh yeah. Mimic can be useful but is seriously limited, especially with more powerful Pokémon. High level techniques will lack a lot of the power if used by a Pokémon of a different type who hasn’t trained in those sorts of technique, for example. Or if they are able to ‘brute force’ it to keep the same power as the original technique, it’ll be extremely inefficient.

## **Q.264. On what Mew’s role as the “Guardian of Life” means.**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Legendary Pokemon, Mew*


You’re pretty much correct. Basically the ‘Guardian of Life’ is looking at all life rather than individual organisms or species. Mew ensures life as a whole continues, although it’s also essentially had to reboot organic life several times due to Legendary conflicts.

## **Q.265. Any thoughts on mining in Traveler-verse?**

- ## *Tags: Technology*


I can’t answer everything right now but I’ll address a few of the recent questions. Mining exists, and is usually reliant with negotiations made by the League with wild Pokémon. In the past it was more aggressive, but that was a disaster for all involved. Fossil fuels have been heavily used in the past, particularly at the advent of the industrial era, but led to serious issues with wild Pokémon. Pollution heavily irritates local populations, and they’re more than happy to take a detour to sabotage whatever strange technology the humans are using.

Coal and other fossil fuels are still used in some capacity, but with other, less disruptive forms taking priority.

## **Q.266. I'd imagine steel use would have to be much lower, right? \[see question 265\]**

- ## *Tags: Beldum, Rustboro City, Stone Family, Technology*


Yep. Mining has been an essential part of civilization since the beginning, even with the presence of Pokémon providing many, many other advantages that let them work around common challenges early civilizations faced in our world. The Stone family, for example, carved out its current high place in Rustboro by using their Beldum colony to safely mine areas. They essentially held a monopoly on it for many years. 

I’d say in urban environments steel use would still be very common, and it’s a useful material in many other ways as well. But yeah, in general I imagine the Pokémon World favors wood more, especially in rural areas.

## **Q.267. On Traveler verse’s tree biology.**

- ## *Tags: Technology*


Trees and plants tend to grow slightly faster in Traveler’s world as well. Just an adaptation for living in a world with superpowered monsters haha. But yeah, tree farms \[see question 266\] are mostly how it’s done. Actual logging and deforestation is a nightmare to deal with \- taking territory from wild Pokémon without regard just sows the seed for conflict.

## **Q.268. Do berries grow really quickly? \[see question 267\]**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Wild Pokemon*


Yep. It’s not like they’ll grow overnight, but they have evolved to grow rapidly in order to spread as widely as possible \- which is definitely helped by the huge nutritional requirements of most pokemon. 

Of course, that’s also been slightly helped along in some areas. Humans aren’t the first organisms to practice agriculture, although they have taken it the farthest. There are plenty of sedentary wild Pokémon populations that deliberately replant seeds and ensure wild berry and food growth. Alakazam are a good example \- their communes have resulted in many strains of larger, more nutritious berries that then spread and outcompete wild berries.

## **Q.269. How does a Shedinja's Wonder Guard work in Traveler? Does it just have a force field around it?**

- ## *Tags: Dark type, Distortion, Ghost type, Nincada, Pokemon Biology, Pokemon Behaviour, Shedinja, Wonder Guard*


So, essentially Shedinja is the discarded carapace of Nincada that is possessed by a Distortional entity. The carapace is extremely fragile, and as a result a massive amount of the Shedinja’s power is devoted solely to defense, essentially a shroud that nullifies almost any attack. It also invests a large portion of its energy into fortifying its shell. There are only a handful of weaknesses:

1\. Distortional energy as found in dark and ghost type attacks and abilities. It has the ability to disrupt the Wonder Guard and directly deal damage. 

2\. The other weaknesses are those intrinsic to the exoskeleton. While not sentient, the exoskeleton retains some semblance of what it once was and imparts that into the ghost. That instinctual fear of things like fire, winged predators, and rock can disrupt Shedinja’s focus and make it vulnerable.

## **Q.270. Does a well-trained one\[Shedinja\] focus on minimizing the moments of vulnerability? \[see question 269\]**

- ## *Tags: Dark type, Distortion, Ghost type, Nincada, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology, Shedinja, Wonder Guard*


Yep. Strength in Shedinja honestly comes down mostly to mastering themselves and reducing the chinks in their armor.

## **Q.271. Is Mewtwo hiding at Mt. Quena again as per canon?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Mt. Quena, New Island*


Nope, he has no need since he’s remained at New Island.

If we’d seen a heavier redemption \- something more akin to the anime \- I think Mewtwo would want to leave New Island behind and find a new beginning in a place like Mt. Quena. But since he’s basically the same as when he wanted to conquer everything (maybe a little softer around the edges) he’s more content to remain in New Island.

## **Q.272. There was no elite with Metagross \[during the Last War\]? And how rare are Metagross actually? Is Stone colony only one?**

- ## *Tags: Beldum, Distortion, Hoenn, Last War, Metagross, Metang, Steven, Stone Family*


Well, Steven’s Metagross to be specific. There were probably decent numbers of Metagross deployed by Hoenn. They’re very valuable in that situation due to their innate durability and psychic prowess. 

They’re a species that has been very successful worldwide, but tend to have small populations and vast territories. Due to their effectiveness, many Pokémon are very, very aggressive in banding together and thwarting attempts of Metagross to create new colonies. 

It’s pretty difficult to acquire them. There are limited amounts of Beldum traded out by Metagross colonies to certain humans and the League if they can offer something valuable in turn. 

Isolated, individual Metagross do exist but they tend to be mad and extremely dangerous...not very useful in a fight. Occasionally you can find drifting Beldum that have been separated from their colony, usually laborers whose Metang overseer was struck with a Distortion-based attack and lost control.

## **Q.273. How thorough is \[Steven’s\] Metagross's physics knowledge?**

- ## *Tags: Metagross, Porygon, Psychic type, Steven*


Metagross have very good physics knowledge. They see much more through their psychic awareness than their eyes, which gives a massive rush of data/information from the environment (which is also how Steven’s can snipe fliers so well). With their brains, they can interpret that data very effectively  and it leads to an intuitive comprehension of physics. 

Steven does ensure his Metagross is exposed to more sources of information than most, and his Metagross has grown skilled in uncommon areas such as thermal manipulation that allow it to affect the world on a finer scale than most psychics. But most wild and trained Metagross are exposed to the same sorts of data \- trained ones are just given better resources and guidance to take advantage of it. 

Metagross have similar nerve pulses to other beings, as compared to artificial Pokémon like Porygon. Their brains are excellent at computation and gifted with great intelligence, but they’re still living things.

## **Q.274. Are they\[Porygon\] used in battle?**

- ## *Tags: Normal type, Pokemon Battle, Porygon*


Yep, although they’re uncommon. Honestly, using them in battle is probably the least effective way to utilize them.

 Pretty much everything. Different Porygon are trained in different ways but they’re very flexible.

- ## *Tags: Normal type, Porygon, Technology*


They are used by the League.

## **Q.277. When an Exeggutor dies naturally, what happens to its eggs?**

- ## *Tags: Exeggutor, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology*


They’re powerful enough that weaker predators would ignore them out of fear, but plenty of Pokémon would like to snatch up a dropped head. 

## **Q.278. Do you think that ditto cells within Traveler will lead towards age, non-lethal injury and ailment immortality?**

- ## *Tags: Age, League, Technology, Wild Pokemon*


Yep. Ages will definitely vastly increase. It’ll be something that contributes to serious overpopulation in the future, pushes for expansion, and inevitable conflict with wild Pokémon unless the League regulates it.

## **Q.279. Does Mewtwo even require sleep?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology, Psychic type*


If you took away his vast psychic abilities, he would need only minimal sleep due to the genetic engineering. But with psychic powers he doesn’t need it \- he’s basically capable of passively ‘refreshing’ his brain to keep him well-rested. He’s escaped most biological needs.

## **Q.280. How skilled a psychic is Mewtwo honestly?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Pokemon Behaviour, Psychic type*


Basically Mewtwo is about as skilled as he needs to be. With the ridiculous level of psychic power, he’s capable of manipulating the world on micro and macro scales. But in a fight he’s going to default to simple blasts, beams, and grips for the most part. Time is a valuable resource, and even a tiny delay in creating a more complex effect might not be worth it. Not against something as powerful as a Legend anyway.

Mewtwo’s done some crazy stuff. He can work on a fine enough level to manipulate genetics. He experiments quite a bit, but just doesn’t often need to do much with the knowledge outside of alleviating boredom.

## **Q.281. Given what we know of pseudo-legendaries and how powerful they are, what is a Slaking like in Traveler given it's versatile moveset, insane bulk attack, good defense and speed and special attack and how does Truant measure up in Traveler? Are they just lazy super weapons? And has there been a normal master or champion with a Slaking cornerstone?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Hoenn, Slaking*


Slaking are known as absolute beasts. Very difficult to train since they tend to be fairly unmotivated, but their natural power makes them forces to be reckoned with. Their biggest issue is stamina. They overheat easily, and are best used for explosive bursts. They tend to focus on elemental attacks for longer battles. There have definitely been powerful leaders in Hoenn with Slaking, but the League is too recent to have had Champions with it.

## **Q.282. Is the duel not accepted if one of the trainers doesn't have the money to pay it off then?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Trainer*


If a trainer tries to battle without having above the minimum balance, it’ll either be a battle just for fun or be declined.

## **Q.299. When it comes to a missing limb (say Ash lost his left arm), do they replace the limb with a biological prosthetic grown via ditto cells? Or do they use ditto cells to somehow grow a new arm in its place?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Ditto, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology, Rhyhorn*


I just skimmed the rest of the discussion and I’ll try to answer the main questions\! Let me know if I miss anything. 

So, basically Ditto are capable of completely regenerating limbs. It takes time, however, and is generally done through growing the limbs separately instead of just slapping Ditto cells on the severed area. It can then be pretty easily attached \- of course, the optimal solution is to preserve the original limb and use Ditto cells to reattach it. They’re able to adapt and restore it until it’s essentially completely back to normal. 

Ditto are sentient. Pretty much all Pokémon are, although there are definitely differences in intelligence. Just look at Rhyhorn, which tend to not be the brightest.

## **Q.300. On Ditto.**

- ## *Tags: Ditto, Legendary Pokemon, Mew, Pokemon Biology*


Let’s just say Ditto has some help in the whole ‘DNA amplification and arrangement’ by virtue of being a failed clone of Mew. It kept some semblance of the instincts. Skilled Ditto are able to mold their form without DNA samples to resemble inanimate objects, but it is very, very difficult to hold it for long and is mostly used as a disguise.

## **Q.301. If Dittos can transform their body structures completely, wouldn't that imply that if such a change was forced on Ditto cells by outside stimuli, like using Ditto cells to regrow an arm in a lab for example, that the change would either be resisted or temporary?**

- ## *Tags: Ditto, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology*


Essentially, Ditto cells separated from the main intelligence simply act as pluripotent stem cells that adapt to whatever they are in contact with. Honestly, one way I’m using to avoid the whole ‘blatantly breaking conservation of mass’ and change it into ‘slightly breaking conservation of mass’ is to have Ditto much, much heavier than in canon. They’ll weigh several hundred pounds, which is enough to properly copy and adapt to most pokemon. They’ll have serious issues with larger Pokémon. I’m passing on the question about being able to breed with humans, but they can transform into them. It’s very uncomfortable and not good for their mental state, however. It’s against their nature and they don’t hold it for more than a few seconds in most cases.

## **Q.302. What does ash wear? How does it look? Simple t-shirt and pants?**

Yep. He wears shorts pretty often in Hoenn (unless he’s going through rough territory) and normally just a plain shirt. And the hat of course.

## **Q.308. Are there any Victory Roads in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: League*

## **Q.309. How potent are techniques like Attract in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Attract, Pokemon Battle, Torrent*


So basically Attract varies a lot from Pokémon to Pokémon. It’s most effective on Pokémon of similar biology and egg groups, although most organic Pokémon can use it to some effect against other organic Pokémon. Certain Pokémon can outright shrug it off. What does help is that there’s a powerful psychic component to it in addition to the mass release of pheromones, which offers a lot more flexibility to the technique.

Honestly, Torrent would’ve struggled if Attract had been used from the outset. He hasn’t had any training to resist it, even though his willpower helps him out in that regard.

## **Q.310. Who would do a better job of using Attract, providing there aren't any other independent variables? A Psychic type who's reliant on the mental proportions of the move, or a Fighting or Grass type primarily utilising the pheromone aspect?**

- ## *Tags: Attract, Dark type, Fighting type, Grass type, Psychic type*


I’d say it does depend on the Pokémon. The psychic is probably going to be able to cast the widest net and ensnare many different Pokémon, including nonorganic if it’s able to manipulate their minds properly. I think Pokémon primarily using the pheromone aspect would have it be more powerful on specific Pokémon (particularly dark-types). 

A skilled enough psychic could technically instigate hormone production, but at that point it’s basically taking a longer route to the same objective. It’s easier to just implant the thoughts and let the Pokémon’s physiology do the rest.

## **Q.311. So psychic has versatility (minus Dark) and natural producers have efficiency it looks like. \[see question 310\]**

- ## *Tags: Dark type, Psychic type*


Yep, good way to look at it. And there are particularly potent psychics who have developed incredible skill with mental techniques like that and can match natural producers \- with psychic powers it really ends up being a matter of specialization.

## **Q.312. Given that ghosts with more formless or incorporeal proportions carry psychic abilities (Gengar, Mismagius) is there an argument for why they can't use Attract?**

- ## *Tags: Attract, Distortion, Gengar, Ghost type, Mismagius, Psychic type*


Sort of \- certain ghosts in Traveler can absolutely mimic Attract’s effects. Quite a few have very potent abilities to influence minds. In Traveler, they’re incapable of using actual psychic abilities but are able to use Distortion-based power for similar effects.

## **Q.313. Instead of a control-and-order based system psychics use, ghosts might be using a persuasion basis?**

- ## *Tags: Distortion, Ghost type, Psychic type*


That’s a very interesting, well thought out perspective\! I’d love to see that implemented in a fic\! I haven’t seen  anyone introduce rules like that before. Traveler’s rules are a bit different when it comes to ghosts \- basically, ghosts are able to manipulate Distortional energy in the same way that psychics can manipulate psychic energy. Distortional energy can be precisely manipulated to achieve effects similar to psychic energy, but it has the nasty side-effect of breaking down whatever it’s in contact with. 

I have dark-types as resistant to ghost’s Distortion-based abilities essentially because they have the same sort of energy running through their body and have a physiology able to protect them from its negative effects. Hope that makes sense, and if you have any further questions I’m happy to answer them\!

## **Q.314. How are we defining Mythical at this point? There’s really not many similarities between most of the species. Like, there’s a ton of Shaymin. What makes them special compared to, like, Chikorita?**

- ## *Tags: Chikorita, Hoopa, Legendary Pokemon, Mythical Pokemon*


Yeah, a lot of the recent Mythical Pokémon are more ‘rare, powerful Pokémon’ than Legends in my eyes, and that’s going to color how they are adapted to Traveler. There are exceptions of course\!

I will say that Hoopa is a proper Legend in Traveler\!

## **Q.315. Are there any actual cults in the pokemon world? Any major religions?**

- ## *Tags: Chinatsu, Clefable, Ecruteak City, Hoenn, Johto, Legendary Pokemon, Mt. Moon, Sinnoh*


So, there isn’t really a large spanning religion in the Pokémon World. It highly depends on the region and tends to be localized, based upon the Legendaries they were exposed to (although pseudo-Legends such as Mamoru, the Mt. Moon Clefable, or Chinatsu might also be worshipped as local gods). 

As the Legends faded away for their long rest, most of their cults faded away as well. You still see a common respect for Legends, but most people don’t actually worship them anymore. 

You see exceptions in highly traditional areas such as Ecruteak (and much of Johto), the archipelago in Hoenn, and especially Sinnoh. In Sinnoh nearly every mountain village has a tale about a patron Legend that they hold dear

## **Q.316. Can we get spoilers on how Dazed is going to be developing power-wise cuz I did not appreciate her getting trucked by Pryce's Mamoswine?**

## **Q.317. What’s the approximate worth of the currency within Traveler compared to a currency we have? Additionally, do you price match the game for pokeballs?**

- ## *Tags: Technology*

## **Q.318. Hey Elf, what are your thoughts on subspecies? Like, would a Nidoran native to the Safari Zone be any different than one native to Mount Moon in any way?**

- ## *Tags: Mt. Moon, Nidoran, Pokemon Biology, Safari Zone*


Hmm. I mostly consider subspecies that would develop in isolated areas. It takes a lot of time, and I feel like most of the subspecies would just end up being regional variants in Traveler. There might be subtle differences worth noting, but nothing too dramatic.

## **Q.319. On trade routes.**

- ## *Tags: Technology, Teleport*


Really like that write up\! One thing to note is that traditional trade routes and physical travel are essentially dead at this point due to common teleportation and extremely convenient matter-energy conversion in the form of pokeball technology, which allows mass transport of goods for almost no cost. Most travel between cities is done by teleportation for safety and convenience. Planes and ferries and such do exist for inter regional travel, although there are some ‘taxi’ services affiliated with the League that maintain jump stations across the oceans.

## **Q.320. Did Mewtwo’s power cause extra interference in travel for Psychic types?**

- ## *Tags: Bob, Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Psychic type*


Mewtwo’s power is potent enough to seriously disturb teleportation if you aren’t a skilled psychic. Even skilled psychic’s essentially get drunk off it if they aren’t accustomed to it, such as Bob. By a day or two later it still permeates the world in that area enough to be easily accessible to normal psychics to draw on.

But yeah, in general most Legendaries seriously disrupt fine-tuned psychic abilities. 

That’s the thing \- he isn’t transporting a shipping container of food, but tons of food stored in significantly smaller, less massive storage compartments in an energy/data form.

## **Q.321. On the consequences of a broken transportation infrastructure.**

- ## *Tags: Technology*


Honestly, I think that’s where Pokémon come in. Even with infrastructure heavily damaged, I can imagine specialized rock and ground-types able to construct rudimentary shelters and infrastructure. Nothing fancy or particularly long-lasting, but enough to get by until construction crews are able to offer a more permanent solution.

## **Q.322. On how the reappearance of Team Rocket affected public safety.**

- ## *Tags: League, Ranger, Team Rocket, Wild Pokemon*


It's definitely a complicated system \- most of the time the world is reasonably safe even for young trainers due to League efforts to keep close contact with wild Pokémon, psychics and Ranger scouts surveying the wilderness to keep an eye on things, and most dangerous Pokémon having been killed or forced out over the centuries. Until human problems like the Rockets make an appearance things are pretty idyllic.

There’s definitely a suspension of disbelief required, however, no matter how much I try to develop the system.

## **Q.323. I vaguely remember there being an old anime episode(Grampa Canyon, I believe? Main thing I remember is Charmeleon evolving haha) where they found a bunch of fossil Pokemon still living inside the caverns. Are there any cases of that kind of thing in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Fossil Pokemon, Relicanth*


Good question\! Honestly, I’m not a fan of that idea just because of how unrealistic it is for the fossil Pokémon to have survived in a tiny community like that for so long...but I also hate just outright denying stuff like that was in the anime. I’d probably try to spin it off as a refuge for released fossil Pokémon, honestly. Maybe a research project designed to see how they’d interact in the wild? I’d have to put some more thought into it.

Then again, Relicanth is a thing so who knows\!

## **Q.324. Will the Aether foundation make an appearance anytime in the near future?**

- ## *Tags: Aether Foundation, Crime*


I might make reference to Aether, but honestly I’m not sure if Traveler will reach that far. I’d like for Ash to at least visit every main region, so they’ll likely make some sort of appearance.

## **Q.325. If you rank how old each league is, does it follow the order of the games?**

- ## *Tags: Hoenn, Indigo, League, Region, Sinnoh, Unova, Volumo Empire*


Not really\! I did have Indigo as the first as a reference to the original gens, but Hoenn is actually one of the newest Leagues after existing as separate city-states since the fall of the Volumo Empire a little over a thousand years ago. I based them a little on Italy. Sinnoh has ancient civilization, but also a fairly old League. Unova’s League is relatively new, while Kalos incorporated the League model after the Last War into their traditional aristocracy.

## **Q.326. What regions would you say have the rockiest relationship with Kanto besides Orre?**

- ## *Tags: Alder, Champion, Indigo, Kanto, Last War, League, Orre, Region, Unova*


That’s a hard one. Most major powers are pretty warm with the new generation of Champions that came in the last decade or so \- most are highly idealistic, having been born during or shortly after the Last War and raised on the stories of its horrors. There’s still some bitterness between older generations of Unovans and Kanto, but that’s mostly overshadowed due to Alder’s new League essentially purging the former government from its ranks.

## **Q.327. There is also quite a bit of tension between Hoenn and Unova still, right?**

- ## *Tags: Alder, Drake, Hoenn, Kanto, League, National League, Unova*


Similar situation to Kanto \[see question 326\]. Hoenn suffered under Unova, but during the Unovan Restoration they built closer ties. Drake was hard on them, but fair to the new government and wise enough to see the necessity of building war torn Unova up instead of tearing it further down as some of his command desired. 

One thing that urged Alder and the new League of Unova a lot of goodwill is that they rose up in a coup after staging a rebellion for much of the Last War, punching holes in the Unovan defenses and seizing key locations and leaders of the fascist government. They saved tens of thousands of lives on both sides, which made the National League much happier to negotiate with them on warmer terms.

## **Q.328. Assuming they follow the same lives, what happened to Ash’s pokemon in the original anime that were abused/abandoned by their original trainers? Like Charmander, for example.**

- ## *Tags: League, Pokemon Trainer*


For the sake of avoiding grimdark I’ll say the existence of a political, competent Pokémon League got the ones who needed help the help they needed, while the others live happily.

## **Q.329. On Ash’s goal for Nidoking’s growth.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Nidoking, Pokemon Behaviour*


Yep, Ash desperately wants Nidoking to have his own identity. Pretty much the entire team invests a great deal of their identity into Ash \- and he does the same for them \- but Nidoking basically grew into an extension of Ash out of sheer loyalty.

## **Q.330. On the Black Broth.**

- ## *Tags: Black Broth*


Yep, I was inspired by the Spartan black soup. No exact recipe survived, but the main ingredients were pigs’ legs, blood, salt and vinegar. Obviously they aren’t using Pokémon legs for the broth (anymore), but I imagine protein from the artificial meat plants and a disgusting amount of nutrients are packed into it, plus a few secret ingredients for fun :slight\_smile: I can’t spill all the secrets, but that’s the base\!

The black broth is basically half valuable nutrition in the field and half hazing. It’s an acquired taste, but there are additions some trainers can use that make it tolerable.

## **Q.331. On Metagross’ diet.**

- ## *Tags: Metagross, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology, Rock type, Steel type, Wild Pokemon*


Yep, I always figured that Metagross were ultimate omnivores. Probably a large amount of their diet comes from rock and steel-types, but they eat basically any living thing they can find in the wild.

The black broth is basically half valuable nutrition in the field and half hazing. It’s an acquired taste, but there are additions some trainers can use that make it tolerable.

## **Q.332. What would you say is the most dangerous Pokemon? Not strongest but just so insanely dangerous to train.**

- ## *Tags: Chandelure, Ghost type, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Trainer*


Honestly, Chandelure (and ghosts in general) are way up on that list.

Just because they can be so unpredictable and their abilities don’t mesh well with human squishiness.

## **Q.333. What does being a ghost type mean in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Ghost type, Pokemon Biology*


Hmm, I’d say the closest I can get to a real definition (without too many spoilers) is an extradimensional entity that’s slipped into the material world. They’re eroded by existing in the Pokémon World, and require some corporeal form to possess and manipulate to continue existing.

## **Q.334. How do abilities like No Guard, Contrary, Protean, Wonderguard, etc. carry over to Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Contrary, No Guard, Protean, Wonder Guard*


Pretty much as \[redacted\] described \[see question 269\]\! Protean is something I have plans to address, but haven’t settled on a specific explanation. Contrary would probably be a more psychological thing \- say a Pokémon tried to intimidate a Pokémon, but it would just infuriate the other Pokémon and make it more aggressive instead. No Guard is more psychological\!

## **Q.335. Can some ghosts like Decidueye and Jellicent have eggs?**

- ## *Tags: Decidueye, Ghost type, Jellicent, Pokemon Biology*


Yep, some ghosts can\! It mostly depends on the species.

## **Q.336. What's the current listed height for Bruiser? I remember Bruno's Machamp being something like 6' and being referred to as massive for the species.**

- ## *Tags: Bruiser, Bruno, Machamp, Pokemon Biology*


Gonna be honest, Bruno’s Machamp’s size will probably come down to being early installment weirdness\! I’ve trended towards Pokémon being significantly larger than the PokeDex lists in most cases. Can’t remember if I’ve given an actual height for Bruiser in the past, but I’d say he’s somewhere around six feet? Bruno’s will probably suspiciously grow the next time he appears...although I do like the idea of a strangely short Machamp that’s just an absolute unit.

## **Q.337. How many vines does Tangrowth have roughly?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Biology, Tangrowth*


I’d say he has several hundred, but not all are suitable for combat. Many are thinner and designed for more delicate work, but he has dozens of combat ready vines that can extend to long ranges.

## **Q.338. If he\[Tangrowth\] had all of his combat one’s outstretched, would we see smaller vines protecting the rest of him? \[see question 337\]**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Biology, Tangrowth*


Yep\! Sort of like an undercoat of vines.  They’re responsible for a lot of his shock absorption.

## **Q.339. How do friendship evolution’s work in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology*


I can’t find the quote I gave \[see question 118\], but basically it tends to affect highly social Pokémon. When they have high positive feelings \- which in the wild correlated to feelings of safety or status \- they would evolve and assume leadership positions.

## **Q.340. If Ash were to channel Lightning through the Feather, would he be able to stimulate the evolution of any electric types?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Electric type, Electrizer, Evolution, Feather, Pokemon Biology, Technology*


Yep, he could. It would have to be directed into the electric-type (not just in the area) but would be able to stimulate evolution. It would be a struggle to mimic the intensity of an Electrizer, but would be feasible if he was careful.

Theoretically he can channel just as much power as Tani did in Recollections, but he limits himself (and for good reason).

## **Q.341.Is there a distinction between vertebrates and invertebrates in the Travelerverse? I meant neurologically.**

- ## *Tags: Aerodactyl, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology* 


 I’m rolling with the ‘every Pokémon is sentient\[sapient\]’ category for Traveler purposes. It makes the wild and Pokémon training an ethical nightmare when looked at too closely, but it rolls with the suspension of disbelief. Some Pokémon have different thought patterns and might not have the same attachment and ‘human’ emotions that many Pokémon do, but can still think and operate at a much higher level than any animal in our world. Even the dumbest Pokémon tend to be very intelligent \- I’d rank them at worst as dolphin or elephant levels of intelligence, but with psychic powers making inter species communication possible I think there’s a much higher awareness and value placed on them.

I figure that intelligence is a self-selecting for trait in Pokémon, so it’s naturally risen over the years as a form of competition. Aerodactyl is still very intelligent, but her mind operates in a way more similar to, say Blue from Jurassic Park World than the happy go lucky Pokémon we know. She’s more controlled, but still naturally more savage.

## **Q.342. I am a little surprised to not see more fire pokemon in Ash's team since he is in possession of the feather, I kind of thought they might get attracted to it a bit.**

- ## *Tags: Absol, Ash, Hoenn, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology*


Honesty, Ash is a beacon for a lot of Pokémon at this point bht\[but\] is so mobile that they have a hard time keeping up. Pay attention to the references to Absol migratory movements while he was in Hoenn...

## **Q.343. On Ash’s growth.**

- ## *Tags: Ash*


Yep, honestly Ash is in the sweet spot where he has the motivation, is insanely dedicated to training at all hours, and found his way into the connections to maximize his talent. Not even mentioning that he’s pretty much addicted to battling lol. Oh, and the fact that his team freaking loves him. That helps a lot too.

## **Q.344. What sort of psychic niche does Grumpig fit into? Is it more mental technique oriented or physical manifestation focused?**

- ## *Tags: Grumpig, Pokemon Battle, Psychic type*


It strikes a bit of a balance. Grumpig excels at defensive psychic abilities and limited physical manipulation, but also has a great deal of talent in striking mentally at opponents to daze or disorient them.

- ## *Tags: Dazed, Grumpig, Psychic type, Teleport*

## **Q.346. How does the league properly protect their spectators for champion level ghost, dark, and bug special attacks? A shed load of Alakazam?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Bug type, Dark type, Ghost type, Pokemon Battle*

## **Q.347. Why is it that Alakazam have largely been used for barriers so far? being more common and or versatile?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Pokemon Battle, Psychic type*


Mostly they are versatile. They’re also very adept at keeping an eye on combatants thoughts and using that to prepare the defenses accordingly. Even when other psychics are used for additional power and security, Alakazam tend to be at the center of the network.

## **Q.348. On the fail safes in place during a Pokemon Battle.**

- ## *Tags: Absol, Ash, Hoenn, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology*


There tends to be redundant failsafes, and it’s ridiculously difficult to actually shatter psychic barriers. It’s happened, but there is never only one layer protecting spectators in high-level matches. Bad PR if a bunch of people get burnt by an angry Magmortar.

## **Q.349. Is Brusier the biggest fucking tank of a Machoke in Traveler verse or what?**

- ## *Tags: Bruiser, Fighting type, Machoke, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Biology, Rampage*


Yep, it’s even something that’ll be addressed when Ash meets Bruno haha. Rampage is essentially one of the only ways for a Machoke to reasonably increase their physical strength. Most Machoke are so ridiculously strong already that they would never try to increase it for fear of losing control \- the way they see it, their strength is already 15/10 so it’s best to focus on other aspects of battling. So as a result Bruiser is one the strongest, most durable Machoke on the freaking planet...but it also ties into his fears of being unable to control that strength.

## **Q.350. On Ash’s team's natural ability.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Infernus, Pokemon Battle*


Yep, Infernus is pretty much the only one of the teams that’s a natural monster. The others’ bodies have just adapted to the crazy training and dedication.

## **Q.351. On Ash’s team's future growth.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Hoenn, Master Trainer, Pokemon Battle, Tangrowth*


Oh yeah\! We’re going to see some rapid growth when he \[Trangrowth\] gets to Hoenn and the pace picks up, and Ash will be getting that boost that lets him fight more fairly with Masters. It’ll open up a lot of new opponents for him and I can really have him go wild\!

And yeah, we’ll probably see battling take less of a priority. Lots of training, but with a lack of meaningful opponents most will be more low key.

## **Q.352. Elf who’s your favorite Pokémon that you wrote?**

- ## *Tags: Dazed, Infernus, Meta*


Hmm, Dazed is the funnest to write in terms of dialogue and interactions \- she has that extra layer through her telepathy. 

My favorite to write is probably Infernus though. He’s such a maniac and I kind of wrote him how I felt when I used to wrestle \- just that thrill of fighting and willingness to do anything to win.

## **Q.353. On how Infernus is regarded by other Pokemon Trainers.**

- ## *Tags: Infernus, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Trainer*


One thing that helps Infernus is that he’s so terrifying to most trainers that EVERYONE is trying to think up counters for him. 

## **Q.354. Do the public even know that the First Champion having a Rhydon is the reason for all the Rhydon symbols? Or has that been lost to time and just taken for granted in the present?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Chinatsu, Mamoru, Ninetales, Rhydon, Shinobu, Taimu, Tauros*


They do know that the First’s cornerstone was a Rhydon, and historians are aware he had a Ninetales and Tauros as well.

There was more common iconography of Chinatsu and Shinobu alongside the First and Mamoru in the first few centuries after the unification, but eventually Rhydon overshadowed the others.  
Chinatsu prefers to be forgotten as well. Makes her work much easier.

## **Q.355. Will we find out about what happened to Tangrowth before Ash caught him? And does destiny bond affect Infernus’s passive flames since it’s technically accidental damage?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Destiny Bond, Infernus, Tangrowth, Pokemon Battle*


Most likely not for Tangrowth, I want some things to stay mysteries\! And yes, the feedback from the pain caused by Infernus’ flames would still affect Destiny Bond. Some Destiny Bond users will deliberately injure themselves to hurt their linked opponent.

## **Q.356. How does Distortion interact with Aura, if at all?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Distortion, Psychic type*


I won’t go into detail, but I will say that you can look at Aura as positive, psychic powers as neutral, and Distortion as negative and make of that what you will.

## **Q.357. How (if at all) does the Scyther \> Scizor evolution happen in the wild? Or is Scizor only typically found in the hands of trainers/as released Pokemon? Is Pain Split similar to Destiny Bond in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Destiny Bond, Evolution, Ghost type, Pain Split, Pokemon Biology, Scizor, Scyther, Wild Pokemon*


So my current theory for Scyther is something along the lines of their evolution taking place once they’ve hit their prime. Their armor slowly begins to harden, and at a certain point when they’ve reached full maturity their body registers higher level of minerals, which provides the impetus for evolution. 

And yep, Pain Split is another one of those primarily mental techniques, although ghosts can use it on each other (or other Pokémon with enough training) to absorb their energy for their own use. For the most part it doesn’t actually heal the user, but just tears the opponent down to a similar level of pain. It’s often used by badly injured Pokémon \- in the wild, it evolved primarily as a way to frighten off predators who had managed to do quite a bit of damage already.

In general I try to treat trade evolutions as more ‘experience’ evolutions in Traveler.

## **Q.358. In that respect then, I imagine Metal Coats are made to quicken up that process\[evolution\] for trainer owned Scythers and Onix, as well as just generally being useful for Steel and Rock types, I assume? \[see question 357\]**

- ## *Tags: Evolution, Metal Coat, Onix, Rock type, Scyther, Steel type*


Yep\! I figure they’re just a way of giving some control to the trainer and Pokémon instead of waiting for nature to take its course.

## **Q.359. I wonder how far back the historical record goes? Like we know there are entities like Chinatsu that tell his feats to others, but how much does the average person know about the time?**

- ## *Tags: Chinatsu, Concept, Fuchsia City, Mamoru, Psychic type, Wild Pokemon*


There are Pokémon that serve as living repositories of information as well as many who have destroyed vast amounts of information through their inherent power. Mamoru and Chinatsu singlehandedly set Fuchsia’s development back centuries in their rampage, for example. There are several examples of this that will be explored within the story\! 

But yes, it can be very difficult to retain information through psychics. They (and Pokémon in general) see the world in a very different lens than humanity. They tend to view the world in terms of concepts and roles rather than as individuals...plus, psychics are just plain confusing to communicate with in general. A major advantage of human records is the ease in which they can be reproduced and understood.

## **Q.360. Has Mewtwo made plans to fight the other legends like Darkrai if it came to it?**

- ## *Tags: Darkrai, Legendary Pokemon, Mew, Mewtwo, Unown, Pokemon Battle*


After Mew’s warning Mewtwo has been very paranoid and is trying to seek others out. Witnessing the Unown and their power shook him badly.

## **Q.361. Is Ash going to have to participate in the Indigo League again and win it before challenging the Elite 4?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Elite Four, Indigo, League, Pokemon Battle*


Nope, as a member of the League Ash will be able to make his own challenge when he’s ready.

## **Q.362. Will Ash be changing his tactics/strategy now that he battled Karen? Would Steven teachings sink in and Ash know when to use Lance powerhouse techniques properly?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Elite Four, Karen, Lance, Pokemon Battle, Steven*


Yep\! Ash will be adapting due to his loss.

## **Q.363. Have you ever been afraid that you've made Ash's team a bit too powerful? If so, how did you remedy this?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Infernus, Pryce, Torrent*


Oh absolutely\! If I could go back to 2012 I’d slow down his early development a bit. We’re seeing the struggle right now as he’s in the difficult spot of being too powerful for 99.9% of trainers to beat but isn’t quite ready to take down the best of the best. Finding compelling opponents for him is very difficult, and as a result Ash is generally using his weaker members more and more often to get a bit of a thof rill. But if it’s a real fight and he has to bust out Infernus or Torrent there’s very, very few cases where he could reasonably lose. It’s one of the reasons I’ve tried giving him new hobbies and interests outside training. It does give me an excuse to go full steam ahead into worldbuilding, though\! 

But good question\! I guess the way I remedy it when it comes to battles is to have Ash more interested in the fight itself than just winning. We see it with Pryce, for example. Ash wants to help his team grow and chooses teammates that will be tested by the battle instead of just tossing out Infernus. If he wanted to just win he would release his strongest every battle. Instead, Ash wants to grow. In tournaments he’ll always go for the win, but outside of that he sees much more value in a good fight.

## **Q.364. When it comes to fleshing out Ash, how do you approach that?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Delia, Lance, Pallet Town*


Of course\! So basically I worked it in as naturally as I could. In Pallet I figure most of their trainer classes would revolve around survival, practical skills, and science. With history somewhat neglected, I figure Ash’s original interest would mostly be shown through his love of his mom’s stories and myths. 

Over time, as Ash learned more about the world and discovered these incredible secrets, that evolved into more of an interest in history as well. I see Ash as someone who has a genuine love of learning \- of people, history, science, and learning for the sake of learning...probably something he inherited from Delia. He’s all about growth, and I felt that it would just grow stronger over time as he hears Lance’s stories or discovers treasures like the First’s tomb.

So while him getting hobbies is partly an important tool I use as the focus shifts somewhat away from his growth in battling to his growth as an individual, I also wanted it to reflect a natural growth of Ash’s character. If you look back it’s a development you can trace throughout much of the story until it’s reached its current state. It felt natural instead of suddenly giving Ash an interest in, say, interpretive dance.

## **Q.365. Does Traveler contain any small insects?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Legendary Pokemon, Mew, Pokemon Biology, Wild Pokemon*


So it’s something I’m hesitant to give actual answers on, but here are my thoughts: bacteria and microorganisms exist 100%. They’re in the best position to survive extreme environments in the Pokémon World. Actual animals do not exist because they’d just be horrifically outcompeted on every front \- intelligence, not being able to breathe fire, durability, etc. 

One thing I’d like to be clear on is that the original life on the Pokémon World evolved exactly as ours did. It just couldn’t properly survive because of the Legends, and as a result Mew edited in traits to make complex life feasible, which resulted in Pokémon’s impossible attributes over time. 

That said, I can imagine tiny insects existing to a point. It’s not something I plan on addressing in-story, but the only organisms I can feasibly imagine surviving the challenges of the Pokémon World are R-type organisms that don’t require many resources to survive, emphasize extremely quick reproductive cycles, and would do the work of pollinating that many Pokémon are just too large and resource-intensive to properly do. One Pokémon can accomplish the work of tens or hundreds of animals in our world, but I figure tiny insects are more suited for things like pollination.

## **Q.366. On whether Pokemon meat is sold.**

- ## *Tags: Slowpoke, Pokemon Berry, Team Rocket, Wild Pokemon*


There is a market for ‘real’ Pokémon meat. Super illegal but you know Team Rocket is in it with things like Slowpoke tails. Messed up rich people have to get their jollies somehow I guess.

But yeah, that’s taken a massive hit with Team Rocket’s near destruction. That’s one market the League is particularly interested in disrupting.

Yep. Back in the day it was a matter of survival. There are berries that provide large amounts of protein, but products from Pokémon were invaluable.

## **Q.367. Are there pokemon that eat other pokemon much in the wild?**

- ## *Tags: Frontier Regions, League, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology, Wild Pokemon*


Most are primarily satisfied by League feeding stations, but it’s pretty common for hunting to occur, especially in the wild areas with fewer resources from the League. Prey Pokémon are generally accepting of occasional deaths from predators, but if a wild Pokémon is killing for the sake of killing the local populations will band together and kill the offender. There’s a balance there. 

Sort of. We don’t see major alterations from domestication, but due to human influence the world’s a much, much nicer and safer place in the core regions. The frontiers are much wilder, and the world remains unchanged in areas outside the human domain.

## **Q.368 Given that wild Pokémon are appeased by the various leagues, do Aqua and Magma appease ground and water types respectively in part by promising to expand the land and sea by awakening their gods?**

- ## *Tags: League, Team Aqua, Team Magma, Wild Pokemon*


Ehhhhh kind of? Magma are extremely human-centric and want to create new land that humans can colonize without having to fight wild Pokémon for it. Aqua are much closer with nature and Pokémon and have close working relationships with the wild Pokémon in the archipelago.

The problem is that local water-types on the shoreline aren’t too happy to lose habitat and tend to sabotage human attempts to expand. 

They also don’t quite realize the extent of what they’re waking up haha. Neither Aqua or Magma really have any idea of what they’re doing lol.

But yeah, Aqua aren’t that bad aside from trying to wake up an Eldritch sea god. They do a lot of anti-poacher activity and help protect the archipelago since the League can’t effectively manage its entire territory. They’re largely made up of locals.

## **Q.369. I presume they’ve \[Team Aqua\] got a strong underground PR network and are seen as a more benevolent, covert Greenpeace? \[see question 368\]**

- ## *Tags: Team Aqua, Team Magma, Technology, TM*


Pretty much\! They’re extremely popular and have no end of recruits. They also tend to be more powerful individually than Magma, although Magma has more resources and more powerful fighters due to heavy use of TMs and other training techniques.

## **Q.370. On Mewtwo’s willingness to battle.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Legendary Battle, Mewtwo, Unown*

Mewtwo’s still a bit of a bully. He doesn’t like fighting battles he’s not sure he can win, and the Unown were strange enough that he decided to stay out of it haha. Like you said \[redacted\], can’t blame him. He’s happy to just do his part in keeping Ash alive and letting him do the heavy lifting since Ash keeps ending up in these situations.

## **Q.371. Could Team Aqua be truly considered a criminal organization? considering they mostly do anti-poaching operations and help protect the archipelago.**

- ## *Tags: League, Team Aqua, Team Magma*

That’s something I’ve mentioned before somewhere in Traveler. They’re into shady stuff, but the League largely tolerates their activity and works with them on occasion. Aqua is tolerated for helping protect the archipelago. Magma is more obviously sketchy but has powerful friends.

## **Q.372. If a shiny Metagross reproduces, would the Beldum also be shiny?**

- ## *Tags: Beldum, Metagross, Pokemon Biology, Shiny Pokemon*

Yep, Shiny Metagross would produce new Shiny Beldum.

## **Q.373. If Metagross evolve by first Beldum combining into Metang, and then two metang into metagross, would that not lead to odd combinations if you had a shiny and a normal one? They're different metal compositions, no? Which gets precedence?**

- ## *Tags: Beldum, Evolution, Metagross, Metang, Pokemon Biology, Shiny Pokemon*

I can kind of imagine it as them basically pooling their different alloys during evolution, then redistributing it evenly over the Metang or Metagross. This could lead to degrees of shininess depending on how many of Metagross’ component Beldum were born shiny.

## **Q.374. Were all fossil pokemon rock types pre-fossilization?**

- ## *Tags: Aerodactyl, Fossil Pokemon, Lance, Rock type*

It’s more of a trend than anything. Pokémon from those eras tend to be more primal, like Lance’s Aerodactyl. It’s not a hard rule, however, and they do have personalities beyond that. 

Huh, good question. I think many were rock-types, but others simply have the rock-type built into them as a way of making them tougher and more robust. Helps a lot in the modern world.

## **Q.375. On Elf’s opinion about future Regions and their Pokemon.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Region*

Ha, I figure I can at least have them exist. Not sure if Ash will end up visiting them all except briefly, but I want to keep the world growing\!

## **Q.376. On leftover space for future Regions in the Traveler World Map.**

- ## *Tags: Location, Region, Southern Continent, World Map*
