## **Q.377. Would Ash getting a Fairy Type have some meaning or help him grow as Pokemon Trainer?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Fairy type, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Trainer*

Yep, it would definitely provide some growth and new tactical choices.

## **Q.378. Does Magic, the one that turned Ash into Ashachu, exist in the Traveller verse?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo*

Hmm, not really. The closest you could get is Aura which has an essentially unlimited versatility, but which is entirely dependent on the individual. Then again, once you get to the Legendary psychics like Mewtwo they can essentially do whatever they want, so that might as well count as magic.

## **Q.379. I swear if I remember right didn't a Lugia get turned Into Shadow Pokemon XD001 right?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Lugia, XD001*

For the earlier discussion, I’ll just say and confirm that XD001 was not Lugia but maintained the same level of power we saw in the game \- pulling the cruise ship from the ocean and dumping it in the desert happened, for example.

## **Q.380. On Cipher.**

- ## *Tags: Cipher*

Yep, Cipher solves the biggest problem in war: having soldiers willing to kill. Most Pokémon aren’t willing to mercilessly slaughter or follow ruthless orders without a good cause, especially without a real connection with their trainer. Cipher created fighting machines and used them to great effect.

## **Q.381. Do Mismagius within Traveler also subsist off of fear in a similar way to Dazed with dreams? If so, would Mismagius literally just attack with Confuse Ray against potential prey in order to feed?**

- ## *Tags: Confuse Ray, Dazed, Ghost type, Karen, Mismagius, SPECTRE Corps*

Yep\! They feed off emotions. We’ll get to learn a bit more next chapter\! But I have it as most ghosts being able to feed off emotions in general, but it’s a hundred times easier to jump out and scare a victim to feed than it is to make them happy and feed off that. But yes, Mismagius might use weak techniques to enhance their victim’s fear, but most try to be delicate. Going full out on squishy humans is a good way to get Karen and her SPECTERs on their trail.

Mismagius would probably open up with a Confuse Ray or other debilitating technique to make sure more dangerous prey couldn’t pose a threat. 

## **Q.382. I’m kind of curious if Mismagius would need to migrate from town to town in order to prevent desensitisation from starving them?**

- ## *Tags: Mismagius, Ghost type, Pokemon Behaviour*

Yep\! In rural areas or small towns it’s pretty common for Mismagius and other ghosts to need to move around frequently. In larger towns there’s enough prey that they don’t have to worry about it, but they do have to take a little less from each victim so it doesn’t turn into a big enough issue to attract attention.

## **Q.383. Would Mewtwo actually live for Millenia, or potentially even tens of thousands of years?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Team Rocket, Psychic type*

Naturally, I think Mewtwo would have either a human or slightly shorter life span since Team Rocket’s genetic engineering was so cutting edge \- they hadn’t had time to really perfect it. 

His psychic powers render his ‘natural’ life span irrelevant, however. He essentially has total mastery over the physical world, including his own biology. Extending his life is less than child’s play for him \- he doesn’t even really have to think about it.

## **Q.384. What would you say is your favorite created technique?**

- ## *Tags: Mind Breaker, Pokemon Battle, Rampage, Sneasel*

Hmm my favorite one that I’ve shown so far is probably Rampage\! My real favorite hasn’t been revealed yet.

Mind Breaker is going to be a ton of fun once Sneasel has a bit more experience\! I have techniques planned out for each member of the team that should be really cool\!

## **Q.385. On Suicune’s strength.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Entei, Legendary Beasts, Legendary Pokemon, Pokemon Battle, Raikou, Suicune*

Suicune just embodies a different concept than Entei or Raikou but they’re all the same level of strength.

In a real fight, I’d prefer Raikou or Entei on my side honestly. Suicune’s incredibly effective but it wouldn’t be truly invested in any battle (unless you have Ash around to link with it).

## **Q.386. If a Concept like Suicune embodies is irrevocably changed, what happens?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Legendary Beasts, Legendary Pokemon, Suicune*

Hmm interesting question\! I don’t think they can be irrevocably changed. You can see it nudged in a certain direction or diluted by another Concept temporarily, but I think it would always return to its baseline given time.

## **Q.387. So Suicune just was concerned about accidental collateral damage, then, and temporarily altering its concept? \[see question 386\]**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Concept, Legendary Beasts, Legendary Pokemon, Suicune*

Yep, and more than anything concerned about irrevocably damaging Ash. He’s not as easy to change as most humans, but he’s still pretty squishy at this point.

## **Q.388. How aware are the other Leagues about Ash's involvement in the Legendaries event? I imagine the National League knows a lot, but how about Unova and Kalos'?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Kalos, Lance, League, Legendary Pokemon, National League, Unova*

National League is fully aware. They’re privy to every bit of information Ash has told Lance and the League. The National League has ensured the other Leagues are aware of the threat and provided a huge amount of scientific data supporting their claims, but leave Ash out of it as much as possible.

## **Q.389. Does anyone know how old Ash was at the Conference Finals?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Ash, Conference, Hoenn, Indigo, Vermillion City*

He turned eleven in Chapter 3 on the way to Vermillion I believe. He turned 12 in Chapter 32, I think. Right before he went to Hoenn.

## **Q.390. The Sinnohoans go by a different calendar?**

- ## *Tags: Alfa Dynasty, Alola, Galar, Kalos, National League, Orre, Sinnoh, Unova*

Sinnoans had their own calendar based on the beginning of the Alfa dynasty, but it’s fallen out of use. Pretty much the whole world has adapted to PIL as a result of the National League being such a monolithic entity. 

Kalos and Galar had their own calendar traditions, Unova developed in relative isolation and has its own. New colonized regions like Orre and Alola began with PIL out of practicality.

## **Q.391. On a future Bruiser v. Snorlax rematch.**

- ## *Tags: Bruiser, Pokemon Battle, Rampage, Snorlax*

Rampage\!Bruiser in a rematch against Snorlax would be really, really cool. Snorlax would be able to survive multiple hits pretty easily, but Bruiser would also be in the situation of completely outclassing Snorlax in maneuverability. Plus Bruiser’s still in the situation where he doesn’t get superior anchoring or anything \- hits from Snorlax would send him flying. 

## **Q.392. How replicable is Air Lens?**

- ## *Tags: Air Lens, Fire type, Jonathan, Magcargo, Magmar*

Air Lens is a fairly simple technique for certain species like Magmar and Magcargo, but extremely draining for other fire-types. They can learn it but it can be best used in short bursts instead of sustained. 

I envision Air Lens as something that was difficult to discover, but easy to reproduce if that makes any sense.

Air Lens is also a fairly recent development if I remember right, generally taught by specialists to their apprentices (or people like Jonathan) who are usually pretty leery of teaching it to other trainers. It’s not unheard of, but it’s difficult to learn by yourself.

## **Q.393. How strong Bruiser really is?**

- ## *Tags: Bruiser, Fighting type*

I don’t honestly have the expertise to give exact numbers\! What I will say is that Bruiser is to the point where increases in raw strength don’t actually matter much in battle \- his raw strength is so much above other fighting-types that it doesn’t matter what he’s facing other than another super strong Pokémon. At this point his biggest issues are anchoring and getting leverage to actually use his ridiculous strength to its full potential.

## **Q.394. When he \[Bruiser\] uses Rock Tomb, would he use that to give himself better leverage and to unbalance his opponents? If fighting another super strong Pokémon? \[see question 393\]**

- ## *Tags: Bruiser, Pokemon Battle, Protect, Rock Tomb*

Yep, Rock Tomb will be great for bracing himself and keeping him in a fight. Protect as well.

## **Q.395. On Oz’s stamina as an Electivire.**

- ## *Tags: Evolution, Infernus, Oz*

Oz will have better stamina once she evolves, but Infernus is just a natural stamina freak...partly because he throws 100% into every battle. She can improve, but I don’t think she’ll ever quite match him on that front.

She still has a lot of development to go through\!

## **Q.396. On the effect of Rampage on Bruiser’s growth.**

- ## *Tags: Bruiser, Evolution, Rampage*

Rampage basically counted as an evolution for him haha. It compensated for so many of his weaknesses.

## **Q.397. How does the energy used by Dragons work, is it produced in an organ like Dark types have for Distortion?**

- ## *Tags: Dark type, Distortion, Dragon type, Pokemon Biology*

Good question\! So, I have some thoughts on draconic energy but I’m still working on some aspects. I won’t go into detail yet but I will give you some tentative basics. 

It comes from both within and without. Dragon’s are by their very nature powerful. Their bodies are strong and tough, their natural abilities superior to most other Pokémon. This dominance and power is intrinsic to their nature, and it’s something that they can express into the world in the form of draconic energy. 

The without comes from the fact that draconic energy is latent throughout the universe. Truly skilled dragons are able to use that power to fuel their own abilities. 

I won’t go into more detail than that for now, but I hope it answered your question\!

## **Q.398. It's especially interesting that you mentioned Draconic Energy being latent through the universe, since (and IIRC you did play OR) so is Infinity Energy. Is it then the case that those are one and the same? \[see question 397\]**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Dragon type*

Infinity Energy is difficult. It gives me just enough that I can make some guesses and try to work it into my framework, but it’s a little frustrating that they have such little information on it in Gen VI and then proceed to never revisit it.

In Traveler, I’d envision Infinity energy as related to Aura, essentially the first steps of a more modern approach to understanding it.

## **Q.399. On Ash’s team longevity. \[see question 46\] \[see question 130\]**

- ## *Tags: Age, Aron, Ash, Tangrowth, Torrent*

Torrent will most likely live for around two centuries. Tangrowth and Aron are biologically immortal. The rest are somewhere around human length.

## **Q.400. Do all dragons have that sort of longevity, or is it limited to the Kingdra line? \[see question 399\]**

- ## *Tags: Dragonite, Dragon type, Kingdra, Last War, Yari*

Dragonite can live up to two hundred. Elder Yari’s Dragonite just sustained massive damage in the Last War that cut her lifespan down dramatically.

## **Q.401. What happens to pokemon that outlive their trainer, like Torrent when Ash kicks the bucket?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Ash, League, Pokemon Behaviour, Torrent, Wild Pokemon*

Some choose to work with the League or remain with their trainer’s friends or families. Others go their own way and live out in the wild \- these are often the ones the League likes to keep as contacts in the wild Pokémon community.

## **Q.402. Are psychic powers fueled by emotion, as well as the mind? Would a happy memory like ponded infernus be a fuel to make  psychics more powerful?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Psychic type*

Sort of\! It’s a bit of a double-edged Sword. Emotions like anger can help provide brief spurts of focus \- or let psychic output immense amounts of force as they ignore their own limits \- but it also poses the risk of breaking their focus, which is instrumental in using psychic abilities. That brief surge of power is like running a sprint \- a huge, quick output but a psychic will be exhausted afterward. 

Ideally, a psychic retains a cool, detached mind. They won’t have surges, but it increases stamina and offers clarity. Stress, anxiety, and similar emotions can have serious negative effects on psychics, although some actually specialize in using heightened states of emotion to fuel their abilities. There are different techniques, but most favor clarity over passion.

## **Q.403. When champions spar, like Lance and Steven, do they use mega’s? Because it was stated that it took either 3-4 of Lances Pokémon to take down metagross, but is that normal meta or mega meta?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Lance, Mega Evolution, Pokemon Battle, Steven*

Mega are only very rarely used in sparring\! It happens, but the strength it gives a Champion-level pokemon makes them extremely dangerous. That kind of strength can’t be easily controlled.

## **Q.404. On Cynthia vs Steven. \[see question 221\]**

- ## *Tags: Cynthia, Metagross, Pokemon Battle, Spiritomb, Steven*

Cynthia and Steven’s fights can go either way. Steven kind of hard counters her by forcing her to expend two or three of her valuable teammates just to bring down Metagross, but she’s great at outmaneuvering the others...not that they aren’t extremely powerful themselves.

Spiritomb is such a glaring hole in Metagross’ OP armor that Steven has a few plans on how to handle it.

## **Q.405. What would you say is the difference between steel types' armour?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology, Steel type*

Basically their genes just result in the production of different alloys in their armor. Diet and environment also plays a part. 

## **Q.406. Hasn’t Spiritomb also been mentioned to gradually getting weaker or calmer overtime by Cynthia?**

- ## *Tags: Cynthia, Pokemon Battle, Spiritomb*

Yep, Spiritomb is gradually growing weaker as it loses the hatred and malice that fuel it and replaces it with more positive emotions. That said, it can learn to use the new abilities it gains with the new emotions if it’s creative enough...which, with Cynthia as its trainer, it surely is.

It’s losing raw offensive power, but that’s not the only aspect of a fight.

## **Q.407. On Metagross vs. Tyranitar.**

- ## *Tags: Metagross, Pokemon Battle, Tyranitar*

As for Metagross vs. Tyranitar, that honestly comes down to training. In the wild, a lone average Metagross would lose to an average Tyranitar...but they would also probably avoid each other since nothing has anything to gain. Plus a Metagross is likely to have an entire colony backing them up. 

When training and additional techniques are introduced it really comes down to the skill level. Trained Metagross are able to hit Tyranitar where it hurts, but so are Tyranitar against Metagross.

## **Q.408. What is the justification for poison types being weak to psychics?**

- ## *Tags: Muk, Poison type, Pokemon Biology, Psychic type*

I think I referred to it somewhere in the Conference maybe? Basically psychics are extremely good at pinpointing vulnerabilities and poison sacs with their abilities, which are extremely damaging if ruptured.

It does depend on the poison-type, but psychics tends to be effective against the majority. Muk will be vulnerable to piercing attacks like Psybeam, for example. The real strengths of a psychic is just how versatile they are.

## **Q.409. How soon after the Conference did Greenfield happen?**

- ## *Tags: Conference, Greenfield, Indigo*

Roughly three months after the Closing Ceremony\!

## **Q.410. How much bloodier was Orre in Traveler during the events of \[Pokemon\] XD?**

- ## *Tags: Michael, Orre, Wes*

It was definitely at its worst in Colosseum. Wes brought a measure of peace to the region, but it was really just a breath of fresh air. XD was pretty bad, but things only went to Colosseum levels when Michael left \[see question 223\].

## **Q.411. Do we know how the other regional champions in Traveler compare to the big three \[Cynthia, Lance and Steven \]?**

- ## *Tags: Alder, Alola, Champion, Cynthia, Diantha, Drasna, Elite Four, Galar, Kalos, Lance, Last War, League, Leon, National League, Steven, Team Flare, Unova*

I’ll have to keep it a little briefer than I’d like, but I’ll be able to go into more detail this afternoon if you’d like\! 

One thing I’d like to clarify is that Unova and Kalos shifted to the National League’s system of Champion:Elite Four:Gym Leaders after the Last War. They had their own systems of governance beforehand, although some jumps had been made. The National League system just works really, really well in the Traveler world. 

Unova: As of now, I’d say Alder is the weakest of the Champions. Still a monstrous opponent, but he lost important members of his team in the Last War. He’s universally loved in Unova, however, and his relations with his Elite Four are extremely close. He’s been a mentor to most, if not all, of them. 

Kalos: Diantha is another extremely popular Champion, and quite powerful as well. Her diverse team makes her a force to be reckoned with, and she’s similar to Steven in that she’s a very powerful defensive trainer. The Kalos Elite Four is fairly close, but not quite as beloved by the people. All but Drasna (who is from Sinnoh) are from the old aristocracy and seen as somewhat aloof and disconnected. They get along well with Diantha, but the situation will get more and more complicated as Team Flare rises. 

Alola: Doesn’t currently exist, although the calls for a League being implemented are rising. 

Galar: Leon’s actually just a few years older than Ash at this point. Already making a name for himself in Galar, but Galar’s isolationist in Traveler and not much news gets out

## **Q.412. And Metagross are very statistical in nature, right? So how would they fare in this \[a card game called Mao\]?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Metagross, Pokemon Behaviour*

I think Metagross would be great at the statistical part \- probably the best blackjack player of all time \- but Metagross would struggle in something like Mao where there are unwritten rules. They can logic it out, but they’re fairly inflexible. Alakazam would be amazing though. 

## **Q.413. The main reason I was curious structure wise was that it was stated that Drake got 3 E4 kills during the Last War, for clarification. \[See question 411\]**

- ## *Tags: Drake, Elite Four, Kalos, Last War, Master Trainer, National League, Unova*

That's honestly just an inconsistency since I hadn’t developed aspects of the Last War’s repercussions, but one way I might explain it in-story is that Unova and Kalos had already adapted a powerful core of Masters directly serving the government before the Last War. It’s easy to imagine the National League just translating that as ‘Oh, it’s the Unovan Elite Four\!”.

## **Q.414. Why Alakazam? The reading minds thing? \[see question 412\]**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Metagross, Pokemon Behaviour*

Yep, Alakazam and Metagross are both hyper intelligent and capable of processing vast amounts of raw information, but they specialize in different areas. 

Metagross take the computer route: cold, logical, capable of processing enormous amounts of data in instants, and extremely precise. They’re rigid, however, and take what they see as the shortest point from A to B. They also struggle with understanding alternate viewpoints or solutions outside of simple logic. Not to say they’re emotionless, but they’re numb. 

Alakazam are more of what you’d imagine the perfect human brain to be. Extremely intelligent, can maintain multiple streams of thought at once, and very attuned to the emotions and thoughts of others. Most of all, they’re flexible. They see dozens of potential solutions in an instant, many of them not as efficient in the moment but preferable long term (especially when dealing with other humans or Pokémon).

## **Q.415. Honestly in direct battle, I'd imagine Gallade's probably scarier than both \[Alakazam and Metagross\].**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Gallade, Metagross, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Behaviour, Psychic type, Teleport*

A properly trained Gallade is terrifying, especially in a larger scale battle where they can abuse teleportation under the cover of the battlefield’s chaos. They’re amazing at going after squishier psychics that tend to avoid the frontlines.

## **Q.416. Beyond teleportation, would a Gallade be more of a physical psychic specialist?**

- ## *Tags: Gallade, Pokemon Battle, Psychic type*

Yep. Gallade are fairly powerful naturally, so they’d be able to use some mental effects but not to as much effect without proper training. They are excellent at mind-reading, however. While they can use ranged attacks, I view their optimal strategies as teleporting to their opponent and overwhelming them with offense (ideally) or, if they’re incapable of teleportation, using their psychic abilities to protect themselves from ranged attacks and increase their speed while they attempt to close the gap.

There’s a massive spectrum in there, of course. Psychic abilities are ridiculously versatile and a lot depends on the individual.

## **Q.417. When it comes to a Champion being recognised as a Master, is there a criteria that must be met in order for a committee or organisation of some kind to recognise you?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Elite Four, Master Trainer, Pokemon Battle*

No committee or organization involved in being recognized as a Master\! It’s typically just when you’ve achieved enough or shown Master-level skill. A common time to be recognized a Master is defeating or fighting an Elite Four member (or other recognized Master) on fairly even terms. A lot of it just acknowledgement of your skills by another Master. 

But yeah, becoming a Master is basically just tied to the recognition of it. Outside of battling, you’ll often see Specialist Masters publicly recognizing their apprentice as a Master when they have reached that point.

## **Q.418. Is it fine for us to know the relationship between Alder and the other champions?**

- ## *Tags: Alder, Champion, Diantha, Kalos, National League*

Sure\! Alder is on pretty great terms with everyone. His rebellion and coup made the invasion far less bloody than it might’ve been so the National League likes him. The former Champion and leaders of Kalos weren’t huge fans, but he and Diantha are on good terms and rekindled the friendship between their regions.

## **Q.419. Does Professor Oak get included in the same channels as Steven Stone when they're both ex-champions? Or is Steven a special case due to his involvement with Pierce? Is Oak a special exception as he's turned to a researching career, and thus would occupy a different position within the league with his services?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Marcus, League, Professor Oak, Region, SCRY Project, Southern Continent, Steven*

So, basically Oak and Steven are in similar boats where they’ve maintained extremely close ties with the League. Oak has his own responsibilities, but still works closely with them on essential, confidential projects such as SCRY Project. Steven takes a more direct role in acting as a field agent of the League. 

Retired Champions can either choose to retain close contact like Steven/Oak, or you get people like Marcus who wanted nothing more to do with it and went off on an adventure to the Southern Continent. They don’t have the same legal authority unless they’re retained by the League. 

Most Champions will be wealthy or influential enough to have grounds for their team even within a city, but most retired to somewhat isolated, rural areas so they can continue to train easily. Oak’s the premier example of that. 

Former Champions that choose to leave the League will always be highly monitored just to be safe, and there are MANY precautions in place. It would take enormous amounts of resources to stop a Champion-level trainer.

## **Q.420. I take it that Ash is recognized as a Master or on the verge of being recognized as one?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Bruno, Karen, Koga, Master Trainer, Mind Breaker, Will*

Yep\! Ash is basically just beneath proper Master-level. He just needs some refinement. A more established Master like Koga or Bruno would bulldoze him (and by that I mean probably 3 or 4 to 6 in a match) but less experienced Masters like Will and Karen are in his weight class.

I’m really excited to show the techniques that Ash has been working on. Mind Breaker is just the beginning\!

## **Q.421. Would Infernus technically be considered Ash's Ace?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Infernus, Pokemon Battle, Tangrowth, Torrent*

Yep, I’d definitely consider Infernus as the cornerstone. Aside from being a combat beast, he’s instrumental in setting up the battlefield for other teammates. 

It’s kind of a strange situation since Tangrowth and Torrent are both near Infernus’ level, but I think Infernus is the ace as of this moment.

## **Q.422. What's the Champion induction process like?**

- ## *Tags: Champion*

There is a Hall of Fame that only Champions are allowed into where they are inducted, along with a formal ceremony witnessed by the public. Generally, new Champions are trained by their predecessor in the role for a year or two, upon which the previous Champion formally steps down.

## **Q.423. Actually is Ash his \[Lance’s\] first student/apprentice?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Champion, Elite Four, Lance*

Yep, Ash is his first real student. Lance helps other members of the Elite Four; but his specialty hasn’t lined up with others. Ash is his first dedicated student.

## **Q.424. What new regulations do the Leagues are putting on Unown? Like, can you now never gather more than 100 in one place or something?**

- ## *Tags: Greenfield, League, Pokemon Battle, Psychic type, Unown*

Yep, outside of one or two odd individuals that are found they’re extremely uncommon\! Most are only found in protected archaeological sites, and oftentimes trainers aren’t very interested in the rare Unown they do find other than as a curiosity. They aren’t the best battlers on their own\!

It helps that the majority of the Unown were cleaned up and hidden a long time ago. Back in the day it wasn’t uncommon to find psychics and other Pokémon hoarding them, although none ever came close to amassing the numbers needed for a Greenfield incident.

## **Q.425. On human development.**

- ## *Tags: Age, Ash, Legendary Pokemon*

For Traveler, humans are basically identical to real world humans. If I was redoing Traveler, I would age Ash up a few years. At least 13 or 14 (still incredibly young) before going on his journey. But trainers are exposed to circumstances that tend to force them to mature faster. 

As for Ash, he’s just a VERY unique case. Human brains aren’t really supposed to be exposed to Legendaries, let alone the malleable mind of a child. It’s changed him deeply.

## **Q.426. Would prolonged contact with psychic Pokemon also accelerate mental maturity?**

- ## *Tags: Psychic type*

Depends on the psychic Pokémon\! What is certain is that it will change you in some ways, even if it doesn’t necessarily make you mature.

## **Q.427. I wonder if humans would have a weakened ability to communicate verbally? \[see question 426\]**

- ## *Tags: Psychic type*

Yep, there’s a ton of factors \[like age of the human when exposed, length and type of exposure, strength and intelligence of the psychic Pokemon in question, etc.\] at play\! And that’s an interesting question. I think the child would quickly adapt to primarily communicating with their thoughts, even using their thoughts to ask questions. Their ability to speak verbally would atrophy quickly. It does depend on whether the child is psychic or not.

## **Q.428. Can the Magnemite line be artificially created in Traveller?**

- ## *Tags: Magnemite, Pokemon Biology*

Nope, they’re completely natural\! I do imagine them looking slightly different in Traveler \- completely identical, but they appear a bit more natural and rugged instead of the wholly artificial look.

## **Q.429. On the Infernus clone created by Mewtwo.**

- ## *Tags: Infernus, Mewtwo, Pokemon Battle*

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Battle, Porygon*

They can battle if uploaded into a physical form, but their greatest utility is definitely outside of combat. They were created fairly recently, but are useful enough to see widespread adoption. \[see question 274\]

## **Q.431. Elf, favorite and least favorite to write? \[see question 352\]**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Ash, Cynthia, Dazed, Gary, Grey*

I have a few favorites (other than Ash of course). I’ll only use those that have dialogue for this. 

Dazed \- I love the psychic jargon and figuring out how to explain things from a psychic and Pokémon perspective \- is way up there. Gary is up there, of course. Lance is one of my favorites to write as well. Agatha is really fun but she’s very, very difficult for me to write. Bob because he’s such a jackass. 

Least favorite...hmm. I don’t have anyone I absolutely hate writing. There are some who are really difficult to get correctly like Agatha and Cynthia, but I enjoy their characters and the challenge.

That reminds me\! Another one of my favorites is Grey. He was a ton of fun to write even if his appearances were pretty brief.

## **Q.436. Based on that tier list and Elf's statement that Flint's magmortar would beat Infernus quite comfortably, does that mean that Flint's magmortar is Lance's Dragonite or Cynthia's Garchomp level?**

Charizard hasn’t had any interest in fighting Infernus, and ranges too far from Pallet for Infernus to track him down. Infernus hasn’t beaten Arcanine yet, but he’s come close.

## **Q.438. On Infernus’ potential parenthood.**

## **Q.439. Does Steven swear or does he just have a filter around Ash?**

Steven doesn’t swear gratuitously, but it happens. He definitely censors himself around Ash though\!

## **Q.440. What is the order of Prof in terms of power level? I think it's Oak=Rowan\>Birch and Elm?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Trainer, Professor Birch, Professor Elm, Professor Oak, Professor Rowan*

I don’t see Rowan as a real trainer, but I’m sure he has Pokémon companions and partners\! Plus he could always intimidate any Pokémon. He doesn’t need to be a Champion like Oak.

Oak is the exception. Most Professors are academics, not fighters. Oak is just ridiculously good at everything.

## **Q.441. Does Hydreigon actually have intelligence in its’ other heads? Or are they just other sets of eyes and when they snap at each other it’s because Hydreigon is so stupid that it doesn’t realise that it’s fighting itself there?**

- ## *Tags: Hydreigon, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology*

I imagine them to be semi-intelligent. They don’t have proper brains, but have well-developed enough nervous systems that they’re able to react to stimulus. They also receive sensory information from the main head that helps guide them.

It was fun reconciling the information in the PokeDex against how I wanted to portray it in the Conference. When you see Hydreigon’s heads snapping at each other, it’s basically a visible sign of frustration \- the little heads are guided by the main head’s emotions and sensory information, so they start attacking the closest thing to them.

## **Q.442. What did you think of my hypothesis that the original leaders of Ecruteak were Bearers of Ho Ohs and Lugia's Feathers? The Tao and Tsuki?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Ecruteak City, Ho-Oh, Legendary Pokemon, Lugia, Taiyo, Tsuki*

That was a great insight\! The Taiyo and Tsuki are descended from Twin Champions of Ho-Oh and Lugia. They had true authority and power, and their descendants inherited a close connection to Lugia and Ho-Oh. Over time the legends grew muddled, partly due to the Taiyo and Tsuki intentionally spreading propaganda that painted them as true descendants of the Legends to maintain their authority. 

## **Q.443. Does Metagross have any scarring that you can think of?**

- ## *Tags: Drake, Metagross*

I imagine it to have several scratches across its chassis, but it’s so effective at this point that most have darkened to just a shade lighter than its normal color. I can imagine it having a claw mark left over from his battle with Drake that’s still noticeable.

## **Q.444. Did Grey have the organ surgically removed or did he remove it in a more savage (for lack of a better word) way? And was the removal consensual and/or legal?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Dark type, Distortion, Grey, Hydreigon, Pokemon Biology, Psychic type*

So I’ll answer the biggest questions first: It was legal and Hydreigon consented to the surgery. It’s an uncommon procedure, but not unheard of in League teams such as ACE trainers if their team isn’t specifically focused on Distortional abilities and the Pokémon isn’t too reliant on that aspect of their abilities. 

It does require the Pokémon to be fully evolved. Evolution can get weird with crippled or heavily damaged organs. Some will be completely restored, while in other cases a crippled organ like that could cause serious complications over time as the body tries to repair the damage during evolution. 

During the surgery, the organ is not destroyed. It’s Distortional flow is crippled and stunted, but some small flow remains. This results in a minor resistance to psychic abilities, but allows incredibly vital techniques such as teleportation and telepathy (which is a massive boon in the field for ACE Trainers and trainers like Grey) to make it through with some extra effort. 

It also holds some appeal for dark-types as well in that it makes it possible for deeper levels of communication with their trainer, especially if there’s a psychic on their team that can link them. 

The gist of the surgery is that it’s uncommon, but not unheard of. There are valid reasons for it, especially in combat teams, and so long as the Pokémon consents and is informed then it’s allowed.

## **Q.445. On the hurdles Torrent must overcome when battling Infernus.**

- ## *Tags: Ice Storm, Infernus, Pokemon Battle, Teleport, Torrent* 


Teleport is also a nightmare for Torrent. It lets Infernus close the distance immediately and get past Ice Storm if Infernus manages to force Torrent out of the water.

Infernus and Torrent are both interesting in one-on-one because they’re both that ‘army-killer’ type of fighter. Massive AoE and range.

Artillery is a great way to look at them. That’s what I’ve modeled Torrent’s style off of. Good comparison \[redacted\]\!

## **Q.446. Do you limit yourself to the learnsets of Pokémon in game, or if it’s feasible for them to learn the move then they can?**

- ## *Tags: Psychic type, Teleport*

Yep. I stick as close to the games as possible, but I can be flexible. Plus if something’s just an extension of their current (or learnable) abilities they can generally learn it. 

Teleport’s a good example. All psychics can theoretically learn it, but not all have an affinity for it

## **Q.447. How does Wallace compare to the champions we have seen. Did Steven abdicate from his position and Wallace just was the strongest person who was willing to take the job or did Wallace take it from Steven?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Master Trainer, Steven, Wallace*

Wallace is a true Master. He specializes in the sheer complexity of techniques. He can pull things off intricate enough that Ash will have a hard time believing they’re possible. \[see question 198\]

## **Q.448. I'm curious how Elf is going to handle the Gen 8 and the awful decision to do Legendary \[Birds\] Regional variants.**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon*

## **Q.449. Have there been any attempts in infusing Pokémon DNA into Humans in the Traveller to make Pokémon/Human hybrids? Or is this something that's not to be known yet?**

- ## *Tags: Giovanni, League, Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Psychic type* 

Not particularly. It’s not something the League would condone. I’m 100% confident that Giovanni would have had experiments going for it, but I doubt they would meet much success. His experiments were more focused on Mewtwo (which provided all sorts of useful information for other genetic enhancement experiments) and otherwise creating enhanced Pokémon. 

Honestly though, if there were experiments based on enhancing humans, I’d expect it to involve some kind of attempt to introduce psychic-type DNA into a human to enhance their psychic potential. They’d see the points in which humans could feasibly be improved to fight on a Pokémon’s level (aka psychic powers) and focus on that area first and attempt to branch out once they had a better foundation.

## **Q.450. Do they \[the League\] use actual cash like bills and coins? Or is it more of a bitcoin kind of thing, where people can’t see the money?**

- ## *Tags: Conference, League, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Trainer*

The League has many, many sources of income. Taxation is the major one \- I have a hard time imagining Leagues directly taxing property and residents in their territory, but what I do imagine is taxing battle wagers and other trainer activities while their primary source of income is paid by cities to the League from their tax revenue. While the League is a massive overarching presence, they tend to allow cities to handle things like taxation themselves so long as the rules are followed.

Merchandising is huge, of course. They also profit from tournaments (the Conference being the biggest by far) and other events held by the League. 

One of their biggest sources is found in contracting their trainers out. The League is a popular choice of employment for trainers wanting to settle down, and often places trainers with agencies and firms that need them for security or industrial use.

The League is interwoven with industry and business of all sorts. They have a near monopoly on high-level trainers.

## **Q.451. Are pokedollars based on the gold or silver standard or is it something like fiat money?**

- ## *Tags: League*

I’d say fiat.

## **Q.452. On the League’s social programs.**

- ## *Tags: League*

I do imagine the League tends to have very strong social programs. Pokémon make it very easy for many basic needs to be filled. 

I see the Traveler world as having very deep communal roots in most societies. In the old days everyone had to rely on each other heavily to survive in a hostile world, and that attitude has survived to the modern day...it doesn’t hurt that the whole world relies on cooperation with Pokémon either.

## **Q.453. On Ash’s economic status.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, League*

And yep, Ash is very well off. The League likes to keep their elite trainers well taken care of\!

## **Q.454. I guess that Team Rocket was also a major rejection of that communal kind of society with their focus on profit and accumulating power?**

- ## *Tags: Hoenn, Team Magma, Team Rocket*

And yep, I see Team Rocket as being part of a new wave. The world isn’t quite to that point yet, but as technology advances rapidly and reliance on Pokémon and traditional systems becomes (slightly) less necessary, there are people who are taking a much more human-centric view.

We’ll see aspects of that in Hoenn with Magma.

## **Q.455. What’re we thinking about the cost of Mewtwo?**

- ## *Tags: Giovanni, Mewtwo, Team Rocket, Technology*

Yep, I imagine the Mewtwo project went easily into the billions. Team Rocket and their benefactors have deep, deep pockets. It doesn’t hurt that the technology and discoveries developed during the project could also be used in other ventures and repurposed for commercial use.

One thing to remember is that Team Rocket was excellent at moving money from legal investments and ventures into shady areas. They had massive connections in both legal and illegal markets and organizations.

Team Rocket has their hands in pretty much everything. Black market activities, contraband, poaching...and that’s not even getting into the corporate side of it. They held investments in countless companies and operated other businesses to launder their illicit gains. 

The criminal activities operations we see are just the surface level operations. Giovanni craved power above all else and made sure his voice would be heard wherever he went.

## **Q.456. Is it confirmed that Ditto were the result of Rocket experimentation with Mew DNA?**

- ## *Tags: Ditto, Mewtwo, Team Rocket*

I haven’t confirmed it in-story, but Ditto are failed attempts at Mewtwo. Team Rocket didn’t realize their potential at first and many excess specimens escaped or were released.

## **Q.463. How does one get to be an Ace trainer?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Conference, Pokemon Trainer*

ACE Trainers are generally recruited from Conference members\! Generally the final few rounds \- probably starting at Top 32 and maybe Top 64 for special cases \- are where they’re drawn from. There’s extensive training for trainers in terms of law, tactics, and teamwork with similar training for their Pokémon.

## **Q.464. Do the E4 actually go all-out in the E4 challenges?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Champion, Elite Four, League*

Yep. One thing to keep in mind is that the Elite Four and Champion are designed to be as stable as possible. Very few trainers can beat even a single Elite Four member and that’s how the League likes it \- while the system is designed to reward hard work and talent, they would rather keep members on as long as possible. 

When you do see Elite Four shake-ups, it’s normally due to members retiring. Generally the League prefers to bring high potential trainers in as ACE or Elite Four trainees, train them up, and have internal challengers for positions that they already know and trust.

## **Q.465. On Torrent’s strength.**

## **Q.466. Does Mewtwo sleep?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Pokemon Biology*

Mewtwo doesn’t sleep. Biologically he needs it, but he has enough control over his body to refresh himself constantly.

To be fair, Mewtwo probably needs to sleep. It would probably help him process through all his subconscious baggage...that does make me wonder what horrible things would happen if Mewtwo had a nightmare though. \[see question 279\]

## **Q.467. I want to ask about what Team Rocket is and how did it start? Was it inherited by family or by the Alpha there?**

- ## *Tags: First Rocket War, Giovanni, Madame Boss, Team Rocket, Western Continent*

So, none of this is set in stone but this is the premise I’m currently working with. 

Team Rocket is a direct result of the decline of Giovanni’s family. They were historically very powerful nobles, and retained a great deal of wealth and prestige to the modern day, but as they witnessed their power slipping his grandfather sought to rebuild new influence and exploit the new world built over the last few centuries. He built a powerful trading company that imported and exported to and from the Western Continent (whose seas had only recently made travel possible) and quickly increased the family’s wealth and position. 

Over time he began to dip into shadier areas of revenue \- poaching, smuggling, etc. Those activities required enforcement, and built the foundation of Team Rocket. 

Madame Boss (Giovanni’s mother) inherited the empire. As tension between East and West grew, their businesses bled money. She compensated by doubling down on the proto-Team Rocket, slowly taking control of the Kanto underground inch by inch. 

About 13 years ago, Giovanni killed her and took the reins. He was a bit more ambitious and we saw how that turned out.

## **Q.468. That was the First Rocket war? \[see question 467\]**

- ## *Tags: First Rocket War, Giovanni, League, Team Rocket*

Yep\! It had started a few years before as the League began to crack down on the Rockets, but Giovanni is the one who ramped it up to the next level.

## **Q.471. Was the League back then aware of Giovanni involvement? \[see question 467\]**

- ## *Tags: Giovanni, League, Team Rocket, Viridian City*

And nope, the League was never aware of Giovanni’s involvement. He kept his position by ruthlessly cracking down on Team Rocket and keeping Viridian the safest city in Kanto. 

The League was constantly kept occupied in other territories, and whenever they were about to look at the details of Viridian there always seemed to be something else that happened to keep them busy. Interesting coincidence, that.

Giovanni was definitely careful to make sure that the League was incredibly grateful for him being hyper competent. There was so much going on elsewhere that they were desperate for any but of stability in the territories.

## **Q.478. What do you think will be the first case of human intervention and experimentation on Pokémon?**

- ## *Tags: Last War, League, Pokemon Biology, Team Rocket, Unova*

There’s actually been quite a bit of experimentation on Pokémon already \- the League avoids harmful experimentation, but organizations like Team Rocket and pre-Last War Unova’s government are more than happy to experiment with chemicals and combat enhancers. I kind of imagine that’s where the root research of the X items came from. 

There is plenty of harmless experimentation that goes on too. The League works with scientists to develop treatments for genetic issues that afflict pokemon, for example.

And that’s just a few as examples \- just the first to come to mind for me.

## **Q.481. On how a normal Pokemon can become as powerful as a Legendary.**

- ## *Tags: Articuno, Elemental Spheres, Jirachi, Ho-Oh, Legendary Beasts, Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon, Moltres, Zapdos*


Not going to touch on Jirachi, but I will say that the only way for a mortal Pokémon to compare to a Legend is to be uplifted by a Legend \- Ho-Oh investing a huge amount of its essence into the Beasts is the best example for now \- or to master something like one of the Elemental Spheres, which are essentially another Moltres/Articuno/Zapdos in another form. That’s...extremely impossible for about 99.99% of humans and Pokémon though. The unprepared mind would be obliterated.

## **Q.482. Can the legends... be killed?**

I will say that if you somehow managed to destroy a Legend, it would basically instantly reform. They’re parts of the universe. Constant. 

And yep\! Moltres survived \[after its battle against Mewtwo\]. It would have burned its way out of the ocean eventually, but it was dragged back up before that became a necessity.

## **Q.490. Could you expand a little bit more on the role of the League President?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Charles Goodshow, Ever Grande, Indigo, Lily of the Valley, League, National League*


Charles Goodshow is the current National League President. This is largely a symbolic role, but does offer the President a role in dealing with foreign nations and treaties, although all of these have to be approved by the Champions of the Indigo, Ever Grande, and Lily of the Valley Leagues.

The primary role of the League President is to act as a figurehead for dealing with foreign nations and, more importantly, mediate between the member Leagues and promote strong cooperation and bonds between the different regions.

## **Q.491. What are the foreign nations?**

- ## *Tags: Alola, Galar, Kalos, Ranger Union, Unova*


Unova, Kalos, Alola, Galar, etc. The Ranger Union.

## **Q.492. On the Ranger Union.**

Sinnoh pulled back, largely abandoning the Ranger Union in order to consolidate its strength, and as a result the Ranger Union became its own entity.

## **Q.496. Previous year challengers can come back, from what I remember?**

## **Q.497. What happens to most conference champions?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Champion, Elite Four, League, SPECTRE Corps*


Most Conference Champions lose the Elite Four challenge (badly) and are offered into the ACE program or Elite Four trainee program. Generally the League recruits from the Top 64 for ACE. 

A lot of Conference Champions accept a job offer from the League, although not all choose the ACE program.

ACE are largely drawn from the Top 16, but the League actively looks at candidates from the Top 64 just to be sure there isn’t a competent trainer who fell through the cracks.

If it’s a valuable specialist like a ghost specialist, then they don’t need to be as strong to be recruited. The SPECTRE Corps are a valuable commodity and always need more members.

## **Q.498. Karen is another Conference Champion, right?**

- ## *Tags: Karen, Champion, Conference*


Yes, Karen was a Conference Champion\! 

## **Q.499. Like full exhibition matches \- do the Elite Four have full access to (presumably the Conference battlefields, as they're the most protected?) if they want to grapple with each other?**

- ## *Tags: Elite Four, Conference, Pokemon Battle*


Yep, and I can see an Elite Four exhibition match in a Conference grabbing a lot of attention. Most people never get a chance to see that level of battling. 

## **Q.500. On Blaine’s current strength.**

- ## *Tags: Blaine, Elite Four, Last War, Pokemon Battle, Sabrina*


Yep, Blaine has definitely fallen from his former heights. Several members of his team received major injuries in the war that led to lower life expectancy. 

He also made training a lower priority when he stepped down as an Elite Four member to more heavily focus on science and spearhead the development and refinement of cloning. 

The last main reason for his current level is that Blaine and several members of his team suffered horribly in the war. Fighting can be hard for them, even if Blaine refuses to show it. 

But honestly, if I was writing him at this point I’d have made him slightly more powerful. At least as dangerous as Sabrina. One of the problems with early Traveler is that I hadn’t quite figured out where everything should fall strength wise.

## **Q.501. Is there a traveler reason for why ghost types can't hit normal types and vice versa?**

- ## *Tags: Ghost type, Normal type, Pokemon Battle*


I’m still tinkering with my explanation for normal-types not being affected by ghost techniques, so I’ll pass on that for now. Ghost-types are able to ignore many physical attacks because they tend to have some control over their bodies that lets them twist or even dematerialize for a brief amount of time. Elemental attacks tend to be better because there’s something ‘extra’ that can linger or act as a sustained attack that ghosts can’t just phase through. 

## **Q.502. What are the mechanics behind odor sleuth and Foresight?**

- ## *Tags: Foresight, Ghost type, Normal type, Odor Sleuth, Pokemon Battle*


Odor Sleuth I imagine is that Pokémon try to track a target’s scent. It doesn’t let them attack ghosts with normal-type or physical attacks, but it does let them keep an eye on them and know where they’re coming from so they can time attacks better to get past the ghost’s defenses. 

Foresight is something similar, but focusing on sight instead.

## **Q.503. Does physical attacks also extend to stuff like Stone Edge for example, where they just phase through the physical material the move is composed of?**

- ## *Tags: Ghost type, Pokemon Battle, Stone Edge*


Yep\! I’ve basically extended the weakness to all physical attacks. Stone Edge would be much harder to phase through if it was more of a stream. Fire is effective against ghosts because it’s more of a continuous stream in a lot of cases, and will still heat the air to a point where it can damage the ghost when it rematerializes. 

## **Q.504. So would SPECTRE have normal type specialists as well?**

- ## *Tags: Distortion, Normal type, Pokemon Trainer, SPECTRE Corps*


Nope\! SPECTRE is basically purely focused on Distortion.

## **Q.505. Do fire types have latent psychic abilities?**

- ## *Tags: Electric type, Fire type, Psychic type*


Yep\! That’s how Pokémon are able to guide their flames to some degree, but most have little skill with it beyond the basics, and a lot of them use their latent abilities to help ignite the spark as well. 

Another example of psychic abilities being used to accentuate an elemental Pokémon is in electric-types. 

On its own, the electric-type moves we see are really, really impossible even in the world of Pokémon. The amount of energy for a tiny Spark would be through the roof \- air is a very, very poor conductor of electricity. 

My solution isn’t perfect and I’d welcome the input of someone more familiar with physics who could help me make it more accurate, but it tries to address this. Many electric-types have developed specialized psychic abilities that allow them to make the whole process a tad more efficient. 

Basically, when electric-types fire off an attack, their psychic abilities will create an area of localized negative charge at where they want to strike. When they generate their own electricity, it is guided to the negative zone. 

Like I said, I’m not the best when it comes to physics so I would welcome anyone else’s advice\! I try to keep things as reasonably accurate as I can, and I know that physics is one of my weaknesses. 

## **Q.506. Do you think it's possible to train against confuse ray, by repeated exposure?**

- ## *Tags: Confuse Ray, Dark type, Distortion, Master Trainer*


As for Confuse Ray, I don’t think you can develop a resistance to it. There are techniques that will allow a Pokémon to have a resistance to it \- such as flooding their body with Distortion to basically make them a temporary dark-type \- but the Confuse Ray we see from specialists and Masters is just too potent to naturally develop a resistance to.

## **Q.507. On what classifies as a Pseudo Legendary.**

- ## *Tags: Clefable, King Under the Mountain, Pseudo Legendary*


Basically what I call pseudo-Legendary in Traveler is these monstrous Pokémon that are essentially demigods. The King, Clefable, etc. Just a fun twist of the normal term for me haha. \[see question 91\] \[see question 227\]

## **Q.508. On the strength of Pokemon being trained in the present in comparison to those trained in the past.**

- ## *Tags: Gym Leader, Taimu, Technology*


Yep\! Especially when the power level of Pokémon tended lower. Even the strongest trained Pokémon of Taimu’s day would barely scratch Gym Leader now with access to more advanced training, nutrition, TMs, etc.

## **Q.509. On Pierce's strength.**

- ## *Tags: Gym Leader, Metagross, Pierce*


Pierce is a bit unique in that he’s not so much strong as he is dangerous. His team doesn’t hesitate to kill which is a massive advantage in his favor, particularly with Metagross. Metagross is stronger than the rest of his team by a wide margin (I guess that quality runs in the family) and is a massive force amplifier that would let him take on most Gym Leaders evenly. 

## **Q.510. On Ash’s view on death.**

- ## *Tags: Ash*


Yep\! I think even now Ash would choose to accept death and not fight it, although he might be tempted if it meant he could stay with his team. He’s been in so many dangerous situations that he’s sort of internalized the prospect of his own death. He’s a bit numb to the idea, even if he doesn’t want to die. Desensitized. 

But dealing with other people dying? That’s a whole different story. 

## **Q.511. How much does the Metagross colony share its stored knowledge? Does the League consult them? Especially now with the Legendaries events happening?**

- ## *Tags: Metagross, League, Team Rocket, Volumo Empire*


Fairly often. Nothing earth shattering, but very basic information about the fall of the Volumo empire and what caused it has been gathered, and they also provide tracking of nearby Pokémon and inform the League of Rocket activity. That’s about it, though. The colony is close to the Stone family, but that only barely applies to the League.

## **Q.512. How do other trainers sort that out \[exceeding the amount of Pokemon a Trainer can carry\]?**

- ## *Tags: League, Professor Oak, Pokemon Trainer*


There are both private and League facilities that care for Pokémon you aren’t able to have on you. The Corral is technically one of those facilities, although Oak restricts access to those he personally knows or trusts.

But yeah, most trainers just don’t catch that many Pokémon. Even a full team is almost impossible for the average trainer to manage and care for.

## **Q.513. How much did it cost to make Mewtwo? Like, could they have theoretically made an army of them (not that they would serve them but)? Also, could other Legends be cloned like Mew was, or would that be impossible due to lack of DNA?**

- ## *Tags: Giovanni, Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Team Rocket*


Yep, I view the cost for the Mewtwo in the billions. Team Rocket was a very, very rich and powerful organization and Giovanni spared no expense. \[Redacted\] is correct in saying that Giovanni viewed Mewtwo as his magnum opus. His masterwork that would secure his position at the top of the world, ushering in his age. 

I don’t believe an army of Mewtwo would have ever been possible. I think Mewtwo’s success at all was a complete accident, a twist of fate. They attempted dozens of Mewtwo, and most burned themselves out early in the process. There are complications in trying to clone a Legend.

## **Q.516. How come Ash got his pokemon so strong in his rookie year?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Legendary Pokemon, Pokemon Trainer, Professor Oak, St. Anne*


Yep, Ash is the combination of the perfect circumstances, basically. 

On his own he started out with a love of Pokémon, training, and a love of combat. His mom and Professor Oak helped make sure he had a lot of raw knowledge starting out, so he began on a strong foot. A very hard worker with a knack for battling and who loved building strong bonds with his team. 

Then comes the St. Anne. Ash is alone, traumatized, and his team and training become his entire life. Ultimate dedication, honestly to the point of being unhealthy. He’s still in that phase for the most part. 

And one of the biggest factors is his teachers, of course. Ash got lucky with his connections and the opportunities he’s been provided, but he only keeps receiving these opportunities because he works his ass off and everyone who meets him knows it. He’d be reaching the same milestones eventually, but this has definitely sped his development up by several months. 

And last, the Legendaries. They don’t give his team a power boost, but they do provide inspiration for Ash and act as yet another motivator. Ash is going to be using them as inspiration to reach new heights.

Sorry that this is pretty unrelated at this point, I kind of just wanted to have it out there\!

Someone said above that they’re investigators first and fighters second, and that’s a great way to look at it. Most of the muscle tends to come from whatever League they’re working with.

## **Q.522. On the strength of Mewtwo, Mew and Lugia.**

- ## *Tags: Ho-Oh, Legendary Beasts, Ghost of Lavender, Legendary Birds, Lugia, Mew, Mewtwo, Unown*

## **Q.523. What makes one Concept more or less powerful than another?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Kyogre, Lugia, Tao Trio*


A big part of the Concepts and how they manifest is related to their effect on the physical world, although there are exceptions\! 

Look at Kyogre and Lugia. Kyogre is Sea/Ocean. Lugia is the Guardian of the Sea, but also represents aspects such as hurricanes, ocean storms, and also the effect of the moon on the planet in Traveler. 

Lugia has incredible physical and psychic power, but overall it’s nothing compared the simple enormity and physical power of the ocean itself. 

That’s one way to look at it. There also Concepts that can be incredibly powerful, but don’t tend to act physically. The Tao Trio, for example. Massive Concepts, but they tend to act through intermediaries or empower others rather than acting directly themselves, which limits them.

And I imagine Johto as having much more territory than Kanto, but it’s far more rugged and wild, especially in the north. \[see question 214\]

## **Q.530. Does the calming effect \[produced by Suicune\] affect Raikou and Entei?**

Raikou inspires feelings of creativity, revolution, a desire for change. The spark to set great things in motion, or the impetus to make even a small change in your own life. 

Entei is perhaps the most similar to its corresponding Bird. It is power, fortitude, the resolve to carry out this inspiration and not let it go to waste. The courage to embrace something new and burn down the old.

Suicune was definitely the best one to meet Ash at this point. There’s a reason the others didn’t tag along.

## **Q.537. How common is it for carry limits to be removed from non League trainers?**

- ## *Tags: League, Pokemon Trainer*


Not especially common. The average trainer really struggles to maintain even a full team of six \- the limit is there to keep people from biting off more than they can chew. 

It’s not just the financial aspect either. It’s difficult to juggle so many different species with different needs, keeping team dynamics healthy, and balance radically different personalities and ambitions. That said, most skilled or experienced trainers will have at least some extra slots added once they pass licensing exams from the League or are trusted by the League.

## **Q.544. Would you judge your version of legendaries to be similar to Fractals? All of them have an associated infinity, and they are definitely infinite. However they occupy a finite space. A 3D fractal has an infinite area, but the volume is still finite. The difference in the powers of legends to me just indicates a different iteration method, or a different starting volume. After all, Mew and Mewtwo both occupy a similar infinity, but Mewtwo has the benefit of a larger volume. Both have an infinite area, but one is indeed larger than the other. I suppose this makes the volume, whatever the concept itself is, such as the amount of water on the planet for Kyogre. Though if that is the case, Dialga and Palkia may have an infinite volume as the universe may be infinitely big, making them a 4D fractal in this analogy. It falls apart a little, but would you say this encompasses any of your views for legends in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Dialga, Kyogre, Legendary Pokemon, Meta, Mew, Mewtwo, Palkia*


I’d say yes. To be honest, some of that goes above my head but I get the gist of it\! 

Basically, the way I’ve been thinking about it is also in term of infinities, although it’s a more general surface concept for me than one based in math. Similar idea though, in which all Legendaries are infinite but some infinities are bigger than others, or in that some of these Legends are able to output/access more of the infinity at once if that makes sense.

## **Q.547. How long have the Conferences(Particularly Indigo/Silver) been around for? Has the prospect of getting the chance to challenge the Elite Four if you win always been around?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Conference, Elite Four, Gym Leader, Indigo, Kanto, League, Lords of Kanto, Secession of 827, Silver Conference, Taimu*


Indigo and Silver Conferences have been around for a few hundred years, evolving out of regional championships designed to hunt out the strongest fighters. There have been several different methods of choosing Champions, and eventually it was decided to essentially be a tournament based on qualified individuals \- back then, the people who would have been involved were generally powerful nobles or clansmen (aka people who could afford to support several pokemon). The current system evolved from that set up. 

Yes, generally the Conference was used to hunt out worthy challengers and the winner would be given a chance to reach the highest echelons of the League if they were strong enough.

The Conference and badge system is designed to have trainers follow in Taimu’s paths \- it would have been shown in Champion how he unified Kanto by gaining the approval and respect of the Lords. 

Something I didn’t get to go into as much detail as I’d like in Chapter 54 with the Secession of 827 is that it was how the Gym Leader system arose \- it was the end of the Lords, many of whom were adapted into Leaders afterward as the nobility system was shattered by the Champion of the time.

## **Q.548. On the difference between a Lord and a Gym Leader. \[see question 547\]**

Yep, kind of a consolation prize with the stipulation that it (usually) wouldn’t pass on to their descendants.

## **Q.549. Was Cinnabar always part of the Indigo League since Taimu?**

- ## *Tags: Altomare, Cinnabar Island, Hoenn, Kanto, Taimu*

## **Q.550. How strong was Taimu’s team when he was alive? How would he compare to current champion / e4?**

- ## *Tags: Blackthorn City, Chinatsu, Dragonite, Drake, Elite Four, Gym Leader, Mamoru, Moltres, Pokemon Battle, Shinobu, Taimu, Technology, TM*


Taimu was a monster for his time. Mamoru was always a giant with immense physical strength and durability. Chinatsu was nowhere near as powerful, but she was still vicious, brilliant, and blessed by Fire. Shinobu was a force to be reckoned with, a physical powerhouse with a ton of speed. They were essentially unmatched in their era. 

Right now, they would be counted as low Gym Leader-level. 

Between TMs, techniques, nutrition, medicine, training resources, and pokeballs, trainers now are exponentially more powerful than they were in the past. In Taimu’s day it was rare for a trainer to have more than one or two Pokémon \- Taimu was one of the few who could hope to control three strong-willed Pokémon. Plus, like \[redacted\] said, you had to be much more cautious. A battle between equals could easily end with both dead. Modern medicine makes the extreme battle’s we see in Traveler much more sustainable. 

It actually was just the Drake of Blackthorn and his Dragonite against Taimu \- flight and maneuverability are a massive advantage, and I think it shows how monstrous the Drake was in battle. Absolute top-tier.

Yep, the Ryuujin was the Cerulean Champion and son of the Cerulean Lord.

The Ryuujin was very limited in where he could go. He could cover enough ground that most of the territory was protected, however, and was essentially unbeatable in water. 

Quite a rise for a young boy who made friends with a Magikarp.

## **Q.557. What was the kill count of the birds?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Birds*


I mean, over their lifetime they’ve wiped out millions of living things each, easily. That’s an incredibly tiny estimation. They’re old. Pokémon are hardy enough to run or survive brief exposures, but even the Fractured Birds are enough to obliterate everything for miles upon miles around even when holding back. 

They roamed wherever they wanted, whenever they wanted, leaving scars of charred earth, glass, and frostbite behind them. When humans built cities and kingdoms in the old days, they would last for perhaps a century or two before a Bird’s path crossed theirs and sent them right back to the Stone Age. Humanity reached the Bronze Age equivalent dozens of times across the world, and it would always be sent crashing down.  
Really is impossible to say \- back in the day they were all so deadly and careless that they had similar kill counts.

## **Q.560. How did the psychics do that? To create a constant in the unpredictable universe with conceptual creatures such as the legends? \[see question 556\]**

- ## *Tags: Chosen One Prophecy, Legendary Birds*

Psychics are uniquely sensitive and in turn with the universe, including Time and Space. A Legendary could create a prophecy/constant as well, but few would ever care to. It’s a permanent loss. The psychics who unmade themselves gave everything they had to almost bring a new Concept to life, in a way: the Prophecy.

## **Q.565. On entertainment in Traveler-verse.**

- ## *Tags: Meta*


Oh yeah of course. Tons of books, shows, movies, and games. Gaming in general is probably a little less developed than in our world despite more advanced technology, but not too far behind. Just less diversity I think.

## **Q.567. We know that 1000 psychic’s gave up their life/bodies to create the great prophecy, but what exactly did it do? Did it ensure Ash would make it till shalmunti, or did it just allow him to be born, and if the second, what would have happened if he died earlier in his journey? Would the prophecy make sure a chosen one was always available to save the world, or was it all resting on Ash living, or was Ash’s luck influenced by the prophecy? And if that, did it ensure he was strong enough to have a chance at completion by having him get as strong as he did, or was that just circumstance?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Chosen One Prophecy, Shamouti Island*


So basically, the psychics has no effect on Ash’s journey overall. What they did when they unmade themselves was create the Concept of the Prophecy/Chosen One. 

Think of the Chosen One as a role or slot to fill \- what the psychics did was ensure that someone with the potential to fulfill it would be present. There are a few different people or Pokémon at this point in time who could’ve accomplished it, or at least had the potential to. The prophecy didn’t guarantee success, it just stacked the odds a bit\!

## **Q.568. Who else is in that list? \[see question 567\]**

- ## *Tags: Cynthia, Lance, Legendary Beasts*


A bit too into spoiler territory, but I’ll offer a few: 

Lance had the potential, but ironically his connection to Moltres ruined him. 

Cynthia would have been a good option. 

The Beasts could have been dispatched to do the job. 

There’s a few Legendary Champions we haven’t met that could have been involved, and overall probably \~100-200 entities worldwide that could do it, but weren’t in the position to do so.

## **Q.569. Are the cornerstones of Masters considered base Champion level?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Master Trainer*


On average, I’d say yes\! It’s not an absolute rule though.

## **Q.570. On how painful evolutions are.**

- ## *Tags: Evolution, Nidoking, Nidoran, Nidorino*


I will say most evolutions aren’t that painful. Uncomfortable and mildly painful more than anything, except when major changes occur. Nidoran to Nidorino wasn’t especially painful, but it was a lot worse going from Nidorino to Nidoking because of how much his body changed if that makes sense.

## **Q.571. If Alakazam can make psychic swords can it project other weapon shapes?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Psyblade, Psychic type*


Yeah, psychic energy can be shaped however the psychic chooses. It does take extra effort for actual shapes \- in most cases it’s most effective to shoot a beam or just grip with psychic power. 

Alakazam’s Psyblade was more of just forming a cutting edge, which is really useful against soft opponents.

## **Q.572. Is she \[Oz\] 6ft like Infernus?**

- ## *Tags: Electivire, Evolution, Infernus, Oz, Pokemon Biology*


I’d say she’s a few inches over six feet. Electivire always struck me as having a ton of physical bulk. She’d be larger if she’d waited a bit longer, but she’ll grow into it.

## **Q.573. How did humans survive in Travelers' early world, given how delicate they are compared to pokemon?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Pokemon Behaviour, Psychic type, Wild Pokemon*


In the earliest days, it was often a result of partnering with local wild Pokémon, facilitated by psychic abilities and Aura users. Certain psychics were curious about humanity and taught gifted humans how to access their psychic powers, offering them a valuable tool for communicating with Pokémon and defending themselves.

## **Q.574. If A water type pokemon gets Moltres’ feather then will it go through some sort of mutation?**

- ## *Tags: Moltres, Feather, Pokemon Biology, Water type*


I think the water type would really struggle with Moltres’ Feather, perhaps even being entirely incompatible and causing it to damage the Pokémon.

- ## *Tags: Feather, Gyarados*


Majorly on the Pokémon itself \- I think some water-types would have the right temperament and force of will to adapt to it instead of being slowly destroyed. Gyarados would probably do quite well with the Feather.

## **Q.576. Is this statement \[an Alakazam being able to lift several hundred pounds\] still accurate with regards to power levels?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Psychic type*


Ah, yes that’s still accurate then. Several hundred pounds isn’t that much for an Alakazam, but it does take some focus and effort.

## **Q.577. So no regular animals?**

- ## *Tags: Meta, Pokemon Biology, Wild Pokemon*


Yeah, normal animals never evolved to a point where we’d recognize them as fish, reptiles, mammals, etc. Bacteria and very basic organisms evolved, but were constantly disrupted. Pokémon and humans are the only complex life to really exist. 

People still eat meat. The League took the bodies of dead Pokémon and basically used them as templates many decades ago as the base for the vast synthetic meat plants that feed the human world (and plenty of wild Pokémon in core regions). 

This had a major positive effect on the League’s relationship with the wild Pokémon populations and made the world we see in Traveler possible.

## **Q.578. How much does the average high level trainer/coordinator make? What about the Wandering masters? And how does this money compare to other jobs?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Coordinator, League, Master Trainer, Nomad, Pokemon Trainer*


The average high level trainer is pretty easily making 100-200k \- the best can hit up into the millions through sponsorship deals, but most get snatched up by the League before that point. They’re a valuable commodity, and that’s if they aren’t popular competition battlers racking up show fees and contracts. High level ACE make a similar amount, probably hitting a ceiling of 300k. The League loves to keep its trainers happy, though, and is meritocratic enough to institute performance based bonuses. 

Top Coordinators probably make a ton as well. Very easy to turn that into sponsorships and shows since coordinating is so personality based. There’s a lot of celebrity in it. 

Wandering Masters basically make as much as they want to. If they do deign to take the occasional job to let them resupply then they can basically charge whatever they want. They see little interest in wealth, for the most part, and most will just work long enough to get what they need.

## **Q.579. If the trainer has joined the League, does he still have the option to commit to sponsorship deals side by side?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, League, Ranger*


And it depends \- ACE or Rangers? Probably not. Somebody who is more of just on retainer would be fine though.

Basically as long as it doesn’t have an effect on security \- although psychics would sniff that out quickly.

## **Q.580. How high would the tax brackets gotta be for such high incomes?**

- ## *Tags: Crime, League*


Not too high. I figure the League largely taxes industry and makes their money off skimming from trainer bets, tournaments, entertainment, etc. Plus whatever they seize from criminal organizations. Not something I’ve fleshed out too much lol.

## **Q.581. The God-King existed some time before Taimu, right?**

## **Q.582. On Sinnoh after the God-King’s era.**

- ## *Tags: God-King, Mt. Coronet, Sinnoh*


The west \[side of Sinnoh\] was a bit more peaceful than the east. It had Mt. Coronet separating it from most of the warlike powers, and they primarily were either drawn into war through alliances or minor border squabbles and raids on their neighbors.

## **Q.583.On Lugia and Ho-Oh’s current strength. \[see question 522\]**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Ho-Oh, Legendary Beasts, Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon, Lugia*


Just caught up\! Wanted to clarify that Lugia and Ho-Oh are both on an equal of level of power at this point. A major reason for Ho-Oh guiding the Beasts through apotheosis instead of just resurrecting them was to restore the balance between it and Lugia. 

To understand why these different actions cost the same power, you have to break them down. 

Lugia split the Birds into three. Unnatural and against their nature, and so long as they’re split it will always be diminished as well. It’s an act of destruction. 

Ho-Oh forged three mortal Pokémon into Concepts in their own right. It’s an act of creation. Like the Birds being split, the apotheosis was going against the mortal nature of the original Beasts. 

In general, creation requires more than destruction. Both unnatural acts in this case, but it took more effort to uplift the Beasts from mortal to sort-of-Legends than it did to split the Birds.

## **Q.584. Lugia split the birds so long ago, why would restoring the balance be such a major reason now? \[see question 583\]**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Lugia, Ho-Oh*


Yeah, have to think of the timescales involved \- for timeless entities, a few thousand years is just the blink of an eye. It was something to be corrected, certainly, and ate at them both as long as it wasn’t, but from their perspective Ho-Oh got right on it.

I have no current plans for mystery dungeons haha.
