## **Q.587. Does Vaporeon have the ability to liquefy itself within Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Chinatsu, Pokemon Biology, Vaporeon*


I don’t have Vaporeon as able to physically turn into water. Not most of them, anyways. You could see an extremely skilled or pseudo-Legendary Vaporeon pulling that off (similar to Chinatsu with her flames) but most Vaporeon are basically just so good at camouflaging that they’re basically indistinguishable from it while submerged.

## **Q.588. On whether Acid Armor liquifies Vaporeon and Grimer/Muk though.**

- ## *Tags: Acid Armor, Grimer, Muk, Pokemon Biology, Vaporeon*


My POV is that Muk and Grimer are basically liquid already. Vaporeon is too...solid for me to imagine it completely decondensing. Too much structure.

## **Q.589. What's the difference between the Pokémon used in such armies from Guardians?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Guardian, Mamoru, Pewter City, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Behaviour, Ryuujin*


In general, I don’t have an over abundance of Pokémon in ancient warfare. The average soldier wouldn’t have the support of a Pokémon, or perhaps one set to cover for a small group. Just a handful with partners, since especially at that point it was both incredibly difficult to support large Pokémon and most Pokémon wouldn’t have been trained for combat like they are now. You still see partner Pokémon all over the place, just not as many specialized for combat since it was so much more dangerous without modern medicine. Pokémon are ridiculously hardy and tough, but fighting an equal is a good way to come away with a permanent injury. Like animals, they primarily postured against one another. Pokémon partners to average soldiers were mostly just there to provide logistical support more than anything. 

Humans and Pokémon that desired to fight together became Guardians. They specialized in combat. The backbone of an army will always be the footsoldiers when it comes to occupying enemy territory and actually claiming new land and holding positions, but the Guardians were the spearhead \- force amplifiers that could penetrate enemy lines and open up holes for the army to punch through. Just imagine young Mamoru against a bunch of humans armed with spears and bows (or perhaps a weak psychic). He’d be completely unstoppable even without his stone manipulation. 

I imagine each territory to easily maintain hundreds of Guardians (by different names in each territory), with the largest cities pushing over a thousand. With each having one or two Pokémon partners, they could theoretically field thousands of well trained Pokémon in a battle, but that would be a bit of a waste \- for the most part, with the exceptions of certain Guardians like the Ryuujin or the Pewter Champion \- they’re more valuable harassing enemies and chipping away at their strength than just throwing down in pitched battle.

## **Q.600. It's often mentioned in the story that Pokémon, although willing to hurt and scare away humans, won't intentionally kill them (barring exceptions).**

## **Is that a recent development? Or was it the same throughout history?**

- ## *Tags: Indigo, League, Pokemon Behaviour, Technology, Wild Pokemon*


Yep, the world was a pretty hostile place before the rise of the Indigo League (and even up until the last two centuries or so, really). There were certainly friendly Pokémon, but it was much less common before technology and training advanced and psychics became more commonplace.

It doesn’t hurt that wild Pokémon and humanity were both happy to unite to drive out Pokémon that just loved killing.

## **Q.601. Were livestock a thing?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Berry, Wild Pokemon*


Livestock weren’t really a thing. You’d have groups of Pokémon that might live alongside people in a partnership, but you definitely wouldn’t find Pokémon being raised to slaughter \- they wouldn’t put up with that for a second, and it’s only recently humans would even have a chance of pulling it off. You’d see large groups of hunters going after some Pokémon if desperate, but it was very rare, honestly. Most Pokémon on their own could slaughter a dozen humans, and the ones that couldn’t are probably going to be in groups.

They might trade with Pokémon for dead prey occasionally, but there are lots of berries they could eat that have evolved to be massive sources of protein that they could reliably cultivate as well for most of their dietary needs.

## **Q.602. Hunting probably only really started being a logistically possible thing for them once they began to befriend groups of Pokemon like Growlithe/Arcanine.**

- ## *Tags: Arcanine, Growlithe, Wild Pokemon*


Yep, hunting would be possible but it still runs the risk of making the wild pokemon outright hostile, which makes life much more difficult.

Yep, absolutely. Not all, but there are plenty of crueler species like Sneasel who’d happily hunt a human, if only for the sport.

## **Q.608. would it be possible for Dazed to use a liquid as a foci if it was viscous enough? Are foci best when homogenous?**

- ## *Tags: Dazed, Psychic type*


 I don’t think the foci actually do anything themselves. I think of them purely as a mental tool to help psychics focus and retain clarity of thought \- something to center themselves around, I suppose. Theoretically, anything could be used as a foci. I think metal, crystal, and stone tend to be favored because they are difficult to damage, and the shine of metal and crystal catches the eye...plus, some psychics might just think it looks pretty. I imagine they get a massive personal attachment to their foci.

## **Q.609. Do we know anything about farming in the Traveler verse?**

- ## *Tags: Grass type, Ground type, Meta, Technology, Water type, Wild Pokemon*


What was the farming question again? 

For a general answer, farming is still very much an important part of the Pokémon world. I imagine it would be based primarily around cities and towns due to the danger a single angry wild Pokémon could pose. Better to have it in a fortified area. Less important these days but I can’t imagine too many have been created in the wilderness. Teleportation makes it possible logistically, but it’s easier to continue developing in the same area. 

I’m imagining less technology than in our world (although it’s still very heavily used) and a large reliance on Pokémon. Ground-types, grass-types, and water-types especially would be invaluable.

## **Q.610. On the existence of normal animals.**

- ## *Tags: Meta*


Yep, anything too complex would just be instantly outcompeted. You have bacteria, plants, fungi, protists, etc but normal animals just can’t survive in a world filled with Pokémon for the most part. I imagine some small insects exist, but it’s not something I’ll address in story.

Just ridiculously tough and strong even without taking into account elemental abilities.

## **Q.613. Does a Zoroark’s illusions show up on a digital camera, or does it just fool organic lifeforms?**

## **Q.614. Are there any rules in the league that regulate people using family members or other people's pokemon to just sweep through gym challenges or low level tournaments?**

- ## *Tags: League, Meta*


Yep. It’s handled pretty much on a case by case basis, but generally transferring a Pokémon over to a family member or friend (or anyone really) comes with some heavy stipulations on entering competitions. It’s pretty rare for the most part because most Pokémon wouldn’t agree with it, although there are exceptions.

And by that I mean it’s a totally different situation for a Pokémon to go off with a friend or family member of their trainer for protection or security purposes than “Oh, he needs to sweep this tournament real quick\!”

## **Q.628. Were they ever described in an order or something? \[see question 626\]**

- ## *Tags: Celadon City, Cerulean City, Cinnabar Island, Fuchsia City, Kanto, Lavender Town, Mamoru,  Pewter City, Saffron City, Taimu, Vermillion City, Viridian City*


I never described the order, although I do have a rough estimate of his \[Taimu’s\] journey in my head. 

Saffron, Celadon, Vermillion, Fuchsia, Cinnabar, Viridian, Pewter, and Cerulean last. Lavender was the last to officially join \- they intended to see the nascent League and Cerulean batter each other, then make large gains. 

They just didn’t expect Taimu doing so good of a job, and eventually they were forced to join for fear of the rest of Kanto banding against them. They remained relatively independent (similar to Ecruteak) but I imagine Mamoru has their symbol engraved as well, somewhat apart from the rest. 

Since I don’t believe I’ve described it yet, Lavender’s symbol is a black tower.

## **Q.629. Do the regions in Traveler have anything akin to WMDs or Nuclear Weapons?**

- ## *Tags: Master Trainer, Meta, Mewtwo, Technology, Wild Pokemon*


Sort of\! Like \[redacted\] said, the Pokémon world is capable of manufacturing powerful weapons able to affect pokemon. They’re primarily used for sieges \- pyrobombs, cryobombs, and similar technology. Loaded up into battleships and things like that. 

That said, they were on a similar level to the ordinance in WW2. Devastating and capable of massive damage, but not something like a nuke. 

Overall, weapons technology in the Traveler world is fairly primitive. One of the things where they have the capacity and technological ability to build horrifying instruments of war that could obliterate cities, but mostly stick with Pokémon. Firearms were never properly explored because primitive firearms tended to anger wild Pokémon with their loud noises (and weren’t reliable against Pokémon ). 

Honestly, if I imagine any WMD being developed in Traveler (other than Mewtwo, anyways) it would be some awful bioengineered plague or something like that. 

In practice, Master-level trainers are the Traveler setting’s WMD. Enormously flexible, capable of ripping through lesser trainers like nothing, and a single Master can completely change the tide of battle. They can be the tip of the spear or an impenetrable wall.

## **Q.630. Any \[weapon technologies\] that exists mostly are within the realm of supporting their Pokemon and keeping the trainer themselves safe right?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Team Plasma, Team Rocket, Technology*


Yep. There’s plenty of that. Most human weapons technology is built around supporting their Pokémon or buying the human some time to run away. Pokémon are just too tough and powerful to fight on even footing.

At least when humans are squishy like Traveler’s.

And even groups like Team Rocket and Plasma are all about augmenting Pokémon or making them more powerful through drugs, genetic engineering, etc.

Funny enough, humans as individual fighters might have been in a stronger position back in the old days when Aura was relatively well-known and usable psychic powers were much more common.

## **Q.631. How old is Nidoking or Torrent or Dazed?**

## **Q.636. Were Legends the only beings we can consider Gods?**

- ## *Tags: Ho-Oh, Legendary Pokemon, Lugia, Mew, Ninetales, Pseudo Legendary*


So there are a lot of layers of worship. It’s very regional and dependent on location. 

There’s a bit of a sliding scale. You have certain species revered by cultures and take on an almost sacred reputation, you have many long-lived pokemon such as Ninetales that acted as patrons and advisors to powerful human families (and often engaged in decades to centuries long political maneuvering against rival patron pokemon), and after that you get into what could truly be considered gods by the humans. 

Pseudo-Legendaries were often the subject of local worship, acting like regional gods or demigods (albeit very aloof on average). 

True Legendaries were often feared and worshipped in equal measure. There were plenty mankind had little experience (or at least not enough survivors to keep track of) with, but some like Mew, Lugia, and Ho-Oh that actively intervened with humanity quickly became common deities to follow. \[see question 315\]

## **Q.637. considering that the 1000 psychics sacrificing themselves made a constant. Could material sacrifices of significant value to the person doing it, have an effect on reality?**

## **If a person were to sacrifice another person could they have an effect on the world? Would one of them have to be psychic? Would it have to be the person conducting the sacrifice?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Chosen One Prophecy*


Mm, I’d say no to that. A big part of the Prophecy being shaped is that the thousand psychics went into it willingly and had the skill and knowledge to accomplish their goal. 

The way it worked is that when you Unmake yourself, you’re essentially sacrificing your Aura \- the sum of yourself \- towards a specific goal, like adding a drop of water in a bucket until it tips, or adding just a little bit of weight to the dice so it lands the way you want. 

In making this sacrifice, you must clearly understand your goal and be harmonious. Fear, resistance, indecision \- all emotional triggers that can lead to an impurity of purpose that makes your sacrifice meaningless. 

The Unmaking of a single individual is insignificant, even for minor things. It takes mass action (which is difficult with individuals as rare and powerful as psychics capable of performing the fear) to make a tiny change and there aren’t many reasons important enough for most psychics to risk that.

## **Q.638. Is Aron the oldest team member?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Aron, Oz*


Nope, I’d say that’s probably Oz. She’s got a good few years on the rest of the team.

## **Q.639. On the future growth of Ash’s team.**

- ## *Tags: Age, Ash*


They’re going to age at fine wine. I’d say most of Ash’s team is at 80-85% of what they would be if they were fully mature. Still incredibly powerful, but their skills and experience far outstrip their bodies. \[see question 351\]

- ## *Tags: Dark World, Indigo, Johto, Kanto, God-King, Rota, Ore Mountains*

## **Q.645. How strong is the average ACE squad member and how strong is the average commander?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Conference, Jessica, Master Trainer, Nomad*


Average ACE member is about equivalent to Top 16 in Conference. Think Jessica. Commanders tend to be around Top 4 to Finalist level, occasionally pushing into Master territory. 

They tend to stagnate a little in raw power once they hit ACE. Absolutely there’s improvement, but most of their focus becomes protocol, working on teamwork, and enhancing tactics and strategy. Turning them from fighters to soldiers \- an average ACE squad can fight evenly with the average lone Nomad, despite being outclassed in skill and strength.

## **Q.646. Do Agatha's Pokémon have names?**

- ## *Tags: Agatha*


She did not\! Due to her abilities they could communicate on a pretty deep level, so verbal names weren’t necessary for her. It was kind of like what we see with Pokémon perspectives where she’s mostly referring to them mentally by what they mean to her, or a string of words meant to embody their place.

## **Q.647. Is the Traveler Earth/World smaller than our own?**

- ## *Tags: Location, Meta, Southern Continent, Wild Pokemon*


Nope, it’s at least the same size. One thing to remember is that humans only inhabit a tiny fraction of the world. The vast majority is still solely the territory of wild Pokémon. 

The map I’ve posted is still missing vast tracts of the southern continent \- it’s kind of meant to show the limits of human exploration.

## **Q.648. But don’t they at least have satellites?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Rayquaza, Technology*


Yep, it’s very recent. Too many things that can mess with them \- one very large, green serpent in particular isn’t a fan. It’s not immediate, but it makes them expensive 

Enough to have limited functionality, and they do have a complete map of the world, but much of the southern portions are still a mystery in terms of Pokémon and detailed understanding. \[see question 48\]

## **Q.649.  Is pollution a large problem in Traveler, I understand that Muk and other Pokemon exist but would it cause global warming?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Muk, Pokemon Biology, Rayquaza, Technology, Wild Pokemon*


Humans haven’t caused any real changes such as global warming due to their smaller population and more efficient technology. There were some growing pains with the industrial revolution, but the hostile reactions of Pokémon to pollution forced a relatively quick transition to more efficient and less polluting sources of energy. 

That said, I don’t think Rayquaza would purify the atmosphere. It would just target the source of the imbalance and remove it.

I see it as not caring about slow, steady changes, or even relatively fast ones on the ecological scale (so hundreds of thousands to millions of years). It’s more the rapid spike that infuriates Rayquaza. Think the frog in the boiling water analogy.

## **Q.650. Do psychics and ghosts poop?**

- ## *Tags: Dazed, Ghost type, Pokemon Biology, Psychic type*


I can’t believe I’m answering this, but yes. Although Dazed subsists on dreams, it’s essentially used as a source of energy similar to how plants use light to drive the reactions of photosynthesis or certain bacteria are able to produce energy using chemicals. So it’s just a source of energy, but it’s used to drive chemical processes in her body. Which technically makes her an animal autotroph which is whole interesting thing on its own.

## **Q.651. So does this reaction produce no waste? Like, I don't specifically mean feces, it might be interesting if she emits vapor or something as a result of the reactions. \[see question 650\]**

- ## *Tags: Dazed, Hypno, Pokemon Biology*


No, she \[Dazed\] does still produce waste. Still gotta get waste products out of her body, and given her otherwise mammalian physiology a Hypno would already have systems built in for that instead of developing an entirely different strategy of waste removal.

## **Q.652. How did Champion Taimu and Drake Ryoto look?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Drake, Lance, Ryoto, Taimu*


Taimu has black hair and bright blue eyes, and that’s about as much description as I’ve given haha. I figure he generally wore indigo colored robes, although the white Champion’s mantle hadn’t been incorporated at that point. Relatively average height, although he was taller than most peasants due to a better diet. 

Drake Ryoto was a big guy, probably 6’ 3” or 6’ 4”. Huge, especially for the time period. Overall looked pretty similar to Lance \- dark pink or red hair and sharp features.

## **Q.655. It was already mentioned that steel was a rare commodity in the past of Traveler's universe, generally only obtained through extremely rare Steelix corpses or fallen meteors. ## **Q.657. Is Spiritomb mortal? Age-wise at least.**

- ## *Tags: Age, Aura, Pokemon Biology, Spiritomb*


Nope, Spiritomb cannot die naturally. They’re unique in that they’re physically bound to the Keystone. Most ghosts have their corporeal form constantly degrading, thus requiring Aura to be ingested in order to maintain it. Keystones are immune to that degradation, since Spiritomb are designed for longevity. Don’t want your unique super weapon dying\!

## **Q.660. Which region has the strongest elite four on average in your opinion?**

- ## *Tags: Aaron, Bertha, Drake, Elite Four, Ever Grande, Flint, Glacia, Karen, League, Lucian, Master Trainer, Phoebe, Sinnoh, Sidney, Will*


Going back to the earlier question, I’d say that Sinnoh currently has the strongest overall Elite Four. 

Indigo was a strong contender until recently due to the changing of the guard. Will and Karen especially still have a long way to go, even if they are true Masters. 

The Ever Grande Elite Four are in a similar boat. Sidney and Phoebe still have plenty of room to improve, but at least they still have powerhouses like Drake and Glacia. Drake is probably the single most powerful member of any Elite Four currently. 

The Sinnoh Elite Four are just the most solid overall, I think. Aaron’s still extremely young, but is basically a prodigy expected to be Champion one day. Bertha’s team is still largely in their prime. Flint’s a beast, and Lucian is extremely powerful. Just a really, really solid group overall and it isn’t suffering growing pains at the moment.

## **Q.672. What was the situation in Indigo around Taimu's time? Were there many big nations? Were there very notable ones that had great influence (discounting the Wataru)? Were all the Lords (now Gym Leaders) underneath Taimu and Ryoto Guardians/Leaders of their own tribe/nation, or were there some who simply were notable warriors of great renown?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Indigo, Lords of Kanto, Ryoto, Taimu, Wataru Clan*


In general, Indigo was divided up into city-states. Constantly shifting alliances, and lots of city-states would ally against a greater threat for one war and then prepare to go to war with their former ally. 

Pretty much every Lord was at least a Guardian. Very nice to have that power of your own, while the Champion existed to lead military matters. 

The Lords were largely kept under Taimu in order  to preserve a peaceful transition of power and maintain established infrastructure. Much less bloody, and with Taimu’s charisma cranked up to 10 (and his divine blessing) it left most Lords bending the knee without too much bitterness.

## **Q.673. How does the happiness evolution thing work in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Evolution, Pokemon Biology*


Happiness is basically normally an evolution that comes from a feeling of contentment and being accepted by a group in social Pokémon \- so once a Pokémon matures and has reached a place of esteem in the social hierarchy that’s usually when it will evolve. \[see question 118\] 

## **Q.674. Since Tangrowth grows forever, does that mean he is biologically immortal, will continually grow more powerful, or he just will always be able to regenerate lost limbs?**

- ## *Tags: Tangrowth, Pokemon Biology*


Tangrowth is essentially biologically immortal and will live pretty much up until something kills him.

Like was said up above, I think it really only helps survivability. Instead of being instantly killed when a Legend is nearby, you’ll only be instantly killed if the Legendary focuses on you.

Unown are fairly unique. Theoretically, if you had the right tools, power, and materials, you could create another Legendary. You can’t create or destroy an Unown.

## **Q.682. On what are the factors to be considered when teleporting.**

## **Q.691. What other minor gyms are there?**

- ## *Tags: Gym, League, Pokemon Trainer, Ranger, Wild Pokemon*


Minor Gyms are set up by the Leagues. There’s about 3 per each territory, generally staffed by veteran Gym Trainers for that territory who are looking to gain experience and eventually ascend to a higher role. Their purpose is generally to give the League ability to easily project force into less populated areas and protect towns away from the major cities. They basically act as law enforcement, manage wild Pokémon, support Ranger teams, etc.

## **Q.692. On Erika’s capabilities and deficiencies.**

- ## *Tags: Celadon City, Erika, Gym Leader, Legendary Pokemon*


I will say Erika would be capable of getting a city running. Is it her forte? Not really. But she’d be fantastic at the logistical side and organizing things. She’d be good at picking the people needed to do the groundwork while making things run relatively smoothly in the meantime 

That said, I think she’d have a much harder time in handling a city under crisis after a Legendary event, for example. She can optimize, she can manage, and she can grow a functioning city, but I think when there’s constant action required it would be extremely draining on her. 

With how big Celadon is, best case scenario would probably be to create co-Leader system. Let Erika specialize in management and day-to-day while having a second Gym Leader handling the enforcement and action side.

## **Q.693. How important is privacy for the general population, or the League, taking psychics into account? Like we know they are used for a vetting process of League members, but how much is the Pokemon allowed to probe, everything? Could a psychic be used during a census to preemptively attack criminals? Would the people be ok with that and accept it like we do when going through a metal detector?**

- ## *Tags: Crime, Dark type, Ghost type, Gym Leader, League, Lords of Kanto, Psychic type, Technology*


Honestly, psychic scans are pretty standard fare at this point. People are largely accustomed to it \- the wilds and cities are patrolled by psychics that maintain a surface level scan. Not enough to really read thoughts, but enough to pick up on issues. The metal detector analogy you have is a good one. It’s one of those things where in our world a psychic scan would be horribly intrusive \- in the Pokémon world they’re used to it. 

One reason ghost and dark specialists tend to have a bit of a bad reputation is because they’re frequently used by criminals to obscure that low-level surveillance. 

Deep scans tend to be reserved for more serious things like courts, gathering intelligence, interrogations, and interviewing for security clearance. 

Previously, Gym Leaders have had a certain prestige and unassailability for things like focused psychic scans. The position was established for Lords to switch over to \- maintain prestige and status while also breaking that authority from a single bloodline \- and a lot of that led to a tradition of Gym Leaders basically being above standard scans (assuming everything else checked out). That’s obviously off the table now lol.

Yeah there’ll be frequent scans, probably once every few months in the Indigo League.

## **Q.701. On the average strength of a Conference participant.**

- ## *Tags: Conference, League, Pokemon Trainer, Ranger*


Yep, the majority of Conference battlers will be veterans. Not many rookies are able to join, let alone make it past the first few rounds. Placing in the Conference is a good way to get attention, and that’s when lucrative opportunities from the League and private organizations start rolling in. 

Even a 4-5 badge trainer is a bit above average and can find good work for local government, companies, and working for the League as a Ranger or other worker. Once you get above that you’re going to be in a very, very good place.

## **Q.702. How replicable is a Metagross' strength? Say for example that Steven's Metagross goes to the colony, communicates to them all the things it does under Steven's command, what prevents the colony from "assembling" a Metagross with very close capabilities?**

- ## *Tags: Metagross, Metagross Colony, Steven, Stone Family, Technology, TM*


They do share experience, knowledge, etc. very fluidly\! Going forward, the Stone’s colony will be one of, if not the, most powerful colonies in the world. They’ll be able to utilize that knowledge and Steven’s Metagross’ experience and skills to train exceptional Metagross in defense of the colony. 

That said, any Metagross is still an immense investment of resources. Transmitting knowledge is extremely helpful and accelerates development, but it still falls on individual Metagross to learn how to execute it. They also require many TMs and other training aids to reach a similar level, which the Stones are more than happy to provide. There is a large difference between knowing and doing, and the level of raw force and control that Steven’s Metagross is able to combine to achieve its skills is pretty much legendary even among other Metagross.

## **Q.708. I can see Lance in that naming convention but where did Clair come from? \[see question 708\]**

- ## *Tags: Clair, Lance, Wataru Clan*


I’m just having it arranged by different families \- not everyone does it, and I had Clair’s mom named something different if I remember right. I wanted to show that her family didn’t have that particular tradition.

After some time as a trainer it’s possible to receive a certification allowing for more. It’s not common \- most people simply can’t manage a larger team \- but for those with the talent and trust of a League it’s an option.

Recollections Chapter 21 took place after they were sundered by Lugia, around the times the first true kingdoms and states had been properly established.

## **Q.714. So did Zapdos purposefully leave its feather behind \[for Tani\]?**

- ## *Tags: Feather, Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon, Tani, Zapdos*


Sort of. Zapdos scatters Feathers pretty frequently without care, but they almost always fizzle out before anything finds them (and most things that find them steer clear).

I think you could say Zapdos purposefully adjusted its course to fly over the humans, dropped a Feather, and flew off again.

## **Q.715. What is the political structure of Rota?**

- ## *Tags: Indigo, League, Rota, Tree of Beginning*


It’s one of the last kingdoms still extant in the modern age and is ruled by its queen. It’s a rather small nation but one with a long, long history. Rota was originally founded by worshippers of the Tree of Beginning, and its worship and symbolism remains a prominent staple of Rotan culture. It remained independent from the Leagues, although it has close ties to Indigo and acts as a sort of territory for it in practice \- they abide by League laws, support League members in the area, and in turn receive many benefits while retaining their de facto independence.

## **Q.716. Would Infernus ever learn Confuse Ray?**

- ## *Tags: Confuse Ray, Dark type, Gary, Infernus, Umbreon*


Yep, Infernus can use Confuse Ray although it’s not a ‘proper’ version like you’d see from a skilled dark-type or ghost like Gary’s Umbreon. That level of Confuse Ray \- essentially the OHKO, crippling version \- is extremely demanding.

Still the same technique in theory, but it’s more of a slap to the face than a ‘let me stick my metaphysical fist into your brain and squeeze’.

## **Q.717. On the difference between veteran Master level Trainers and newcomers.**

## **Q.725. On Plume’s strength.**

- ## *Tags: Hyper Beam, Plume, Pokemon Battle*


The thing with Plume is that she’s absolutely terrifying in a lot of ways. In the field she’s easily one of the most valuable members of the team. Regulated matches just don’t play to her strengths in the least \- confined spaces, limited area to fly and accelerate, etc. In the field, though, she’s essentially instant death. Too fast to see or hear coming, capable of sniping with Hyper Beams, and capable of disrupting enemy formations with techniques like Hurricane. She’d actually fare really, really well against most members of the team in a one-on-one. She just has terrible match ups for the most part. It’s something I hope to fix going forward.

## **Q.726. How would that affect their \[Nidoking and Nidoqueen’s\] evolution and sterilisation?**

- ## *Tags: Nidoking, Nidoqueen, Pokemon Biology*


\[Redacted\] is right, as of this moment I have Nidoking and Nidoqueen as sterile for the reasons he mentioned \[and it prevents bloodlines from taking over \- averting the issue of hereditary monarchy. By eliminating the ability for matriarchs and patriarchs to reproduce it enforces a system where the best of the herd is elevated rather than just the children of the matriarchs and patriarchs\]. Keep in mind that Nidoking would NOT naturally evolve at such a young age. In the wild he’d have had one or two decades easily to spread his genes before making the evolution to Nidoking.

## **Q.727. On why Dialga and Palkia’s name appear as a tetragram.**

- ## *Tags: Dialga, Creation Trio, Legendary Pokemon, Meta, Palkia*


That said, that’s just the real world I got inspiration from. There’s plenty of in-universe reasons for culturally avoiding the names. They’re incredibly sacred and given enormous gravitas.

## **Q.734. On Grey’s Scolipede.**

Grey’s whole team is disgustingly effective when they’re working together.

## **Q.735. On the people who are aware of Mega Evolution.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Draconids, Elite Four, Hoenn, Kalos, Last War, League, Lumiose, Mega Evolution, National League*


Yep, they existed in some form in Hoenn but it was a well kept secret by the Draconids. It’s much more common in Kalos and incorporated into many of their traditions. Many Mega Stones are prized possessions of the old aristocratic families. 

The National League received many Mega Stones from the Lumiose League after the Last War as part of their peace agreement and will also provide specific Mega Stones and training for foreign Elite Four members and Champions.

## **Q.740. On the Hashimoto.**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Confuse Ray, Curse, Dark type, Distortion, Hashimoto, Lavender Town, Lords of Kanto, Psychic type, Saffron City, Shadow Ball*


In the past, the Hashimoto were quite plentiful. Several dozen, generally. They perfected the “stuff a screaming newborn ghost into a screaming newborn human” technique a few centuries ago and had time to refine it. When the family was butchered in the war that began the end of the reign of Lords in Indigo, only a single family unit remained. Their potent knowledge of Distortion and hybrids made them prime candidates for buying Lavender time \- the Hashimoto were major parts of the defense in Saffron and the Lavender territory. 

The Hashimoto bid and retained their old manor (by virtue of nothing in the old town being able to burn), the last few surviving coming together to reclaim their home. 

The Hashimoto dwindled. Agatha’s grandfather was the only child born to the remaining few, and watched as his family faded away and lost their influence and power. As a result he grew desperate by the years before Agatha’s birth, and he steeped himself in the old ways, desperate to reclaim some last glory for the family. He knew it would leave Agatha sterile \- it was well-documented \- but he was too egotistical about his great work to care. He saw it as one last blaze of glory.

As for what Agatha gained from being a hybrid...well, it’s quite a bit. She has extremely high tolerance to most Distortion since she’s been steeped in it her whole life. It’s only direct attacks and concentrated Distortion that can threaten her, but the Distortion that exists in her is more firmly rooted than in most ghosts \- in practice, she’s closer to a dark-type than a ghost. 

She’s practically immune to psychics, and has an easy time shutting them down with minimal effort \- she likes to goad psychics into trying to read her mind. She gets along well with ghosts, since she’s essentially one of them. They tend to seek her out. 

She can also perform many, many Distortional techniques. Shadow Ball, for one, but she prefers subtle uses. She’s able to teleport short distances. Confuse Ray is available to her. She could use Curse, but it would kill her in this state. It’s a very, very flexible power.

## **Q.741. So is Mega \[Metagross\] stronger than the ancients, like Mamoru and the nidos and Clefable and the King?**

- ## *Tags: Chinatsu, Clefable, Ghost of Lavender, King Under the Mountain, Mamoru, Mega Evolution, Teleport*


Ehhhhh, I’d say it depends. Chinatsu makes power set would obliterate Metagross. Mamoru would have a rough time against Mega Metagross, and without evolving would be beaten. 

The King is probably a hard counter to Mega Metagross. Too heavy to lift even for Mega Metagross’ psychic power \- which is its major advantage against Mamoru \- and with such strong defenses that Metagross couldn’t pierce them. 

Clefable would probably just teleport away and get out of dodge, or pull some crazy stunts. Mega Metagross would just have a hard time pinning it down. 

The Ghost of Lavender would be a bad, bad match for Mega Metagross of course.

## **Q.765. On Battlus.**

## **Q.767. On nurture vs. nature.**

- ## *Tags: Charizard, Dragonite, Hyper Beam, Pokemon Battle, Raticate*


Eh, I’d say there’s room for a well-trained pokemon to take down anything. Some Pokémon have inherent potential or advantages, but training (especially when it comes to shooting Hyper Beams and elemental attacks that equalize the playing field) make things more fair.

Discipline and experience are massive factors.

But yeah, I do agree that in the wild it would be almost unheard of for a Raticate to take down a Dragonite or Charizard (at least without stealth or allies). It would definitely want to run first.

## **Q.769. In regards to Sidney vs Steven's Metagross, can Metagross prevent any dark type energy from reaching him?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Dark type, Distortion, Ghost type, Metagross, Miracle Eye, Pokemon Battle, Sidney, Steven, Zoroark*


Metagross is a beast. It and Steven have planned for fighting dark and ghost-types. That said, Sidney is a nightmare for it. Once Metagross is struck \- or even just numbed by Distortion saturating the field \- Zoroark’s illusions (which are fueled by Distortion) will take effect and even the battle. Generally it takes 2-3 members of the team to safely weaken Metagross (it can usually take one or two down with Miracle Eye and precision shots) for Zoroark to safely take it down. That’s absolutely crippling when you still have five Champion-levels to fight. Sidney is very, very well-suited to nullifying Steven’s biggest advantage though.

It's not worth it, especially since most Alakazam can easily just deal damage, teleport away, and then chip away at you for the next few days. They're impossible to beat in battles of attrition, so they were given a wide berth.

## **Q.785. Were Dusknoirs around too or were they so reclusive no one had one back in the day?**

- ## *Tags: Dusknoir, Pokemon Behaviour*


Dusknoir were around, but they usually functioned as guardians of places. Very unusual to see one loyal to a human \- they were very respected, but neutral.

## **Q.786. On Torrent’s future defense.**

- ## *Tags: Torrent*


He'll \[Torrent will\] be working towards more specialized forms of defense later on, but currently I will say that a water shield would be able to intercept most elemental attacks \- it requires a water source, however.

## **Q.787. On Ditto’s common battling strategy.**

- ## *Tags: Ditto, DNA*


So, for Traveler, I have Ditto as able to store DNA samples that they can shift into. They degrade fairly quickly (especially when they’re used) so it’s more common to just keep Ditto stocked with the rest of your team’s DNA. It gives it additional versatility, and that experience fighting in a variety of forms make them more adept at taking on opponent’s forms of all body types.

## **Q.788. Are the armor parts of steel/rock types organic?**

- ## *Tags: DNA, Pokemon Biology*


It depends on the Pokémon, but many rock and steel types have primarily inorganic shells with some organic components. It would be a little difficult to get DNA from the shell and armor; but not entirely impossible. It’s just more practical to get DNA from the squishy bits.

## **Q.789. Does Traveler\!Ash see Daisy in any kind of sisterly/relative way or do you think he does/could appreciate her as an attractive female?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Ash, Daisy*


Good question\! Ash views Daisy as something between an older sister/cousin sort of way and a friend. That said, Ash does think she’s pretty. Because of both his age and the way he perceives her it’s a complete afterthought, though.

## **Q.790. On weapons.**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Psychic type, Technology, Wild Pokemon*


Basically, guns don’t exist to the point we have them in real life. The technology exists, sure, but nothing more advanced than primitive firearms were really developed. The problem arises in that more emphasis was placed on heavy weapons like cannons that could feasibly hurt a Pokémon \- most can easily shrug off a few bullets, and early weaponry was so primitive and unwieldy that it just never took off. It wasn’t accurate enough to reliably hit a pokemon, it tended to really piss off and unsettled wild Pokémon, it made humans a much bigger target in engagements (whereas they were mostly ignored by Pokémon before), and psychics had a nasty habit of forcing people with guns to shoot at their teammates through mind control, physical manipulation, or just making the human hallucinate. Not to mention psychic barriers can pretty easily soak up bullets, especially from primitive, undeveloped firearms. 

Basically, a lot of weaponry is developed around not emphasizing the human as a threat. The Pokémon do the fighting, the human is support. If they’re armed with something to do real damage, it’s probably going to be something like a crossbow with explosive tips. But most of the time they’re armed with things to keep Pokémon off them \- stun batons, the equivalent of bear mace, etc \- or tools to augment their team like flash bangs, smoke grenades, etc. 

It really comes down to the fact that humans are squishy. Most of the time pokemon leave humans out of the fight. But if a human becomes an active participant (or if the opposing team attacks the human) then all bets are off and basically the humans are going to get obliterated. \[see question 629\] \[see question 630\]

## **Q.791. On Gary’s Pidgeot.**

- ## *Tags: Dragon type, Gary, Pidgeot*


Yep, Gary’s Pidgeot is naturally a giant of its species. Gary leaned into that and basically trained it as a dragon slayer \- big and bulky enough to match or overpower most dragons and faster too. \[see question 152\]

## **Q.792. How limited is torrent on land again?**

Torrent’s limited to roughly 2/3 of his true strength while on land\!

## **Q.793. Does battling on a field with water pools count as on land? Or is he \[Torrent\] as strong in those pools as he would be at sea or on a fully submerged battlefield? \[see question 792\]**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Battle, Torrent*


The water pools count as long as he’s in them \- just reducing his need to levitate lets him focus his strength on battling. His raw offensive power is going to increase depending on how much water he has available, especially with water manipulation.

## **Q.794. Do you think Dragonite are disadvantaged underwater?**

- ## *Tags: Dov, Dragonite, Dratini, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Behaviour, Torrent*


Underwater, yes. I see Dragonite as being comfortable in water, but they lose a lot of their mobility underwater compared to when they were Dratini and Dragonair. 

I think Dov would still win if it was actually a fight, but if Torrent just withdrew to the bottom of the ocean there wouldn’t be much Dov could do to hurt him.

## **Q.800. On Giovanni’s strength.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Giovanni, Karen, League, Master Trainer, Mewtwo, Persian, Pokemon Battle, Team Rocket*


Giovanni is one of those characters who would hit Master-level easy if he put his mind to it. He probably could’ve been Champion if he invested his energy into it. 

Unfortunately, Giovanni focused the majority of his time and effort on Team Rocket. He could and did have plenty of modified and beefed up Pokémon delivered to him, but that only gets you so far. 

Giovanni basically took the pragmatic view in that he’d be more powerful as the head of the Rockets than as an individual battler. Plus, his ultimate goal was the Mewtwo project which would nullify any advantage the League had in raw power, so as that came to fruition he pretty much slacked off training and threw his full effort into shaping Team Rocket to suit his vision.

Problem there comes from the format of the battle. In a regulated match he’d still get bodied by Karen due to her overall higher quality team, even taking Persian into account. 

The problem with counting him in a real fight is that it’s hard to imagine him ever going into it alone without a massive amount of support haha. 

## **Q.801. Is Oak at his current level weaker than Agatha?**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Pokemon Battle, Professor Oak*


It’s a sticky situation for Oak vs. Agatha. I know in the story that I said Oak could still take her, but as things have become more developed and fleshed out I say it’s a toss up. Agatha is in better shape, but much of Oak’s team still regularly trains (albeit without his input) and it’s not unheard of for League members to come by for a friendly spar. 

That said, a major part of Agatha’s overwhelming superiority is the mystery of her ghosts and abilities. If there’s anyone who can know her inside and out, it’s Oak. I imagine with his knowledge of her old style (and he 100% watches her League battles to keep up) that he’s uniquely suited to nullifying that advantage.

## **Q.802. Could Giovanni alone and unregulated but with prep take down Oak, if Oak has equal prep?**

Yeah, no way he takes down Oak on his own, especially with equal amounts of prep. Oak is several tiers higher.

## **Q.805. On Bruiser’s Rampage current strength \[around chapter 57\].**

- ## *Tags: Bruiser, Pokemon Biology, Rampage*

## **Q.806. How recent is cloned meat?**

- ## *Tags: Beldum, Blaine, Ditto, Moo Moo Milk, Stone Family*


Really in the last 10-15 years I’d say. It’s had the proof of concept done since Blaine’s first forays into cloning, but the mass synthesizing of meat wasn’t practical until Ditto cells became accessible. Solutions with ditto cells were able to make it much, much easier to cultivate. 

In the last two centuries, I’d say the Pokemon World shifted heavily to a more vegetarian diet overall. Pokemon were still eaten occasionally up until the last few decades, but it became more and more taboo as the world modernized and more humans came to have Pokemon companions and the world became more hospitable...not to mention a larger variety of food. 

Before that, I think they’d eat pretty much anything they could. Ranches for the purpose of raising Pokemon for meat just don’t work in Traveler’s world since most trained Pokemon would find it repugnant and the Pokemon in the ranches would have a fairly easy time of breaking out and killing the humans involved. As a result, most ranches basically evolved a symbiotic relationship similar to the Stone family and their Beldum colony \- the Pokemon provides companions and products (such as Moo Moo Milk) and the humans provide protection and easy access to food and other amenities. \[see question 366\] \[see question 577\]

## **Q.807. What's the official name for the unaffiliated traveling masters?**

The official term is Nomad\!

## **Q.808. Now what is making Ash so interesting to the legends, especially to the point of branding him?**

- ## *Tags: Articuno, Ash, Concept, Greenfield, Legendary Beasts, Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Shamouti Island, Suicune*


One thing I will say is that Branding is mostly a passive process. Just being in a Legend’s unfiltered presence leaves a mark. Mewtwo didn’t leave much of a Brand while in the armor, but his encounter with Articuno marked him and altered him, as did his future encounters with the Birds. 

The first time it went beyond a Brand and into something deeper was at New Island, then Shamouti, and then Greenfield, then Suicune. It’s changed and tempered him, and as a result he can handle more direct Legendary interaction.

## **Q.817. In the Pokemon world where there are many species smarter, stronger and more mobile than humans, how did we end up in a world dominated by humans?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Pokemon Behaviour, Psychic type, Technology, Wild Pokemon*


Largely humanity’s ability to organize. Similar to our world, their lack of natural physical power put them at an inherent disadvantage that they compensated for by organizing and cooperating with other humans as well as Pokemon \- until psychics and Aura-users advanced to the point humanity could first begin to communicate with wild Pokémon, humanity was on the verge of extinction. 

Most Pokémon are either solitary or live in small groups. Due to their natural gifts there’s no real need for them to create technology. The groups most likely to develop it due to a generally higher innate intelligence, psychic-types, have no need for it since their powers essentially are their technology. Psychic powers are immensely flexible in Traveler, and they’re essentially the ultimate tool. There was no real need to innovate technology beyond improving their psychic powers, although plenty of Pokémon have developed small-scale agriculture and other helpful technologies to some degree.

## **Q.818. The Pokemon with the capability to develop civilization didn't have the temperament or desire to, and the Pokemon that were more social didn't have the capability? \[see question 817\]**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Technology*


Yep\! Pokémon have relatively easy lives outside of competing with one another. They’re born with incredible natural gifts \- humanity were turned out into the world with little more than intelligence and good social skills lol. 

So without the need to establish even low-level technology since it would take a lot of development for convenience to overcome the hassle, Pokemon never even had the chance to build upon that foundation to reach humanity’s level of technology. 

I do imagine there are individual Pokémon or small groups out there who have innovated some basic level of technology, but it would be more out of curiosity or boredom than need.

## **Q.819. On human psychics over time.**

- ## *Tags: Abra, Psychic type, Ralts, Sabrina, Will*


I will say that psychics appear at roughly the same rate nowadays as they did previously. With humanity’s larger population there’s actually more psychics \- I think the thing is that most are very low-level compared to monsters like Sabrina, or even skilled users like Will. 

All living things have some innate psychic potential, but in the past it was one of humanity’s saving graces for communicating with non-psychic Pokemon and as a means of defense, so more people honed it to usable levels. Nowadays it’s just not worth the effort to most with low to moderate levels of psychic potential, so it tends to be less common overall. Kind of ties back to that perspective of necessity being a major driving force.

I figure the average human could reach the level of weak psychics like Abra or Ralts given sufficient training. Most just wouldn’t have access to that training, and their time could be better spent elsewhere nowadays. You don’t really grab attention to be trained unless you have high potential, which tends to be visible to other psychics.

Of course, we have had periods of history in Traveler where significantly higher numbers of psychics with large potential emerge \- we’re actually looking at the beginning of a new era like that with Traveler’s current timeline.

She’s stupidly broken lol.

If you had the right dedication, you could become a Champion of the Moon Stone. That’s...extremely boring though.

## **Q.861. Has it been mentioned anywhere why exactly Daisy did this disappearing trick on the Oak family in this setting?**

Daisy saw the event happen, and she was roughly four or five at the time. She suffered from years of not really comprehending what happened, not helped by Oak doing his best to pretend it never happened (especially while he was at rock bottom). That’s the biggest rift between her and Oak.

## **Q.863. How does Drake compare to Alder? I know Drake was a former champion, so how does he compare to Alder?**

While both are definitely Champion-Level trainers, like \[redacted\] previously stated, by nature of dragons having longevity, Drake retained most of his strength, while Alder's team waned with age.

Only a third of his original team is still with Alder.

As trainers, they're fairly different in terms of tempo. Drake is more proactive, compared to Alder's more passive and reactive approach.

## **Q.864. Does the red genesect exist? And if so, how does it stack up to the others?**

- ## *Tags: Genesect, Legendary Pokemon*


Yeah, Red Genesect exists. It's not necessarily more powerful than the other Genesects, but it's sort of specialized to act as a leader to the others in combat scenarios.

## **Q.865. Does this mean they \[Beast trio\] are as immortal as demigods, i.e. immortal in the sense that they can still die or does it simply imply that they were once mortal before being turned into legends?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Beasts, Legendary Pokemon, Pokemon Biology*


The latter. The Beasts cannot die.

## **Q.866. How rare are Feebas in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Beldum, Captain Stewart, Daisy, Feebas, Gary, Hoenn, Kangaskhan Lapras, Magikarp, Mt. Coronet, Professor Oak, Sinnoh*


In Sinnoh they're limited to water pools found underneath Coronet \- recall the conversation Gary and Samuel had about Daisy's. They don't breed well in captivity either. In Hoenn they're limited to springs found at the headwaters of some of Hoenn's rivers.

Presumably Feebas require certain kinds of water purity to thrive and don't proliferate enough to feasibly outcompete other water types (read: Magikarp) outside of their ideal habitats.

It took Captain Stewart (the man who ferried Ash to Cinnabar and Seafoam the first time) two decades of searching to find his Feebas and only those 'in the know' would have knowledge of their natural habitats. They're likely protected sites much like Kangaskhan, Lapras and Beldum, with even the information of where kept secret for their own security.

Coronet is particularly an issue because those pools aren't found within the usual well-trodden bounds of the caverns. You have to go off the beaten track which is a fantastically stupid decision for those who don't know what they're doing.

## **Q.867. How rare are Beldum colonies and where would one likely be in regions like Unova and Sinnoh?**

- ## *Tags: Beldum, Eastern Continent, Pokemon Behaviour, Region, Sinnoh, Stone Family, Unova, Western Continent*


Extremely rare \- I'm sure there are a couple over on the Western Continent and whatnot and probably some others on the Eastern but none that are really under the control of the Leagues there, I think. Hoenn's pretty unique in that the Stones have actually formed a working relationship with the local colony. Their situation is pretty unique in that way.

As to the specific 'where'...? Fuck if I know.

## **Q.868. Does the Lucky Egg or Exp Share exist in Traveler? If so, how does it work?**

- ## *Tags: Meta, Technology*


No, those are too gamey.

## **Q.869. How about the choice items? \[see question 868\]**

- ## *Tags: Bruiser, Jellicent, Meta, Pokemon Berry, Technology*


Choice items also aren't a thing. Pokemon don't really hold items in Traveler's battles.

Like, you see Bruiser with the black belt. He has it but it doesn't do anything for him \- it's value is sentimental. Berries would similarly do little \- healing doesn't happen that fast unless you have a specific biological advantage like Jellicent, and the advantage you'd gain from a tiny berry would be minimal at best. Items just aren't useful in Traveler's context in that way.

## **Q.870. Can electric types redirect other electric moves?**

- ## *Tags: Amelia, Electric type, Pokemon Behaviour, Raichu, Oz*


Yes, recall Amelia's Raichu and Oz playing catch with electric charges.

## **Q.871. How do Everstones work in Traveler anyway?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Everstone, Fire Stone, Mamoru, Meta, Rhydon, Water Stone*


Much like Fire Stones or Water Stones impart a spark of Fire and Water energy/concept onto those who come into contact with them, Everstones have a kind of 'static' concept. They enforce same-ness and, to an extent, stagnation.

For that reason I'd imagine there can be issues that arise if you hold on to them long-term. Mamoru is largely exempt because he was an adult already when he started carrying them and most Rhydon don't need to evolve anyways.

## **Q.872. Is Ash's team practicing teamwork? I know there's Infernus/Tangrowth and Infernus/Oz, but I don't know if the focus is more on preparing the field rather than helping each other during a battle.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Infernus, Oz, Steven, Tangrowth, Team Rocket*


Yep, Ash has been practicing teamwork. It’s still not his primary focus, but Steven’s been working it in...plus the Rocket raid made him realize that was a weak point.

## **Q.874. How would Wes have fared against Greevil, minus XD001?**

- ## *Tags: Greevil, Wes, XD001*

With the Shadows\!

## **Q.876. On how Dazed’s pendulum affects her powers.**

- ## *Tags: Dazed, Hypnosis*


I will say that the sway of Dazed’s pendulum affects her hypnosis, but not more physical powers.

## **Q.877. On how Ash uses Infernus.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Conference, Clair, Cynthia, Infernus, Johto, Karen, Pokemon Battle, Teleport*


One thing to remember is that pretty much every battle during Johto (minus Cynthia and Karen) was a vacation for Ash. He was there to have fun in a low-stakes battle and indulge himself and his team. He did take Clair seriously and wanted to win, but the way he behaved in that fight is very different to how he’d behave in something like the Conference or a real fight.

When there’s stakes involved, Ash’s best option is to just have Infernus teleport onto an opponent and give them a nice friendly hug. But he’s not going to do that otherwise unless it’s an opponent that can reasonably fight back against it \- battling is fun for Ash. It’s his favorite thing in the world. Using Infernus as an instant win when he doesn’t need to is boring for him and for Infernus. They’re both battle addicts that like to have fun with it, and that means they won’t always fight rationally if there’s not a pressing need.

## **Q.878. Would a pokemon like Tyranitar that used to be a ground type before evolving retain that electrical resistance or would it have lost that when it became a dark type?**

- ## *Tags: Dark type, Electric type, Pokemon Biology, Tyranitar*


I don’t think it would in most cases, which I’ll attribute to the change in physiology due to the evolution. That said, given how thick and durable a Tyranitar’s armor is, I don’t foresee most electric-type attacks being able to penetrate it regardless.

I kind of play it by species. I’m all for something leaning into a certain type even if it’s not actually that type as long as things make sense.

I’d say it’s more grey than purple\!

## **Q.882. Do they \[Reshiram and Zekrom\] have high intelligence?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Reshiram, Zekrom*


I’d say so. Intelligence is hard to quantify with Legends since they’re so in-tune with the universe and their own nature above all else, but I’d definitely say that Reshiram and Zekrom have more of a ‘human’ intelligence if that makes sense.

## **Q.883. What happens when a legend “dies”?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Legendary Pokemon, Pokemon Battle*


Yep, if a Legend’s physical form is destroyed, they’re able to pretty much immediately reconstitute themselves. Their corporeal form is just an expression of their Concept \- even if their body is destroyed, that isn’t affecting the underlying Concept.

That said, combat between Legends gets weird. What’s happening on the physical level is just a representation of what’s going on under the surface in a lot of ways. Never capable of truly killing each other, but they can definitely overwhelm or temporarily weaken the abilities of another Legend to manifest and act on the physical world.

## **Q.884. The concepts try to interfere with each other’s concepts when they try to battle them?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Legendary Pokemon, Pokemon Battle*


Pretty much\! The battles are as much spiritual as physical. Although in the end those are one and the same.

## **Q.885. Is there a difference between say Zapdos and Zekrom? Or are they the same Concept, just that one has a larger infinity?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Legendary Pokemon, Zapdos, Zekrom*


They have similar ways their power manifest, but it’s derived from different Concepts.

## **Q.886. So, uh, what was up with Ash threatening Moltres at Shamouti? \[see question 883\]**

- ## *Tags: Articuno, Ash, Feather, Legendary Pokemon, Moltres, Shamouti Island, Zapdos*


That Third of Moltres was about as close to its corporeal form being destroyed as possible, and Zapdos and Articuno had ripped it apart metaphysically as well. Could Ash kill it? Absolutely not.

He might be able to destroy its body and it might’ve take time to reconstitute itself with how weak it was, but the bravery and the audacity of the statement helped snap Moltres out of its rage \- that inspired it to reach out through the Feather, comprehend who and what Ash was, and that was what spurred it to retreat. Realistically, Moltres still would’ve slaughtered Ash’s team even at its lowest point.

## **Q.887. If the Clefable from Mount Moon had to fight Lavender, how close would it be?**

- ## *Tags: Clefable, Ghost of Lavender, Mt. Moon, Pokemon Battle, Pseudo Legendary*


Definitely Lavender in this matchup. It’s ridiculously strong, and its scale is just too much for Clefable to beat. That said, Clefable could hurt Lavender like no other pseudo-Legendary we’ve seen, although it isn’t capable of actually destroying Lavender.

- ## *Tags: Chinatsu, Dark type, Ghost of Lavender, Ghost type, Moltres, Pokemon Battle, Pseudo Legendary*


I will confirm that there are other pseudo-Legendaries with the capability of killing Lavender, although it would be incredibly close and a Pyrrhic victory at best. There’s nothing outside the Legends that could outright dominate Lavender.

Chinatsu is a weird case since she’s a vessel for Moltres’ power. On her own she’d be swallowed up and devoured by Lavender, but with enough juice from the Feather she’d win. That said, Chinatsu is too cunning to ever get pulled into that fight.

## **Q.891. On the Lugia and the Legendary Birds/ Ho-Oh and the Legendary Beasts.**

- ## *Tags: Articuno, Entei, Ho-Oh, Legendary Beasts, Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon, Lugia, Moltres, Raikou, Suicune, Zapdos*


There are 9 Birds in total \- 3 of each. There are only 3 Beasts, each unique.

Both Ho-Oh and Lugia were roughly 9x as powerful before the Resurrection of the Beasts and the Sundering of the Birds, respectively.

The Resurrection was actually performed partly in order to balance them. Creation/uplifting is significantly more demanding than simply shattering, which is why only 3 Beasts needed to be made.

## **Q.899. How long have TMs existed in the Pokemon Universe? From a technological standpoint we know Pokeballs were brought into the world by the classic Professor, but I'm wondering if TMs were a later invention? Also were Apricorn Balls invented before Samuel made any?**

## **Q.900. Was it stated that Infernus's heat can even affect ghosts when they fade?**

- ## *Tags: Distortion World, Flamethrower, Ghost type, Infernus, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Biology*


For ghosts, many are capable of briefly phasing into the Distortion World for an instant or two at a time in order to avoid attacks. Sustained assaults like a Flamethrower are useful against ghosts because very few can phase long enough to avoid it, while a simple punch (without any additional energy or elements put into it) can be phased through without much trouble.

## **Q.901. Do Pokémon need to love battle in order to attain higher tiers, or does love for battle play a very small part. ## **Q.902. Why has Daisy not evolved Eevee? Does she want it to stay an Eevee, or something else? Also, what’s the opinion on making a Pokémon not Evolve like Clair’s Dragonair?**

- ## *Tags: Clair, Daisy, Dragonair, Eevee, Espeon, Glaceon, Leafeon, Pokemon Biology, Umbreon*


For Eevee, I have it as one of those situations where the Pokémon itself is perfectly fine staying in its unevolved state.

Eevee are kind of weird in that I see the majority of them evolving naturally into Umbreon and Espeon (aside from Leafeon and Glaceon in areas where that’s likely).

Wild ones would most likely evolve around 2-3 years in. Much faster than a lot of other evolutions since Eevee don’t have an intermediate phase.

## **Q.904. Do Ghosts get the same boost that everyone else does by being close to something like an opening to the Distortion world, or Giratina? Because it feels like they would be linked by default in a similar way as Ash to Mewtwo since they were once a part of Giratina/Mewtwo at one point. But at the same time I don't know if they would have it permanently, and thus have no boost otherwise. Can Ghosts call upon this relationship for a large boost in power? Do they risk unravelling into Distortion by doing so?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Distortion, Distortion World, Ghost type, Giratina, Lavender Town, Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Mt. Pyre, Pokemon Biology*


Yep, although it’s a bit of a double-edged sword. Ghosts can draw on the latent Distortional energies and influence of places like Lavender Town or Mt. Pyre in order to enhance their own abilities and strengthen themselves, but it tends to be temporary and overdrawing will cause instability in their corporeal forms. They’re essentially limited by the amount of Distortion they can safely handle. The stronger the ghost, the more potent they are in those environments.

Ghosts can turn it into a permanent boost, but it takes a lot of time.

## **Q.905. When you say ghosts can turn it into a permanent boost, do you mean that they can permanently boost the max Distortion that they can channel? Or do you mean something else? \[see question 904\]**

- ## *Tags: Distortion, Ghost type, Pokemon Biology*


Pretty much. It basically trains their bodies to grow more accustomed to larger amounts of Distortion.

## **Q.906. Because the Ghost becomes reliant on the area for that strength, that means that Lavender is more or less restricted to Lavender Town unless it was willing to lose it's massive power?**

- ## *Tags: Cresselia, Ghost type, Lavender Town, Legendary Pokemon, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology*


Lavender’s in the odd situation where it settled in the valley because it was a bit more open to Distortion, but at this point it’s converted the entire valley and city into its ‘body’. Theoretically it could uproot the land itself and move, weakening the barriers between the material and Distortion wherever it went, but that would also raise its chances of being hunted by Cresselia.

As for teleportation, Sith pretty much said it. Jumping across a region is a strain, but very possible for Bob. Anything over a few hundred miles usually requires multiple jumps.

## **Q.915. What was Mamoru's herd doing around Celadon/Saffron? What reason do they or any rhydon herd have to migrate around like that?**

- ## *Tags: Celadon City, Mamoru, Pokemon Behaviour, Rhydon, Saffron City*


Herds regularly migrate around for resources, acquiring mates, training, etc. Mamoru also makes a point to make a tour of the region to purge potential rivals and remind everyone who’s boss.

## **Q.916. What exactly is stopping Mewtwo from rezzing Ambertwo?**

- ## *Tags: Ambertwo, Aura, Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo*


Mewtwo has no access to her biological remains, her Aura, or access to anyone who would have remembered the original Amber... on account of him killing her father.

And even if he did have a DNA sample, all he’d be left with is basically Amberthree. He’s more than powerful enough to upload a personality and artificial memories that would basically create an excellent copy of the Amber he knew, but it would still be limited by his half-remembered perception of her.

Basically, recreating Amber wouldn’t work and I think Mewtwo is aware enough to perceive it as extremely disrespectful to her memory, which is one of the few things he puts value in.

## **Q.917. Does Jirachi only have a local effect? Or does it make all of those around the world pursue their desires and dreams similar to ice types being boosted by Articuno?**

- ## *Tags: Articuno, Draconids, Groudon, Jirachi, Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon*


As for Jirachi, it would have a much wider effect normally, even during hibernation. At least enough to drive the desires of those within a few hours, which waxes the closer it is to waking.

The Draconids recognized the danger of this, and part of the reason it was buried so close to Groudon was to mute that effect and drown it out.

## **Q.921. How prominent are the top Coordinators in terms of the public eye?**

- ## *Tags: Coordinator, League*


I’ll chip in and say that Coordinators are a big deal. They and tournament trainers are two sides of the same coin. There is significant overlap, but top-tier Coordinators and top-tier trainers tend to be distinct \- one of the reasons Wallace is such a big deal.

The League does tend to support battling trainers more since that directly supports the region’s strength.

## **Q.922. Is Wallace unique in walking both roads then. I mean to his level it seems like it, pinnacle of both. But are there many that do that?**

- ## *Tags: Coordinator, Daisy, Pokemon Trainer, Wallace*


Nope\! Even Daisy manages to be a high-level combat trainer even if she doesn’t like it. Wallace has just taken it further than most. The average trainers tend to be average at both, but the high-level coordinators still manage to be decent combatants for the most part.

## **Q.923. On the Draconids.**

- ## *Tags: Draconids, Dragonite, Hoenn, Salamence, Wataru Clan*


So, this is something I've been poking elf about, in an effort to create an architectural style and overall design for the draconids, and it's been really fascinating.

First of all, Salamence and their juveniles are a fractious lot, compared to Dragonites. That itself lent a more brutish and martial bent to the Draconid culture.

In addition, Draconids could bring a lot of offensive firepower, but didn't have the aerial dominance to project force that the Watarus did.

The Draconids also tended to balance their dragon population with their human ones, and their displays of dominance and contention meant that more often than not, the Draconids would move away from their home to lend their hand to one of the numerous city states that were in Hoenn.

That, combined with them not having as much clannish tendencies and frequently marrying into outside cities and clans meant that the Draconids got spread way too thin.

So, in essence, they were Salamence tamers who were as brutish and martial-bent as their mounts, and were a very fractured and contentious clan, which led to their numbers plummeting with every passing generation till they got eventually wiped out.

## **Q.924. How did the Wataru spread to this generation if they married inside their family? Wouldn’t inbreeding eventually make that an impossibility to create more offspring?**

- ## *Tags: Blackthorn City, Wataru Clan*


One thing to remember is that the Wataru are massive to the point that their clan compound is basically its own little town. Plenty of branch families, and it was fairly common to marry unrelated people from Blackthorn or political marriages with other noble families throughout Indigo to bring new blood in. You wouldn't see Targaryen-style inbreeding except in rare cases. It was pretty common to see first cousins marrying, but that's also been common throughout human history.

## **Q.925. How do Jinx have pre-evolutions if they were humans changed by Hakuea?**

- ## *Tags: Haukea, Jinx, Smoochum*


Jinx who are turned by Haukea are formed into Jinx directly. Second generation Jinx and beyond go through the Smoochum phase.

## **Q.926. How did they work with Pokémon back then without Pokéball is the wonder?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Pokemon Trainer*


Psychics and Aura-users enabled the first bonds with pokemon to be formed, and after that it turned into a self-perpetuating partnership.

## **Q.927. How does the Snag Machine work?  Does it override pokeball registrations?  Does it only work because Orre is a lawless hellhole and no one really tracks Pokemon ownership the same way as in Kanto?**

- ## *Tags: Orre, Snag Machine, Technology*


Yeah it’s one of those things where there’s really no excuse for it unless the Pokémon is absolutely desperate or protecting itself. Sapience makes things simultaneously more and less complicated on that front.

It basically overrides the link the Pokémon has with its current pokeball, linking it to the snag ball instead. You could theoretically use it in main regions, but you’d have the League hunting you down immediately. Nobody wants something like that going around.

## **Q.928. On the requirements to challenge a region’s Champion.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Elite Four, League, Pokemon Battle*


You have to be part of a specific League’s Elite Four to challenge for the actual position. Most Champions would be happy to do exhibition battles and stuff, but having a random member of another League challenge for the Champion title introduces a lot of problems.

## **Q.929. Has any member of an elite 4 or champion ever had someone use an exhibition or challenger match as an assassination attempt on them or their pokemon?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Elite Four, Pokemon Battle*


Nope, in a regulated setting like an exhibition match deaths are pretty much unheard of. Too much security, too many eyes watching, and too much access to medical care. Even if a fatal blow was dealt, odds are the Pokémon could be brought back.

## **Q.930. How late is too late in the pokemon world? Brain death?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Biology, Technology*


Pretty much. Their medical abilities are absolutely insane. Honestly, so much as the brain isn’t outright destroyed in battle I can imagine you’d be able to bring a Pokémon back (albeit with a ton of resources invested).

## **Q.931. On Plume’s moveset.**

- ## *Tags: Air Slash, Feather Dance, Plume*


She does have Air Slash\! I don’t believe so \[she doesn’t have Feather Dance\].

## **Q.932. Does Infernus have Solar Beam?**

- ## *Tags: Infernus, Solar Beam*


One of those things where he has it, but has no need for it really.

## **Q.933. On how hard it is to learn Blast Burn.**

- ## *Tags: Blast Burn, Master Trainer, Technology, TM*


To address some of the questions above, Blast Burn is learnable by all fire-types in Traveler but does not exist in TM form. It’s a closely guarded secret of Fire Masters, and only taught to those they hold in high regard (or who pay a sufficient amount). Most trainers and Pokémon would be unable to use it even if taught. Mastering even the first stages shows a high degree of both skill and determination.

## **Q.934. So theoretically squirtle hydro cannon is a go?**

Yep.

## **Q.936. Couldn’t he give himself 20/20 vision with his Psychic powers?**

One thing to remember that hasn’t come up in a while is that Lugia’s basically erected seals around Kyogre’s resting place to prevent too much of its influence from leaking out and causing issues like Groudon’s is.

## **Q.940. On how Elf will adapt the movies.**

- ## *Tags: Meta*


I’m planning on incorporating elements from the movies \- you can assume most of the basic stuff is the same \- but actual execution will be extremely different haha. I think Spell of the Unown will be the last truly adapted movie.

## **Q.941. We already know japanese style names were the norm in today's Kanto and Johto, but did Sinnoh and Hoenn have similar styles as well?**

- ## *Tags: Dragonite, Hoenn, Indigo, Johto, Kanto, Meta, Pidgeot, Wataru Clan*


Sort of\! I’ve based Sinnoh a bit off of Greece, so you’d see more Greek-style names popping up back in the day, although there’s also some overlap introduced from relationships with Indigo and other regions \- Indigo had a particular advantage in making contact with isolated places thanks to their abundant Pidgeot and the Wataru’s Dragonite. You see some elements of Indigo’s culture and naming conventions spreading due to that.

Hoenn is more Polynesian in the archipelago and Italian in the mainland, so you’d see more of those naming conventions as you go farther back.

## **Q.942. Since they \[Ranger Union\] didn’t use pokeball, how did civilians tame Pokémon or help themselves when Rangers aren’t nearby?**

- ## *Tags: Last War, Pokemon Behaviour, Ranger Union, Technology, Unova*


The Ranger Union tends to have extremely close relationships with local Pokémon, partly a result of the cooperation between human and Pokémon during the Unovan incursions during the Last War. They’ve historically had great relationships, but that deepened it into something spectacular. Civilians oftentimes find partnerships with Pokémon without any pokeballs involved, although Rangers are definitely the experts in those situations.

## **Q.943. So Ranger Union territory is what N tried to achieve in Unova and the rest of the world?**

- ## *Tags: Guardians of Indigo, N, Ranger Union, Wild Pokemon*


Yep\! Well, the Rangers sort of act like how Guardians of Indigo did in ancient times. It’s pretty common for them to have 1-2 extremely close companions, but recruiting other local Pokémon for additional support when needed.

It’s definitely an extremely integrated society. I’d say all modern regions have very good, healthy relationships with their wild communities, but the Ranger Union has had their culture shaped through the trials of the modern world to retain a real community, as opposed to the distinction between wild and trained Pokémon in other regions.

## **Q.944. If Ash got his Teleport TM recharged could he teach it to Oz like he did infernus?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Infernus, Oz, Technology, Teleport, TM*


Hmm, if I remember correctly Teleport is a permanent TM (but it’s been a long time, so please correct me if I’m wrong). He can teach her at any time, although Oz doesn’t have quite as much psychic affinity so she couldn’t abuse it as heavily as Infernus. It would be a good addition to her repertoire, however.

## **Q.945. Were some of Kanto and Johto's clans formed from remnants of civilizations or broken clans migrating during that period, and settling in?**

- ## *Tags: Blackthorn City, Cerulean City, Indigo City, Johto, Kanto, Mahogany Town, Rota*


Yep\! That’s a great observation. Northern territories like Rota, what was once Indigo City, Cerulean, Blackthorn, and Mahogany all received an influx of new blood, although admittedly there weren’t too many years for the migration south to take place, unfortunately.
