Earth is somewhat special, but on a cosmic scale it still only has the tiniest fraction of Unown. They’ve been scattered pretty much evenly all over the universe.

## **Q.948. How are Claydol made? Are they aura-crafted or something else?**

- ## *Tags: Arid Zone, Aura, Baltoy, Claydol, Legendary Pokemon, Mew, Pokemon Biology*


So, basically that’s a situation where Mew’s boredom came into play. It showed the ancient people of the Arid Zone how to infuse Aura into their symbolic golems to breathe life into them \- Baltoy and Claydol were basically like good fortune symbols or used like gargoyles initially until the first were animated, and were made to be able to self-replicate.

## **Q.949. On Mew’s appearance.**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Mew*


Mew is basically the softest thing in the universe. All the better to make friends\!

But the fun thing is that Mew literally does choose the pink kitten form because that’s most appealing to others lol.

## **Q.950. Has Mew changed its form often then? like if one culture sees pink cats as demonic omens would it change to blue cat when around them? \[see question 949\]**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Mew*


Yep\! Mew basically just appeals to the audience. Which is helped by being a psychic god that can live in an entire nation’s head.

## **Q.951. Do actual paved roads between cities exist, and not just dirt paths?**

- ## *Tags: Dark World, Meta, Pokemon Trainer, Psychic type, Ranger Union, Rapidash, Sinnoh, Technology, Teleport, Wild Pokemon*


Cars aren’t really a thing, though they do exist. Subways exist in cities, and trains were once extremely common, with a notable route going from Indigo, around the Dark World, up through the Ranger Union, and to Sinnoh. Railroads are extremely expensive to maintain since even a weak wild Pokémon could easily destroy or damage a section, so they rapidly fell out of popularity once matter-energy conversion became more common over the last century.

There was once a more extensive road network, but it’s largely fallen out of use. Teleportation and flying taxi services (either on Pokemon or on airships) is common for long distance travel, or Pokémon such as Rapidash might carry people as well.

It’s pretty common for trainers to have at least one Pokémon to make travel significantly faster and easier, which they’ll generally keep as they rotate into a civilian life.

But yeah, the increasing numbers of teleport-capable psychics, ease of transporting goods through pokeball technology, and other factors have led to a steady degradation of standard road networks. They’re maintained, but largely for traveling trainers.

## **Q.952. Do quiet stealth helicopters exist like the military has?**

- ## *Tags: Flying type, Hyper Beam, Meta, Technology*


I’d say most likely not, simply because there wouldn’t be a real need for them. Flying-types are already incredibly quick, agile, and quiet (when they want to be), and the real problem I think would be the relative strength of pokemon. One good Hyper Beam would probably be enough to seriously damage a helicopter like that, so they’d end up being too expensive for what they’re used for.

## **Q.953. Would you say that Noctowl are preferred for stealth?**

- ## *Tags: Hypnosis, Noctowl*


Yep\! Their silent flight, perception, and specialized psychic powers or things like Hypnosis are a huge bonus on that front.

## **Q.954. How hard is it to gather specific species to complete these tasks? Say Unova wanted a Noctowl squadron, would they formally request the Johtoan government for it or would they request prior trainers to donate eggs to train for their requirements?**

- ## *Tags: Johto, League, Noctowl, Unova*


No worries\! Usually they’d rely on trainers who already have them and are associated with the Unovan League. Leagues tend to adapt to whatever their local Pokémon are, so you wouldn’t really see Leagues requesting specific pokemon. What you might see is trainers with Noctowl being loaned out to a friendly League temporarily.

## **Q.955. I was wondering if there existed trainers that lived out of RVs and if they could actually get around their region?**

- ## *Tags: Meta, Technology*


That would be a sight to see haha. But unfortunately RV’s aren’t really an option, although with storage technology you can basically make the equivalent of a cabin wherever you go.

## **Q.956. What's considered impressive for a rookie trainer to achieve in their first league? Like good and above average but not prodigy level?**

- ## *Tags: Conference, Master Trainer, Pallet Town, Pokemon Trainer*


Top 64\. Maybe top 32\. Making the top 16 in your first Conference is basically shorthand for being a future Master.

One thing that I think gets missed because of our skewed sample size of the Pallet 4 is that only the tiniest fraction of rookies even make it there. Any trainer who qualifies for the preliminary rounds of the Conference is already significantly above average, and even those skilled trainers don’t tend to make it into the Conference until a few years in. If you’re making it in as a rookie you already have a bunch of eyes on you, let alone if you actually place.

## **Q.957. Would you say that there are such thing as “late bloomers” for trainers? Those who start off slow but eventually reach the highest levels?**

- ## *Tags: Amelia, Ash, Gary, Jonathan, Pokemon Trainer*


And absolutely\! There are plenty of trainers who only start to take it seriously after a few years, or who slowly and steadily grow. Prodigy freaks like Ash, Gary, Amelia, or Jon are definitely the exception.  
Of course, you also have plenty of trainers who start out strong and jump ahead, only to either burn out or are unable to take their craft to the highest level. Lots of trainers who use powerful Pokémon but lack the ability to innovate or excel, so anyone truly skilled or creative can outfight them.

## **Q.958. So did Jon get scammed by his Fire Master?**

- ## *Tags: Fire type, Jonathan, Master Trainer* 


Nah, I’d say he got exactly what he paid for. Jon got an extremely powerful technique, but since he doesn’t have the extremely deep knowledge of fire-types that a specialist or Master has he can’t take it to its fullest potential.

## **Q.959. If Delia ever became a trainer in her youth, what starter do you think she would have picked?**

- ## *Tags: Delia, Kanto, Pokemon Starter, Pokemon Trainer*


That’s a hard one\! I don’t think she’d be in a position to get the standard Kanto starters, but I totally see her getting a relatively common mon and making it into something really special.

## **Q.960. On Blackthorn Gym’s purpose.**

- ## *Tags: Blackthorn City, Conference, Indigo, Gym, Pokemon Trainer, Viridian City*


One thing to note is that Blackthorn is kind of designed to be brutal. It gatekeeps the Silver Conference much like Viridian gatekeeps the Indigo. Even the side gyms up there are significantly challenging. Manageable for a skilled trainer, but they don’t take it easy.

## **Q.961. How common is it for someone to not be a trainer at all?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Trainer*


I’d say around 99% of people have at least one Pokémon companion. Almost everyone has had some sort of training career, although not everyone goes on a journey and most never progress past the level of a trainer with 4-5 badges. Generally strong enough to protect themselves, but most wash out before they can become genuinely powerful.

Serious, dedicated trainers trying to reach their peak probably makes up 20% of the population at any given time, although plenty rotate into civilian lives and industry as they get older and want something more consistent for their families.

## **Q.962. What do they call “ACE” trainers in Hoenn?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Galar, Kalos, National League, NOBLE Trainer, SEEK Trainer, Unova*


ACE Trainers are all called the same thing throughout the National League, but have different names in Kalos, Unova, and Galar. Unova has SEEK and Galar has NOBLE.

## **Q.963. On what constitutes a Pokemon trainer.**

- ## *Tags: Conference, Meta, Pokemon Trainer*


I use ‘trainer’ basically as a catchall for anyone who has a Pokémon and trains them somewhat, even if they don’t try to shoot for Conference. Pretty much everyone’s going to need at least one decently skilled Pokémon for many job opportunities, so there’s an incentive to train to at least the point your Pokémon can do something useful…plus most kids/early teens who are starting out think battling is the coolest thing ever lol.

There are 100% jobs where Pokémon aren’t a requirement, but even then there are plenty of Pokémon who could help assist with things like research and whatnot. Having a suitable Pokémon is a massive plus in your favor while trying to transition into an industry.

Most people aren’t cut out for the kind of life being a traveling trainer demands. There are plenty who just stay within their own city or town and train, but the vast majority just hang out and battle occasionally as a hobby and stuff like that.

The 20% thing \[see question 961\] basically represents the hardcore trainers that are striving for things like tournaments, League positions, etc.

## **Q.964. On whether the necessary infrastructure exists for Ash to post some dank memes.**

- ## *Tags: League, Meta, Porygon, Technology*


Hmm so the internet isn’t very sophisticated/ not really a thing in Traveler at this point. It’s very, very primitive. Mostly downloadable databases \- Porygon absolutely monitor League installations, but wouldn’t be involved in other unrelated ones (but corporations might have Porygon on loan to protect themselves).

I’m kind of modeling the Traveler situation off of 80s ‘Internet’ \- the infrastructure is in place for it to develop and take off, but it’s something basically unrecognizable at this point haha.

## **Q.965. Is there a lot of focus on developing it \[internet\], either through League or private efforts? \[see question 964\]**

- ## *Tags: Meta, Technology*


Nope, not really a focus on developing it. Kind of like what \[redacted\] said \- nobody’s quite even realized the potential at this point. They’re getting the most basic, practical use out of digital technologies at the moment, but I imagine over the next few years as regions become ever more connected that it might become more and more like our own.

## **Q.966. So how does the pokedex and email systems work in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Meta, Technology*


They do have connections between networks, but it’s pretty much only used for official League or commercial purposes.

Kind of like how the Internet was originally a series of connections between military/universities.

## **Q.967. Who has the strongest trained Pokémon in Traveler and what is it?**

And yep, I’d say Will and Karen are his current benchmarks. They’re just out of reach after his time in Indigo.

- ## *Tags: Gym, Gym Badges, League, Pokemon Trainer*


They have to go through gym rosters each time\!

## **Q.970. On the Elite Four challenge.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Elite Four, Pokemon Battle*


My current system is basically that the Elite Four challenge takes place over at least 3-4 weeks. It would require that long for injuries to heal and for all Pokémon to be at their full power.

What I meant in that explanation is basically that the game situation \- where you’re tossed into the Elite Four and expected to battle them (and the Champion) one after another with a single team \- is pretty much impossible for anyone in Traveler. Their medical technology is good, but not that good.

## **Q.971. We know that Blaine is a former member of the Elite Four, and we know the names of a few of the previous Champions of the Indigo League... but are there any other retired Elite Four members of note still around in Kanto and Johto?**

- ## *Tags: Blaine, Champion, Elite Four, Indigo, Johto, Kanto, League*


There are undoubtedly several in retirement, but none alive that I’ve really put much thought into to be honest\! That might be a fun thing for me to think about.

## **Q.972. Was it Mew's job as Guardian of Life that had it be the one who dealt with Mewtwo or was it just because Mewtwo was its clone? What does being the Guardian of life entail really, stopping  giant plagues or something?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Legendary Pokemon, Mew, Mewtwo*


Mew’s job as the Guardian of Life is strictly to protect life against things it can’t reasonably be expected to survive on its own \- in practice, that means Legendaries. Plagues are fine, extinction of specific species is fine, but when a Legendary threatens life itself, it’s Mew’s responsibility to make sure life continues.

## **Q.973. On how Ash was able to resist Jirachi.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Concept, Jirachi, Legendary Pokemon*


If I remember correctly, Ash didn’t need the Concepts to avoid falling victim to Jirachi.

That said, it’s the exposure to those Concepts combined with his immense willpower which let him resist it. No normal human could pull themselves away from Jirachi, and even most Legendary Champions would succumb without the intervention of their patron.

The tempering of his mind by his exposure to other Legends gave him the ability to resist, and his willpower was what let him make the decision to overcome it.

## **Q.974. I know Traveler Orre doesn’t have any Wild Pokémon like in the games, but does it have relatively few or a regular amount for a region?**

- ## *Tags: Orre, Region, Wild Pokemon*


It has a smaller amount, but that number is gradually increasing\!

Orre is badly off because of the environment. Some Pokémon can lead a comfortable life in the wastes, but the majority are going to live in an oasis, on the coast, or in the mountains. The instability and gangs in Orre cause wild Pokémon stocks to be plundered as well since everyone wants as many Pokémon as possible. Most wild Pokémon steer clear of Orre and live elsewhere on the Southern Continent.

## **Q.975. On how Orre compares to Alola.**

- ## *Tags: Alola, Last War, National League, Orre, Region, Southern Continent, Technology, Unova*


Orre actually is the jewel of the Southern Continent, which is a tragedy. It has the largest population, the most advanced technology (a result of many Unovan remnants fleeing the Last War after the National League’s counterattack), and is one of the only centers of civilization on the Southern Continent, even if it’s currently a garbage heap of a region lol.

Alola WILL be better, but it’s an absolute backwater right now. Minimal population, minimal development outside a few centers, and really has nothing going on at this point, although development is spiking and will continue to do so.

## **Q.976. When you mean unovan remnants fleeing, do you mean Orrian scavenged the tech or did the Unovan contribute the tech? \[see question 975\]**

- ## *Tags: Cipher, Last War, Orre, Region, Technology, Unova*


I don’t want to go into much detail (it’s something I’d rather leave for the story to tell) but basically, some pieces of the Unovan invasion forces weren’t able to regroup to island fortresses or retreat back to Unova proper. As a result, several groups ended up in Orre to carve up territory as warlords, much of which helped to destabilize the region further and were later incorporated into Cipher.

## **Q.977. Is Fantina Kalosian?**

- ## *Tags: Fantina*


Yep\!

## **Q.978. Any thought about where the likes of an old master like Mustard would rank among the young bucks. Would his team be out of their prime like Oak or Drake?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Drake, Master Trainer, Mustard, Professor Oak*


For Mustard, I see him being like Drake where his team is still in top form. Drake has an edge on him in how long-lived his team is, but Mustard seems the type to continuously strive for improvement. His team might age, but he compensated with more fine control and skill. Mustard is still in the Champion tier, although he isn’t what he once was.

## **Q.979. Is Drake and Mustard stronger than Oak?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Drake, Master Trainer, Mustard, Professor Oak*


Oak is still high Master, although even Champions wouldn’t be eager to scrap with him due to his brilliant mind. Mustard and Drake are both stronger than Oak since they’ve maintained their training.

## **Q.980. What would they do with Drake’s dragons when he dies?**

- ## *Tags: Dragon type, Drake, League, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Trainer*


One thing to remember is that since Pokémon are sapient, that pretty much ceases to be an issue. When their trainer dies, most Pokémon go their own way, whether that’s returning to the wild, staying with a friend or family member, or selecting a new trainer. The dragons are going to go where they will, and they’re not likely to just go and rampage. If they did, that’s when the League would get involved.

## **Q.981. On Zygarde’s concept.**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Legendary Pokemon, Zygarde*


Yep, Zygarde is equilibrium. It’s the balance, a representation of the natural order of things.

## **Q.982. So how high of a weight class can Zygarde step in to try and restore the equilibrium?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Legendary Pokemon, Reshiram, Xerneas, Yveltal, Zekrom, Zygarde*


Hmm, can’t say too much on that. I will say that whereas Xerneas and Yveltal aren’t really active physically, being sort of like Zekrom and Reshiram on that front, Zygarde is extremely powerful physically. It acts, unlike the others.

## **Q.983. What would happen if a Ghost was able to nom nom on a Legend's aura (and I'm going on the basis of the Legend allowing it and not immediately destroying it)?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Ghost type, Legendary Pokemon, Pokemon Biology*


That's an interesting question\! So, the majority of ghosts would basically burn out from trying to directly consume a Legend’s Aura. Very powerful ones could survive, and perhaps even use it as a food source, but it would alter them. Regular ghosts could experience something similar by feeding on the Aura of a place or organisms that have been exposed to a Legend’s Aura \- secondhand Concept exposure, basically.

## **Q.984. On whether it is possible for multiple Legends to select the same Champion.**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Champion, Legendary Pokemon*


As for multiple Legends selecting the same human or Pokémon as their Champion… technically possible, but very likely to completely burn out the mortal. Most Legends don’t like to share, and hosting two Concepts would obliterate pretty much any mortal’s mind and soul, particularly if those Concepts were liable to interact in a hostile manner. It would take someone very special to manage that without tearing apart at the seams.

## **Q.985. Any other characters other than Ash which could handle multiple concepts?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Aura, Concept, God-King, Mamoru*


God-King could definitely do it for reasons that will be explored later. Other than that, not really.

Surprisingly, Mamoru would be able to pull it off if they were Concepts working in harmony. His high mastery of Aura and his own nature (plus age) gives him a very sturdy foundation that roots him.

## **Q.986. I'm going to guess that the God King runs counter to what Elf says about how humans empowered by Concepts still can't match Pokemon. Or was that just about Ash?**

- ## *Tags: God-King, Legendary Pokemon, Lugia*


Yep, God-King was basically at the level of Lugia. Extraordinarily powerful.

## **Q.987. Have past legends wiped out species by accident that Mew hasn't brought back?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Mew, Pokemon Behaviour*


Nope \- Mew allows a species to live or die by its own merits, but if it was strictly due to a Legend’s actions then Mew would repopulate the species.

Basically, “Oh, you die because you can’t adapt? You’re a failed experiment. You die because a Legend caused too much change too quickly? That’s fair. Take a species-level 1-Up”.

## **Q.988. What would Mew do if Rayquaza decided to keep ending humanity?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Mew, Pokemon Behaviour, Rayquaza*


Mew would just keep remaking them, or wait Rayquaza out \- it doesn’t have the capacity for a prolonged campaign.

Ah yeah that was a little vague. Definitely has the power capacity, but is lacking in other areas it would need for something like that.

## **Q.989. On Pokeballs’ history.**

- ## *Tags: Apricorn Balls, Aura, Last War, Pokeballs, Professor Oak, Technology* 


So, pokeballs have existed in their current form for about fifty years, and primitive working copies (extremely expensive and impractical, generally very large) have been around for about seventy-five. Apricorn balls have been around for centuries and developed into those primitive pokeballs, although for a long time they worked in…let’s just say esoteric ways rather than technological. Apricorn balls were extremely expensive and pretty much only used by nobility, and even they could only afford a few of them.

You also see ancient civilizations with storage devices, but those were always Aura-based, and far more limited and inflexible compared to the technology of today.

What Oak did wasn’t to actually create the pokeball, but he refined it and advanced it significantly. Due to Oak’s work, pokeballs have become far more widespread, easy to produce, and both stronger and faster. Early modern pokeballs could take up to a minute or two to materialize a Pokémon, while Oak’s processes make it almost instantaneous.

One of the reasons the Last War was so devastating, for example, was because pokeballs were finally becoming relatively widespread. The ease of trainers maintaining significantly larger teams directly correlated to the immense devastation in that conflict, along with the logistical advances that came as a result of pokeball technology.

## **Q.990. Could the process \[of a Pokemon materializing\] be disrupted, and what would happen if it were?**

- ## *Tags: Pokeballs, Technology*


It could be disrupted, but at no harm to the Pokémon. It would just cancel the conversion and return the Pokémon to its pokeball.

## **Q.991. What happens if you destroy the container \[Pokeball\]?**

- ## *Tags: Last War, Pokeballs, Technology*


For my own sanity and to avoid tactics in the Last War of ‘shatter these pokeballs within enemy ranks to nuke them’ I’ll say it just releases the Pokémon. And yep, pokeballs are extremely tough and durable.

## **Q.992. Pokemon are conscious within the pokeball right?**

- ## *Tags: Pokeballs, Technology*


Somewhat. I liken it to being in a shallow sleep \- they’re vaguely aware of what’s going on and can release themselves if there’s a huge stimulus, but overall they’re just in stasis.

## **Q.993. On Professor Oak’s impact on the Pokeball fabrication process.**

- ## *Tags: Last War, Pokeballs, Professor Oak, Technology* 


Professor Oak would have only had a few years to work on pokeballs, but they were already a viable product by then and much more mainstream than even a decade before the Last War.

Professor Oak’s influence by the time of the Last War was largely to make them more efficient \- easier to produce, enhancing their strength and speed, etc.

No huge revolutions, but enough to make them more and more practical.

## **Q.994. What pokemon would be the best choice to have as a companion for a sailor?**

- ## *Tags: Dragonite, Indigo, Pidgeot, Region, Sinnoh, Wataru Clan*


Oceans would be extremely dangerous. Up until the last few centuries only a tiny handful of groups could manage short voyages across the water. Ocean travel was almost impossible \- initial contact between regions was largely done by explorers on the backs of Pidgeot, Dragonite, etc. The Wataru had a very successful tradition of explorers \- quite a few made a major mark on Sinnoh’s perception of Indigo since travel was so difficult.

## **Q.995. Has the plot in Pokemon rangers diverged or is it relatively the same? And if so, has it already taken place or will it take place?**

- ## *Tags: Meta, Ranger Union*


It’s relatively the same at this point, with some differences (similar to how the Orre games are handled). One of those situations where you can assume canon until otherwise, although the Ranger Union likely won’t play a major role to where we’ll see those differences.

## **Q.996. So is the Psychic Sense its own sense or is it more of a  "use psychic powers to collect environmental data then feed data to other senses for translation" type thing? like if Dazed sensed something behind her using psychic powers would it be like she was seeing them or is it a completely distinct sense?**

- ## *Tags: Dazed, Pokemon Biology, Psychic Sense, Psychic type*


It’s completely distinct\! I’d say it does intertwine a bit with her other senses, but for the most part it’s an information dump into the brain. Closest I’d compare it to is echolocation.

## **Q.997. Can that sense be overloaded like sight and hearing? or is it not as vulnerable to the anti-psychic technique? \[see question 996\]**

- ## *Tags: Psychic type*


Oh absolutely. The best way to mess with a psychic is overstimulation of senses, and the psychic sense isn’t immune. Easiest way is lots of people and Pokémon, but another psychic can mimic the effect with the equivalent of a psychic scream.

## **Q.998. What's the best place for education in Kanto for an aspiring researcher?**

- ## *Tags: Celadon City, Cerulean City, Kanto, Saffron City, Vermillion City*


I’d say Saffron is probably the home of the largest universities in Kanto, although there are tons and tons of institutions all over. Celadon undoubtedly has major ones, and I can see Cerulean and Vermillion having their fair share as well.

## **Q.999. Is Gyarados a Flying type in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Flying type, Gyarados, Hurricane, Infernus, Water type*


So for Gyarados, they’re considered a water/flying-type in Traveler purely because I don’t like changing types from the games. I can see it being classified as such in the old days because I imagine Hurricane is a favorite of wild Gyarados \- perfect for territorial displays and tearing fliers out of the sky when Gyarados is hunting.

In practice, I treat Gyarados as just a water-type. It’s not particularly vulnerable to electricity normally due to the heavy plates protecting its body, although that can be circumvented by striking it internally.

Gyarados are notorious enough that every trainer will research how to combat them effectively, much like how everyone and their mother is finding ways to fight Infernus.

## **Q.1000. How would a master level gyarados approach combat considering the amount of techniques that are used to neutralise gyarados in general?**

- ## *Tags: Grey, Gyarados, Gym Leader, Master Trainer, Michael, Pokemon Battle, Primeape, Salamence, Water type*


Ironically, I think a Master-level Gyarados would avoid water-type techniques except when it knew it was safe since they open up a vulnerability.

But honestly, I think it wouldn’t be tactics and physical abilities that make a Master Gyarados stand out. Gyarados already have strength in spades, but the weaknesses most people are able to exploit tend to be their aggression and rage \- without a strong trainer that’s on good terms with them, most Gyarados just run rampant across a battlefield. Powerful and overwhelming, but very susceptible to more skilled and experienced opponents. A Master Gyarados would exhibit qualities of self-control and discipline \- they might still be furious and destructive, but they’d be able to use that cold, focused rage to their advantage.

I see Pokemon like those \[Primeape, Salamence, etc.\] as a ticket to quick power. By having them at all it’ll be a nightmare for beginning trainers and a serious challenge for mid-level trainers. But once you start hitting Gym Leaders, elite trainers like Michael or Grey, and Masters, it’s just asking for trouble. Something strong without the skill to back it up is just asking to get picked apart.

## **Q.1001. On Ninjask’s speed.**

- ## *Tags: Ninjask*


Yep, I see Ninjask as being able to hit high speeds for traveling, but I really see it as just dominating in close confines. Too quick and too agile to hit.

## **Q.1002. How... is the interior of the Indigo League? Where the Elite Four and the Elite Four trainees live, more precisely. I seem to remember something about psychic restrictions making the entire place a maze for any except the Champion. Are Elite Four also immune? Do they all live in close quarters, or do they have their own "segment" of the league? ...Do they have fancy carpets all throughout the corridors because they can afford to have them and keep them clean?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Champion, Elite Four, Indigo, League*


So, there are psychics and ghosts stationed to mess with unauthorized perceptions. League members stationed there such as ACE trainers on duty and Elite Four members are fine. Other personnel authorized to be there are okay as well.

The Elite Four are all living relatively close together, and there are barracks for other trainers not far from there. I’d say the Indigo Plateau is very much a spartan place to live \- a towering citadel of stone. Since most people can’t appreciate its interior due to the psychic interference, walls and corridors are just bare rock and wood. Decorations are reserved for areas such as the atrium, ball room, personal areas, and stations for League personnel. Basically, any public accessible area will have rugs, nicer aesthetics, etc. but it’s still relatively bare.

I don’t think I’ve mentioned much about it in the past other than a few basics, so that’s on me.

## **Q.1003. Does Dazed have names for other people close to Ash?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Champion, Dazed, Lance, Steven*


Yes she does\! She has them fitting more into slots or roles than unique names. Lance is ‘Champion-Mentor’ for example, and I believe Steven would be something similar if not identical since they fill a similar role in Ash’s life.

## **Q.1004. What are the names that other party members have for their companions and such?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Infernus, Pokemon Behaviour, Psychic type, Tangrowth, Torrent*


For Infernus and Torrent they have Recollections chapters where you can see a few of them. All Pokémon tend to see things more in terms of roles/concepts than humans (while psychics are especially reliant on that).

It’s also filtered through perception. Infernus’ massive respect for Ash means he calls his teammates by the names that Ash gave them \- even Tangrowth is referred to as Binder.

Lots of Ash’s team are that way to some extent, calling one another some variation of their nicknames.

## **Q.1005. On Paul.**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Paul, Pokemon Trainer*


Paul would treat Ash with a ton of respect. There’s definitely a bit of a one-sided rivalry if they meet, simply because Paul sees Ash as a mountain to climb. As long as Ash wasn’t busy he’d see no issue with indulging Paul with a battle.

## **Q.1006. Would we see some mentoring there as well? From Ash to Paul?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Paul, Pokemon Trainer, Sinnoh*


I don’t think so, specifically because of Paul’s attitude towards training. There’s no way Ash would bother with him until he got his act together. And even then Ash would be a busy boy in Sinnoh.

## **Q.1007. On Orre’s current technology.**

- ## *Tags: Cipher, Orre, Technology*


I think Orre tends to be very in your face with their tech \- it’s outdated outside of previous Cipher installations, but a lot of civilization relies so heavily on it to survive that you see more of it.

## **Q.1008. How does Feebas evolve in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Evolution, Feebas, Pokemon Biology*


I basically have it as Feebas developing high self-esteem.

## **Q.1009. How well can pokemon communicate with each other in Traveler? Particularly across wildly different species that are nothing alike?**

- ## *Tags: Language, Pokemon Behaviour*


They can communicate tone and emotion through their noises, but more complex meaning tends to be imparted by the rudimentary psychic abilities shared by all pokemon. Not so much words as impressions, feelings, and images.

## **Q.1010. So how do dark types communicate with others if part of it is psychic abilities?**

- ## *Tags: Dark type, Language, Pokemon Behaviour*


There’s a reason dark-types tend to be pariahs among other pokemon. They’re unable to have meaningful communication with others. As a result, many dark-types have evolved to live in packs for their own protection.

## **Q.1011. Does that mean a lot of trained dark types feel like outcasts since they can't interact well with the rest of their team?**

- ## *Tags: Dark type, Language, Pokemon Behaviour*


Yep, although they generally find ways to communicate a little better just through familiarity. It isn’t normally a crippling limit though. Just an inconvenience.

## **Q.1012. Circling back to the Dark type communication problem \[see question 1010\], would it be accurate to compare it to trying to talk to someone with a very thick accent, or trying to talk using similar but distinct language, like Portuguese and Spanish? also Weavile is noted to have a writing system using scratches on trees, was that developed in response to communication difficulties between pack mates?**

- ## *Tags: Dark type, Language, Pokemon Behaviour, Weavile*


I’d say it’s more like the similar but distinct language \- close enough to translate broad meanings, but the finer details get lost. And yep\! A lot of dark-types have very complex social systems and communication skills for that reason.

## **Q.1013. Do you have any obvious flaws you see in Traveler's society?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Meta, League*


That's an interesting question\! In a lot of ways, Traveler’s society is very idyllic. Pokemon provide the answer to a lot of problems, both directly and indirectly by shaping a society that can’t afford to be careless or weak.

That said, that constant threat has also prevented a lot of advances. Their society has a great focus on strength and power, and there are few bounds on a Champion’s or League’s authority. If the fail safes don’t work, it would be easy for a system like that to fall into tyranny, and for their benevolent military dictatorship to shift into a genuine authoritarian government.

## **Q.1014. I wonder if that’s happened in the past to a League? \[see question 1013\]**

- ## *Tags: Chinatsu, Hoenn, League, Sinnoh*


Definitely Sinnoh and Hoenn (even without the League system, governments will have a high martial focus). Pretty much every region was like that in the past. Even Chinatsu would allow it to a point, although mostly when she deemed it necessary. She’s brutally pragmatic like that.

## **Q.1015. When two masters meet, do they tend to gravitate towards fields that work in their favor? How would a water master contribute to a wide scale fight that's mainly inland?**

- ## *Tags: Master Trainer, Rain Dance*


Yep, they definitely shoot for fields in their favor. Every advantage counts in a battle like that. A lot of Water Masters will try to use things like Rain Dance to even the playing field, even if it’s not the same as having something like a pond or lake. A lot of Water Masters are sure to develop levitation abilities in their team so that they aren’t helpless away from a body of water.

## **Q.1016. Rhydon are seen as relatively not smart (would be the kindest way to say it) but we see Mamoru is quite smart even in Champion. Is Mamoru an outlier of his species?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Dazed, Mamoru, Rhydon, Rhyhorn*


Pretty much what \[redacted\] said\! On average I’d say Rhyhorn aren’t the brightest, but there are plenty that could be right up there with Dazed or average pokemon, plus even the dim ones can grow a bit more aware and experienced over time.

## **Q.1017. What is Lance’s team of 6 for title challenges?** 

- ## *Tags: Aerodactyl, Champion, Dov, Dragonite, Lev, Mael, Magnus, Saph, Pokemon Battle*


Dragonite, Dov, Saph, Magnus, Lev, and Mael. Aerodactyl is typically used for battles against fellow Champions he knows can handle her. Too risky otherwise.

## **Q.1018. Do you think he'll \[Lance will\] be able to get gabite/vibrava up to speed with the rest of the team in any close time?**

- ## *Tags: Dragonite, Flygon, Gabite, Garchomp, Master Trainer, Lance, Salamence, Vibrava*


I imagine in the next year Lance will have a high Master-level Salamence, Garchomp, and Flygon to add to the mix. I imagine he’ll alternate out two of the Dragonite in Champion battles to make that work.

## **Q.1019. On Saph’s progress.**

- ## *Tags: Dov, Dragonite, Evolution, Lance, Saph*


I figure she’s still catching up a bit, but at this point Dragonite and Dov have managed to really accelerate her training. I also figure Lance was very patient with Saph’s evolutions, where there would’ve been more of a need for Dragonite to evolve early.

## **Q.1020. Wes died in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Cipher, Wes*


Wes died about seven years before Traveler began. Wes had three years after Colosseum before he was assassinated by Cipher\!

## **Q.1021. How is the Galar League structured? We see in the games that there really isn't a Champion that presides over the entire region along with an Elite 4 (at least in present) and it's more similar to a sports tournament with Leon as the most famous figurehead of the entire tournament. We know that Galar has NOBLE as their ACE equivalent but who do they report and operate under?**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Chairman Rose, Champion, Elite Four, Galar, League, Leon, Macro Cosmos, NOBLE Trainer*


So, Galar is in a unique boat. It does have a League, with Leon as Champion but no Elite Four to carry out his will, but with Gym Leaders there to fulfill a similar role as in Indigo (but with much more of a celebrity bent). The real power lies in Macro Cosmos, which has slowly taken control and power away from the League \- at this point, the League is just a public-facing side of Macro Cosmos. Nominally independent, but heavily reliant on Macro Cosmos’ resources and support to function.

NOBLE does report to Champion Leon, but a large number are also ‘under loan’ to Chairman Rose to assist with Macro Cosmos’ operations, and he’s who they are truly loyal to.

## **Q.1022. Isn't everyone in Galar a step down in terms of skill compared to say the National League, thanks to how isolated they are?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Galar, Master Trainer, National League*


I’d say it’s less that they’re a step down in skill, but more that they’re a step down in experience. They can still reach the equivalent levels, but tend to not be as battle-hardened. In the high tiers you tend to see Champions and such that struggle against equal opponents and Masters more than they should do to a lack of competition. Absolutely something that can be fixed, though\!

## **Q.1023. On how accessible some Master Trainer’s techniques are.**

- ## *Tags: Master Trainer*


My view of it is that training rate has largely peaked, although the rate has room to increase a bit more. Due to the Pokémon World’s more unique and powerful techniques being guarded behind the Master-apprentice system they just don’t have the accessibility and freedom of information our world has.

## **Q.1024. The God-King was noted to be around the same level as Lugia, was this in reference to Lugia now or Lugia before the split?**

- ## *Tags: God-King, Legendary Pokemon, Lugia*


That’s in reference to current Lugia\! Will confirm that.

## **Q.1025. So I assume it’s the same with Reshiram and Zekrom being on par with current Lugia?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Legendary Pokemon, Lugia, Pokemon Battle, Reshiram, Zekrom*


Yep. They’re all roughly on the same level, with different matchups being determined by context and Concept.

## **Q.1026. On whether a Concept can power up another Concept.**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Creation Trio, Legendary Beasts, Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon*


Hmm, outside of rare occasions I’d say no, unless it’s a greater Legend empowering a lesser. Between high-tier Legends like the Creation Trio and low-tier Legends like the Beasts or Birds there’s a significantly bigger gap than between a full Bird and a human.

So just passively soaking up the power from a high-tier Legend can seriously empower lower ones in the right circumstance.

## **Q.1027. So Celebi in Dialga's presence gets a huge boost? \[see question 1026\]**

- ## *Tags: Celebi, Creation Trio, Dialga, Legendary Pokemon, Moltres*


Yep, Celebi would hypothetically get a big boost. As for Moltres…if it was around a member of the Creation Trio, it would benefit from reality being a little more…real, which would amplify its abilities.

## **Q.1028. How do Inkay and Malamar work in Traveler?**

- ## *Tags: Inkay, Malamar*


Basically, they have extremely compartmentalized bodies with lining between different sections that enables them to manipulate both energies at once. If they’re injured, however, there’s a chance that the lining will be disrupted which can nullify their abilities.

## **Q.1029. Do they \[Inkay line\] have the dark type problem of not being able to effectively talk to others or are they Psychic enough to have that talking telepathy thing? \[see question 1010\]**

- ## *Tags: Dark type, Inkay, Language, Malamar, Psychic type*


Due to their psychic abilities they are able to use telepathy and communicate effectively\! They just tend to use it more for dominating others than diplomacy.

## **Q.1030. Does their \[Inkay line\] evolution requirement of having to be upside down to evolve have any correlation to Traveler, or is it just that Malamar's body plan is opposite Inkay's?**

- ## *Tags: Distortion, Inkay, Malamar, Psychic type*


Nothing concrete yet, but I'm considering the idea that it basically has a compartmentalized body. What I mean by this is that the core with all the organs and central brain is protected by Distortion to allow it to nullify psychic attacks and otherwise protect itself. Its head tentacles are used to manipulate Distortion. Its brain, however, is connected to its 'arms' through very tough, protective tissue that separates the Distortion from the neural system that goes to the arms. That allows it to use the arms to manipulate psychic powers.

## **Q.1031. On how much Ash understands Air Lens.**

- ## *Tags: Air Lens, Ash, Blaine, Psychic type*


Just wanted to provide some clarification on that front\! Ash does have a good understanding of the basics of Air Lens \- the fine-tuned physics stuff is beyond him, but thanks to Blaine he does understand the physical processes that are going on (just not in as much detail as Blaine himself). It’s that knowledge he’s using to develop a way around it\!

## **Q.1032. Is there a potential mirror electric Air Lens that Oz could use?**

- ## *Tags: Air Lens, Infernus, Oz*


I currently have it as no mirror electric Air Lens, although Oz is going to focus more on her psychic barriers to counteract elemental attacks like Infernus’.

## **Q.1033. I'd assume no Legends have true "base" forms, aside the pure Concept they embody, like literally fire for Moltres? Their physical form may only be their more practical embodiment, or just something that they "like"?**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Concept, Legendary Pokemon, Mew, Moltres, Psychic type*


This is pretty much it. The physical forms of Legends are pretty much by choice \- whatever represents their Concept, basically. In theory, pretty much any Legend can appear however they wish in those constraints. Psychics and Aura-users are more capable of getting a true perception of them.

That being said, most Concepts are relatively static and as such change form rarely, if at all. Mew is a special case with a special affinity for transformation, which reflects the diversity and adaptiveness of life.

## **Q.1034. So Mewtwo is the only one with an actual physical base form then?**

- ## *Tags: Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo*


Pretty much\! Although to be honest he could pretty easily change his own just through psychic abilities.

## **Q.1035. Which of Ash’s Pokémon is the most intelligent?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Bruiser, Dazed, Hypno, Pokemon Behaviour, Sneasel, Torrent*


More seriously, I’d say a lot of them are pretty average intelligence for their species. I think Dazed is intelligent even for Hypno, but I also imagine Sneasel, Torrent, and Bruiser to be intelligent relative to the rest of their species.

But yeah, Bruiser is very thoughtful in general. It might not be that he’s going to perform much higher on an IQ test, but he spends a lot of time in his own head thinking. Definitely a high WIS stat. Bruiser is all about subverting expectations.

## **Q.1036. On how the Legendary Bird’s Concept was affected after Lugia divided them.**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Legendary Bird, Legendary Pokemon, Lugia*


Yep, the Concept is totally unaffected and still exists as a whole, but its manifestations/aspects were split. One god wearing three faces basically.

## **Q.1037. Can a pokemon decide to live in society like a human does if they want to? Like if an Alakazam wanted to be a teacher or something, is there anything stopping it?**

- ## *Tags: Alakazam, Pokemon Behaviour*


Nothing stopping it\! It would be unconventional for sure, but the main reason it happens is that many Pokemon have no interest, or don’t enjoy living in human civilizations and cities. It definitely happens much more often in rural environments.

## **Q.1038. What was Drake Hiro's Dragonite named?**

- ## *Tags: Dragonite, Drake, Hiro, Meta, Ryoto, Saikaku*


The name of Drake Ryoto’s companion was Akinora. I pretty much ripped the name from Japanese history \- it’s the name of a female warlord and clan leader in the late 1500’s. Figured it was a fitting name for the partner of a Drake\!

## **Q.1039. Were the greenfield Unown all the Unown on earth or just a small part of it?**

- ## *Tags: Greenfield, Ruins of Alph, Unown*


So jumping back a few, the Unown located in the Ruins of Alph represent a major portion of the Unown on the planet, but nowhere near all. Several groups worked together in order to collect all easily accessible Unown and seal them away in various locations, hopefully well-protected enough that nobody would find them. They foresaw something like Greenfield happening, though, and made sure not to seal full amounts away in a single location.

## **Q.1040. What's the official position of the Chairman of Galar?**

- ## *Tags: Chairman, Champion, Galar, League, Macro Cosmos, Rose*


So, the Galar League has a different setup. Macro Cosmos has slowly gained more and more power, and as such the Galar Champion is actually very similar to what we see in the games as a figurehead. Most power reserved for the Champion is ceremonial, or restricted to the Galar Chairman declaring an emergency. Essentially, the Galar Chairman isn’t necessarily part of Macro Cosmos, but handled more of the day-to-day and administrative side of things. With Rose integrating Macro Cosmos into the League’s functions, the role has become pretty much one and the same.

## **Q.1041. Have we ever seen Haukea use her powers to fight someone?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Haukea, Lance*


We have seen Haukea use her powers against Lance and his team, although he admittedly only has a rudimentary grasp of Fire. Or at least expressing it.

## **Q.1042. Lance say that he felt he could take Haukea on with his rudimentary understanding of Fire? Would Lance be comparable to Haukea or is this just Lance being an unreliable narrator?**

- ## *Tags: Concept, Haukea, Lance*


Definitely Lance being an unreliable narrator\! Haukea is old, and she knows both herself and her abilities. She’s an extension of Ice, and wields that power like her own limb.

Articuno spoils her, honestly.

## **Q.1043. Why does Articuno spoil Haukea so much?**

- ## *Tags: Articuno, Champion, Concept, Haukea, Legendary Birds, Legendary Pokemon, Moltres*


Haukea has dedicated herself entirely to serving Articuno for a long, long time. She’s crafted herself into something as close to Ice as can be managed \- basically, Haukea walked like Ice until Ice walked like her, to steal the words of mantling from Elder Scrolls. She became almost indistinguishable, and that affords her a far deeper connection than most Champions of Moltres.

## **Q.1044. Sabrina is just a stronger psychic, right?**

- ## *Tags: Master Trainer, Sabrina*


Yep. Sabrina is someone who could easily be a Master if she set her mind to it, but she is essentially only as strong as she needs to be to achieve her goals and maintain her influence.

## **Q.1045. In the presence of legendaries, do the personalities of mortals change?**

- ## *Tags: Feather, Legendary Pokemon, Vermilion City, Viridian City*


Yes and no. In the short term, the answer is probably 'slightly', but not that much unless the Legend is touching them or directly trying to influence them. In the long term, a mere proximity won't change a personality  (though a powerful psychic can engender psychic powers in others, as we've seen described in Vermillion and Viridian), but if they give a part of themselves like a feather, then yes, they absolutely do.

## **Q.1046. Could a legendary force someone to accept their power and change them?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Legendary Pokemon, Spheres, Tani, Wes*


To answer your question, most often, Legends do not bother with mortals. As seen with Ash, Tani, and Wes, Legends offer their power to those that do accept it. It is a choice.

Well, to be more honest, most of those that bother make it a choice. Bets are off if you piss one off.

And we've also seen what the Spheres tried to do to Ash.

## **Q.1047. Do interspecies ailments exist in Pokemon that pose a large problem for potential team combinations?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Biology*


I don't believe so, actually. Microbes and other such very small viruses and illnesses exist in Traveler, but nothing above that size that isn't explicitly a pokemon. Closest you'd get are Joltiks.

## **Q.1048. Why do Pokemons have trainers? I mean they have these awesome powers and all that, yet they allow themselves to be captured by humans and used in whatever way the human wants. Like what do the Pokemons get out of their relationship with humans?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Wild Pokemon*


This is largely something that evolved from early human practices \- humans benefited greatly from befriending local wild pokemon, which grew into the social custom of partnering up because that's what friends do, which eventually became training as competition was introduced on a social and non-existential (i.e. 'I'm not trying to murder you and take your stuff') level. It's sustained because humans are by and large more ambitious than pokemon? That's a big statement but humans are sufficiently weird compared to pokemon that it didn't just become pokemon training under other pokemon much.

To make one of those points clearer \- you don't see pokemon trainers (emphasis on the pokemon) because, while pokemon teach each other all the time, the actual competitive sport that 'training' as Traveler understands it is a largely human-run enterprise. In the wild, that usually just gets recognized as territorial dispute or what counts as inter-communal politics.

And of course there are plenty of pokemon that fight for sport between themselves (look at any fighting type), but those are limited in ways Traveler's training and battling isn't.

## **Q.1049. Then hasn't any Pokémon ever tried to create a local/regional hegemony with their herd?**

- ## *Tags: League, Wild Pokemon*


I mean, I can't name any, but I'm certain they have. There's a reason the Leagues are confined to their tiny regional areas.

To put it another way: the world of Traveler is fucking big. I'm certain there are communities of wild pokemon that act in such a way. The Rhydon herd has their territory (though it's a rather small enclave \- winter quarters, really), etc.

It's easy to imagine Tyranitar or Rhyperior claiming mountains for their own that they lord over, or Pidgeot claiming swathes of territory for their flocks.

I would imagine the extent would be that large communities might consider themselves as 'living in Bert the Tyranitar's territory \- I send him tribute of berries and he lets me live in peace.'.

## **Q.1050. Can an Eevee evolve into Sylveon within Kanto?**

- ## *Tags: Eevee, Evolution, Kalos, Kanto, Sylveon*


No, they cannot. I'd imagine that Sylveon, if they were to be taken from Kalos or similarly saturated areas, would essentially experience a kind of deficiency \- like, they might be able to generate their own energy for a short time and live well enough but over time they'd face serious health consequences as their bodies fail to keep up with demands.

Like scurvy, but for fairy energy.

## **Q.1051. How do pokemon know what they are when they hatch? Is it an instinctual thing? Do they learn how to say their name from the others around them? What would happen if say, a Charmander hatched but was raised by an Infernape, would it think it's an Infernape? How do other pokemon know what another pokemon is if it just sees them but doesn't hear them?**

- ## *Tags: Charmander, Hypno, Infernape, Nidoking, Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology*


This is an interesting question, but I think it can be answered in part by clarifying one key point: Pokemon names are human constructs in Traveler, they don't do the 'I'm gonna say my name' thing that they do in the anime, it's more like the games where they do the usual grunt, shriek, cry noises. Between themselves, pokemon are more likely to use terms like 'Poison-Herd-Monarch' for Nidoking, or 'Dream-Eaters' for Hypno, etc.

A pokemon raised by one of another species, thus, would be referred to in whatever way the referer sees fit. When you hear pokemon using 'proper' names, like how Dazed or other psychics do sometimes, it's a habit picked up from other humans, usually for the sake of clarity, and key, it's usually being done when they're talking to humans, not other pokemon.

## **Q.1052. How broken is quiver dance in traveler verse?**

- ## *Tags: Kommo-o, Quiver Dance*


It's as useful as any other enhancing move: in some contexts, but not all. All enhancers are expensive energy-wise, or they limit a pokemon's capabilities, are physically taxing in terms of damage (such as Kommo-o's performance), etc.

## **Q.1053. What’s the explanation behind porygon and it’s evolutions in universe? How was it created and what is it exactly?**

- ## *Tags: League, Pokemon Battle, Porygon* 


It's a synthetic pokemon, modeled on computer programs. The evolutions are 'upgraded' versions of the same pokemon.

Primarily the former, I don't think they're used for the latter. They're expensive to make and very specialized \- the League doesn't let just anyone use them. I honestly doubt you'd see one in competitive battling.

## **Q.1054. Would Cynthia have more than 6 pokemon at a champion level?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Cynthia, Garchomp, Glaceon, Lucario, Milotic, Roserade, Spiritomb, Togekiss*


Cynthia's pokemon are Garchomp, Togekiss, Lucario, Spiritomb, Milotic, Roserade, and Glaceon to my knowledge. So, 7\.

## **Q.1055. Do some big name trainers have a team of nutritionists and the like to get their new pokemon up to standards, before they take over the training? Like, Lance trains his newbies up from scratch, but what if its a busy gym leader or something?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Gym Leader, Gym Trainer, Lance, Pokemon Trainer*


Gym leaders and such might delegate that sort of thing to gym trainers since they'd be eating as a commune, essentially, and I could see Lance and the other champions doing the same in busy times, but most of the time a good trainer just knows their team's diets by heart.

## **Q.1056. How much backing did Tobias have to be able to train a team of Pseudo legends?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Conference, Pokemon Trainer, Pseudo Legendary, Tobios*


Less sarcastically, worth noting he was a conference champion. When you're a high level trainer you can generally self-finance with winnings so long as you're proactive.

It's the mid-levels where you might want to expand your team but you're not amazing at training and thus not consistent at winning that poses the greatest barrier to a trainer's overall growth.

## **Q.1057. You mentioned somewhere that Irene's and Cynthia's relationship wasn't exactly the warmest, but did she train under her? Other than when she passed down the Champion mantle.**

- ## *Tags: Byron, Champion, Cynthia, Irene*


Without a ton of detail, Cynthia and Irene didn't have much of a relationship at all. Irene gave Cynthia some advice and hung a lot of her hopes forlfor escape from the champion's mantle on her, but by the time Irene really acknowledged Cynthia, Cynthia was already powerful enough to challenge her. It was actually Byron who did a lot of the mentoring for Cynthia, and guided her along her journey.

## **Q.1058. What’s the tax policy of Almia?**

- ## *Tags: Almia, Fiore, Indigo, Oblivia, Ranger Union, Sinnoh, Unova*


Almia and Fiore are on the same system \- they're just separated by a mountain range. It's still the same Ranger Union with those acting more like provinces than distinct regional entities. Very similar to what you see with Indigo, actually. They're macro-managed the same but on the local level have separate processes, primarily to engage with the local differences that have existed for most of their history, even through their time as part of Sinnoh.

That being said, I'd imagine they have a very involved federal system, with the Ranger Union itself serving as that central government. Most of the local governances are allowed to manage their cities at the local level while the government oversees taxation and distribution of funding to the various programs designed to protect the environment, local pokemon populations, provide health care, etc. The Ranger Union is really big on societal welfare so I'd imagine tax rates are very liberal; the more you make the more you're expected to contribute. They've had their share of exploitation from when Unova invaded and used them for oil and resource extraction at their own expense. Welfare programs are the norm, both to expand education possibilities (i.e. free college and the like) and take care of the very large elderly population as the nation ages on average.

Oblivia's separate because it's quite isolated and waaaaay less developed. I'd imagine they don't pay much in the way of taxes to the central Union government and more use them for their own local communities, whereas the Union actually spends a lot more on them to help them with development of their local infrastructure, educational opportunities (which have up until now been largely absent), and healthcare facilities.

## **Q.1059. Pokémon also dampened colonialism? Because full colonies might be rejected by local Pokémon?**

- ## *Tags: Kalos, Orre, Pokemon Behaviour, Ranger Union, Unova, Wild Pokemon*


Pretty much. Unova (and Kalos) tried that \- The Ranger Union can be considered to have been 'colonized' in the sense that it underwent forced development for the purpose of resource-extraction to benefit the colonizing force, but that only really lasted as long as the War. I would also hazard a guess that something to that effect happened in Orre (can't confirm it, sadly. I don't know myself). But it just generally doesn't work out. Pokemon don't stand for that kind of exploitation of the environment and humans don't really get a choice in the matter unless they can get pokemon to cooperate.

## **Q.1065. So a few questions. Do Jynx's have the capacity to form a bond with a trainer? If a fire master were to catch a Jynx, would the Jynx be able to accept existence within the presence of the team? Or would we see it break its' pokeball to escape? Additionally, with that fading, do distortion based attacks go through that fading ability? Can you kill a Ghost Pokemon by obliterating them repeatedly?**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Aura, Banette, Distortion, Ghost type, Jynx, Master Trainer, Mewtwo, Shadow Claw, Viridian City*


Jynx, like any Pokémon, is capable of their own agency. Masters have been known to capture Pokémon outside of their chosen specialization, so it really depends on the contexts. I highly doubt there would be any first-generation Jynx that would allow themselves to be caught, so any mundane trainer, Master or not, would only be able to capture one from a later generation.

I imagine Distortion-based attacks can also be sustained, so that one's rather nebulous. Though, if it's an empowered physical attack like Shadow Claw, it might be able to dodge it since the moment of contact has gone by.

As Agatha had previously stated, Ghosts, by nature of merging with the physical world to sustain itself, are also vulnerable to Distortion. It's a very double-edged tactic, since it does harm the Ghost with prolonged exposure.

Mewtwo did not obliterate any Ghosts, during the Viridian raid, to my knowledge. He simply forced them to disperse, and it took time to collect themselves once more. It's more physical, than having anything to do with Distortion manipulation.

Particularly skilled ghosts can phase for longer, as can those that are bound to a less solid corporeal form. Gengar phases easier than something like a Banette, for example.

Technically, you could eventually kill a ghost by destroying its corporeal form over and over. It takes massive amounts of energy to reform, so if it’s ‘killed’ enough times it won’t have the energy to reform, and the ghost’s Distortion will be eroded away by the Aura of the world.

## **Q.1066. What is the source for Fairy energy?**

From what I understand, it's Legends that can create an environment hospitable for Fairies to exist comfortably in their native regions. I'm also going to point out that while all Legendary Pokémon are Legends, not all Legends are Legendary Pokémon.

She's just that fast at recovering.

## **Q.1071. Would that mean Lunala and Solgaleo are champions of Ho-Oh and Lugia?**

- ## *Tags: Aether Foundation, Cosmog, Evolution, Legendary Pokemon, Lunala, Solgaleo, Ultra Space, Ultra Wormholes*

They come from Ultra Space, create Ultra Wormholes, have an evolutionary line and can reproduce (quite unlike any Legend) and even in canon Cosmog was considered an Ultra Beast by the Aether Foundation. Additionally, while the idea of a sun/moon duo makes sense from an earthly perspective, it makes little sense from a cosmic perspective given the massive difference in scale between the two.

## **Q.1072. Isn’t Drayden up there in age? Plus wouldn’t his team have already taken a hit during the war that would have possibly included lost members/injury reduced longevity?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Elite Four, Drake, Drayden, Last War, Master Trainer, Sinnoh, Unova*


He's roughly the same age as Drake, who despite his age is still Champion level and the strongest Elite Four on the planet. Drayden was never up to Drake's level, but he's still solidly Master level. The problem with Unova's Elite Four post war was that they were fairly stagnant in terms of challenges. No one wanted to challenge them out of fear of disrupting the political balance, and it was only with the current generation of Unova's Elite Four that the positions were passed on. They didn't see a lot of change like Sinnoh's Elite Four, as an example.

## **Q.1073. On Bruno vs. Marshall.**

- ## *Tags: Alder, Bruno, Champion, Iris, King Under the Mountain, Marshall, Master Trainer*

## **Q.1074. I remember some frequent mentions of people being sent to be re-educated under the old-government of Unova. How many of those included visits to some friendly neighborhood Beheeyem?**

- ## *Tags: Beheeyem, Mewtwo, Psychic type, Shadow Pokemon, Unova, Unown*


Unova definitely had reeducation camps, but they used conventional/real life means to do it. Psychic manipulation of that sort is near impossible to pull off without the power of something on the level of Mewtwo or the Unown for more than a bit of time. Mind control requires constant focus on the target, a Beheeyem wouldn't be able to, say, reach into someone's brain, tweak something, and make them a loyal soldier forever. More likely, you'd see psychics used to enhance or augment existing brainwashing techniques.

That sort of difficulty with brainwashing was what made Shadow Pokemon so terrifying. It was a reliable, simple, repeatable process that could be standardized.

## **Q.1076. On Unova’s government before the Last War.**

- ## *Tags: Last War, Unova*


Yeah, the Unovan regime was an oligarchy run by the Ministers. There was a lot of instability and power jockeying between them, and none of the Ministers had supreme power. There may have been a "Prime Minister" of sorts, but they would have been a figurehead with no real power. The core government was headed by around 30 or so ministers, with some having more power than others. Minister of Expansion (read: war) and Minister of Communication (read: propaganda) were some of the biggest.

## **Q.1077. Wondering how Curse works in traveler verse for non-ghost types?**

- ## *Tags: Curse, Dark type, Distortion, Ghost type, Plume*


Curse in Traveler when used by non Ghost or Dark types works by flooding the body with Distortion energy. It provides a defense against psychics and also improves defenses, though the focus required tends to leave Pokémon more immobile. Granted, for Plume this means “Almost too fast for the eye to track” rather than faster than that.

## **Q.1095. Do the Distortion organs have a role in deciding it? like bio ghost dont have the organs so they are relegated to Ghost instead of Dark?**

- ## *Tags: Dark type, Distortion, Ghost type, Pokemon Biology*

## **Q.1096. How do specialists and generalists compare in terms of numbers at different levels of training?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Cynthia, Gym Leader, Master Trainer, Pokemon Trainer*


Higher level generalists tend to hit the problem where they’re a jack of all trades, master of none. It’s only the most talented generalists that can really match the knowledge and skill shown by Master level specialists in their type.

So, in the bottom and mid-levels of trainers you tend to have more generalists. There’s absolutely a small number of trainers that set out determined to be a type specialist, but for the most part people find a particular type they like and begin leaning into that more as they grow.

But in the high ranks is where the specialists thrive. By Gym Leader-level you tend to have a 4:1 ratio of  specialists:generalists

By the Master-level it’s almost entirely specialists since they can focus in on one type and bringing it to its fullest potential, almost always having nullified standard weaknesses by then.

Generalist Masters are very rare, perhaps 10% of an already tiny group. They tend to remain in the lower rungs, but when they do advance past that wall they’re monsters like Cynthia \- growing from a Master of None to a Master of All.

## **Q.1097. Was it the King's size or just his general power that required the Master Ball?**

- ## *Tags: Bruno, King of the Mountain, Master Ball, Pokeballs, Technology*


Size, really. There's only so much storage that can fit on that thing. The bandwidth alone to release and absorb it is already huge even at the rate it does. Power is more a function of how easy it is to force it to stay in the ball.

A pokeball can hold Mamoru as easily as a Caterpie, it's just how hard it is to make it stay in the first place.

For the King, it decided to go with Bruno after their challenge for several reasons. The first is that it greatly respected the abilities of Bruno and his team \- Bruno himself played a role in defeating it by turning its own strength against itself, and to the King who had gone unchallenged for centuries due to his size, that made quite the impression. It saw the chance for growth with Bruno, as well as a great deal of respect for his noble spirit as well.

## **Q.1098. You can have a Pokémon without having a trainer license, right?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Trainer*


Training licenses are more like, you have gone through some amount of pre-requisite training to be able to work with people/beings who are going to be putting life and limb in moderate danger because that's the nature of the sport. The League wants to make sure there's a basic level of knowledge so there aren't any stupid, avoidable accidents because someone didn't know how to provide first aid.

It's also to keep track of who's actively training and battling, likely for the benefit of public works and services like Pokemon Centers (i.e. Traveler's universal medical care).

Very similar in a driver's license \- you can be an excellent driver without ever having gone to driver's ed, but it's in the interest of the public to ensure that everyone on the road has a basic knowledge instead of gambling on who might happen to know what and who doesn't.

I would imagine it's more or less ingrained into a standard education curriculum. Something akin to a mix of life sciences, home-economics, basic budgeting/first aid/sex-ed practical skill courses, as well as parallel biology and practical knowledge courses tailored to working with pokemon of a variety of species. Many diverse skills that are organized into a useful curricula, essentially.

Like, I couldn't see it being lumped into a 'Pokemon' field, like we do with Mathematics, Reading, Science, etc.

No one label will suffice, so it's a holistic course-curricula.

## **Q.1099. Are there smaller communities that accommodate for that? Like if a bunch of people who have Onix or other Pokémon unsuitable to live in an urban area, would they go and form a more spacious community? Or one more specific for the Pokémon they prefer?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Brock, Gym Leader, Mt. Hideaway, Onix, Pokemon Behaviour, Steelix*


So, things like Onix and Steelix just flat out can't tunnel around population centers and they have to be excessively careful about where they're released surface-side so they don't cause property damage. There was actually a fair bit about it during 'The Master' and 'The Storm' \- as Ash thought about catching one of the giant Onix of Mt. Hideaway and Brock had to explain some of the Steelix protocols while they were tunneling.

## **Q.1100. Are TM moves that the pokemon's biology is able to perform, or are they moves that could be taught by other mons? Also, how exactly did humanity discover TM's?**

- ## *Tags: Arbok, Pokemon Biology, Silph Corporation, Technology, TM*


Yes and yes. You need to be capable of using a technique to use it \- an Arbok can't use Double Kick. And most TM's are just moves, they can be taught directly \- mentor to student \- and that's how moves and techniques have always been passed down. TMs can create a shortcut to being able to use a technique, but it doesn't convey mastery, and many moves just flat out don't really work via the method.

Humanity \- specifically Silph \- developed them in recent years. The how is fuzzy, but I'd imagine it's some manipulation/copying of Psychic techniques to impart knowledge via technological means. I don't know the specifics, it's probably some technobabble like most pokemon science after a certain point.

## **Q.1101. How often do masters under the league convene? Do they ever have meet-your-coworkers to deepen the bonds between them? I’m assuming it’d be to keep nationality and camaraderie strong.**

- ## *Tags: Elite Four, Master Trainer, New Island*


The meeting in 'The Family' with the League gym leaders and Elites is about the closest you'd get to that. Maybe smaller tournaments alike to the kind that was supposed to be hosted on New Island on occasion, just to test who's the strongest.  
But aside from that I'd imagine not. Masters don't have a union, they don't really have any particular reason to build camaraderie or nationalistic sentiments. Aside from those explicitly employed by the League, they're still private citizens doing their own thing.

## **Q.1102. How do evolution stones work? In the sense of does it halt a Pokémon’s development if it’s given early or is that irrelevant?**

- ## *Tags: Evolution Stone, Nidoking, Pokemon Biology*


It doesn't halt development but if you use them too early it can cause problems, because biological development is something of a process. If you skip steps in the process you can fuck things up down the line. Most of the time, in the long term things will work themselves out, but if you, say, forced an evolution on an infant you'd probably be dealing with serious long term developmental issues, stunting, etc.

Whereas Nidoking, who evolved relatively early, just has to deal with hormonal imbalances for a few years.

But they work by essentially triggering latent evolutionary genes via a boost from a stone's natural energies.

## **Q.1103. How powerful is the Master Ball?**

- ## *Tags: Master Ball, Pokeballs*


It's very powerful but honestly that sort of power isn't useful. If you're trying to catch something that is resistant to being caught, then it won't matter if the pokeball goes ding because the moment you let it out it's going to kill you.

That, and it is better at the capturing process, it's just that it's a proof of concept more than anything. Improvements on that scale aren't useful on their own. It's innovation for its own sake, rather than for practical application.

## **Q.1104. Is the process of bringing back fossils going to eventually be streamlined enough for them to be introduced to their own environment? Or will it remain a special service for elite trainers?**

- ## *Tags: Elite Four, Fossil Pokemon, Pokemon Biology*


It's not quite the same level of innovation for innovation's sake \- there's genuine use to having fossil pokemon around to look at. It's just probably not something that'll become mainstream. A forever specialized thing.

## **Q.1105. On the relative strength of the champions.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Cynthia, Lance, Metagross, Pokemon Battle, Steven*


Going back to some of the earlier conversations, I'd say that Lance is the overall strongest. His strategy of turning the majority of his team into the Pokemon equivalent of bombers is very effective and difficult to counter. When comparing the three Champions we've seen, they all counter each other to some extent. Lance has an advantage against Cynthia due to his fliers posing a unique challenge, but Steven's team are a bunch of hardened targets that can resist his elemental storms... plus Metagross, of course. Meanwhile, Steven's Metagross gets countered extremely well by Cynthia, and the remainder of her team can solidly outmaneuver his teammates.

It's hard to pin down the strongest since there's so many variables that come into play. Unique styles, trainer and pokemon personalities, the environment, the weather \- all potential factors in determining how a battle will play out.

Lance has the most advantages, but in general Steven will fare better against him than Cynthia. There's a ton that goes into a battle on that level.

## **Q.1106. How common is it for Mewtwo to tweak the genetic composition of the clones on his island if they’re meant to reproduce?**

- ## *Tags: Mewtwo, New Island, Pokemon Biology*


They're capable of reproduction now, although finding a compatible partner among the clones may be a challenge. They are immortal thanks to Mewtwo, though, so I don't think they see it as a pressing matter yet.

## **Q.1107. On Ryujin’s and Taimu’s relationship.** 

- ## *Tags: Cerulean City, Champion, Indigo League, Kanto, Ryujin, Taimu*


I imagine the Ryujin and Taimu as quite close after the formation of the Indigo League. The Ryujin and his partner greatly respected Taimu as a foe, a feeling which was returned by the future Champion, and eventually turned on his father and secured Cerulean's allegiance during the final battle of the Kanto unification campaign.

## **Q.1108. Do Pokemon like Metagross gain aspects permanently from bonds with people or other Pokemon? Such as a large amount of emotion?** 

- ## *Tags: Champion, Claydol, Metagross, Metang, Pokemon Biology, Steven*


Sort of\! Psychics can begin to take on aspects of people they’re around (such as Claydol) but with significantly more issues resulting from that if they share long-term psychic bonds. That isn’t healthy, and often leads to a loss of identity for both.

Ironically enough, Steven embodies both between Claydol and Metagross.

Overall I’d say it wouldn’t be significantly more difficult on him than sharing headspace with almost other powerful psychics, but would definitely make it harder to adjust to.

I can actually see it being harder on him when he was forging that bond with the two Metang \- similar as they might be, it would still be tugging him in two different directions.

## **Q.1109. Exeggutor are 3-6 separated entities too, correct?** 

- ## *Tags: Exeggcute, Exeggutor, Metagross, Pokemon Biology*
