## **Q.1110. Before Kanto and Johto were called Indigo, did the continent have one name for both Kanto and Johto or were they separate?**

- ## *Tags: Eastern Continent, Indigo League, Johto, Kanto, Ore Mountains, Taimu*


They were separate until the unification under Taimu\! The Ore Mountains were massive enough to be a solid dividing line that left them distinct. At most, they might have been seen as the southern regions of the Eastern Continent.

## **Q.1111. We know how Taimu met Mamoru, but how did he meet Shinobu and Chinatsu?**

- ## *Tags: Arcanine, Chinatsu, Indigo City, Legendary Pokemon, Mamoru, Moltres, Shinobu, Taimu, Tauros*


He met Chinatsu a few months after the destruction of Indigo City, when he was still wandering the wilderness with Mamoru in a daze. They saw an enormous light to the east one day, followed it, and discovered a shrine to Moltres which Chinatsu guarded.

They met Shinobu during their unification \- a young Tauros separated from his herd and badly wounded in an attack by an Arcanine, who they nursed back to health.

## **Q.1112. Was Chinatsu already a maiden to Moltres? \[see question 1111\]**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Chinatsu, Legendary Pokemon, Moltres*


Yep\!

## **Q.1113. Was Chinatsu a new maiden at this stage? \[see question 1112\]**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Chinatsu, Feather, Legendary Pokemon, Moltres, Ninetales, Taimu*


So Chinatsu was only a few decades old at this point. She was a worshiper of Moltres, but was freshly evolved into a Ninetales when she accepted the task to assist Taimu. That’s also when she received her Feather.

## **Q.1114. Any reason why she took a few decades to evolve into Ninetales? \[see question 1113\]**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Chinatsu, Legendary Pokemon, Moltres, Ninetales, Pokemon Biology, Vulpix*


Fire stones can be extremely rare in the wild \- it’s essentially the life goal of Vulpix to find one.

Moltres provides a nice alternative, although quite a few Vulpix would enter into the service of older Ninetales that hoarded the things over the centuries.

Moltres has had countless Champions over the eons \- one mark of Moltres’ is that they are never permanent. They might last for thousands and thousands of years, but that’s a drop in the bucket for a Legend. All fires go out one day, and when that happens their duty is done. Chinatsu is just the latest in a long, long line.

## **Q.1115. Wasn’t he \[Taimu\] around his 50s to 60s \[when he died\]?**

- ## *Tags: Age, Taimu*


Yep\! That’s what went into his Recollection. I feel like I might have said he died in his late 30s at some point though \- lots of time for me to have flip flopped before settling.

## **Q.1116. Were people and their pokemon conscripted in the Last War?**

- ## *Tags: Last War, National League, Unova*


Yep. Unova had mandatory military service for years before the war as they prepared. When tensions began to rise the regions of the National League also began recruitment efforts, then conscripted trainers once information suggested Unova’s invasion was imminent.

That said, the majority of the forces involved in the Unovan Landfall were hardened veterans \- conscripted trainers were mainly left home as security, or used to man bases or otherwise relegated to non combat roles.

## **Q.1117. When challengers in the Hoenn league reach Wallace, do they fight on a modified field for his water types?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Hoenn League, Pokemon Battle, Wallace*


With League battlefields, there’s generally several different environments built into it so that no type of fighter is automatically at a disadvantage. There’s definitely going to be a lot of water, but also normal ground for fighters\!

## **Q.1118. How common were psychic-type companions back in the era of Taimu?**

- ## *Tags: Lavender Town, Pokemon Behaviour, Psychic type, Taimu*


They were pretty rare, especially outside Lavender\! At that point most psychics lived isolated or in enclaves far from humans, and were pretty much able to avoid humanity with ease.

## **Q.1119. So no Saffron enclave of Psychics? \[see question 1118\]**

- ## *Tags: Celadon City, Cerulean City, Lavender Town, Psychic type, Saffron City*


Yep\! Previously, Saffron was dominated by fighting specialists. Lavender set it up intentionally that was as a buffer state between Celadon and Cerulean, its great rivals at the time

## **Q.1120. How does Curse work in Traveler? Is it ghost type exclusive or can other pokemon learn it as well, but as the buffing variation?**

- ## *Tags: Curse, Dark type, Distortion, Ghost type, Pokemon Biology*


Both options are available\! Ghosts use Curse as a technique to inject a bit of their essence into an opponent, while non-ghosts can flood their body with Distortional energy to enhance their offense and defense at the cost of mobility and speed since it’s a concentration heavy technique.

Dark-types have an easy time with it since they have the power in spades already, but it can be difficult training for anything else. Inexperienced users will feel like they have the flu if they use it for too long, and constant use without giving the body time to adapt for long periods of time (ex. Months of using it multiple times per day) can lead to symptoms similar to radiation poisoning if a Pokémon isn’t careful.

But short term use is completely safe \- holding it for a minute is totally fine, for example.

## **Q.1121. On Aron’s age.**

- ## *Tags: Age, Aron*


Aron was only a few months old when he was caught. That being said, if I could go back I’d make him at least a few years old to play into the fun dichotomy of his mentality and combat abilities compared to those of the much younger team.

## **Q.1122. On how hard memory manipulation is.**

- ## *Tags: Psychic type, Unova*


Also, destroying memories or wiping out sections is significantly easier than rewriting them. A somewhat skilled psychic can do that while keeping the person from suffering actual brain damage for the most part.

Identity erasure was actually a favorite punishment of the Unovan regime for serious political dissidents and repeat offenders that went against the regime.

## **Q.1123. How about copy pasting memories? directly inserting one person's memories into another person's head. It'd be obviously fake, but could it work? \[see question 1122\]**

- ## *Tags: Pseudo Legendary, Psychic type*


So for that, I’d say it’s kind of possible? Actually doing anything with memories beyond destroying them is excessively difficult \- transferring memories would basically involved chasing that memory in someone else’s head, recreating it in someone else’s, and then hoping for the best. It might cause confusion, but it wouldn’t stick long or would be easily discernible from natural memories.

Even destroying memories is somewhat difficult \- manipulating the brain like that at all without causing permanent damage takes massive amounts of control.

As for the emotional triggers, honestly not in 99% of cases. Even psychics that do focus on mental skills, hallucinations, domination, etc. tend to focus on the present \- without the constant input of psychic power, the effect wears off.

Removing the emotional trigger in the moment is easy. Completely severing it is extremely difficult, beyond anything but a Master or Pseudolegendary psychic that’s specialized in those techniques.

## **Q.1124. How do League psychics refer to the Elite Four and Champion? Do they just use their title, like "Elite Four Koga", or do they have "roles" like Dazed has, such as "Champion-Mentor" for Lance?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Dazed, Elite Four, Gym Leader, Koga, Lance, League, Pokemon Behaviour, Psychic type*


Generally they’ll refer to them entirely by their titles. Pokemon tend to see things in concepts/roles filled rather than individual names except in extreme circumstances. League-trained pokemon also tend to be better with human forms of address compared to psychics such as Dazed.

## **Q.1125. How do Pokémon sizes work in Traveler again? Can biologically immortal just grow eternally in size?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Biology*


Sort of\! Most do have a cap they reach eventually, or else their growth slows to a negligible amount that keeps them at a relatively stable size.

It does depend on the species though.

## **Q.1126. Would a 500yo Tangrowth have a significantly bigger body then a 50yo Tangrowth, or would the majority of growth be in the vines?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Biology, Tangrowth*


His body would continue to grow substantially, but after a certain point it would primarily be vine growth that added to his size \[see question 674\].

## **Q.1127. On Dark Balls.**

- ## *Tags: Cipher, Dark Balls, Michael, Pokeballs, Snag Machine, Team Rocket, Technology*


Basically Team Rocket absorbed as many of Cipher’s surviving science staff as it could after Michael ended them the second time \- as a result of merging it with Rocket’s own research, they were able to produce the Dark Balls. Not quite as thorough, effective, or complete as the full method, but fast and easily usable. They were also crossed with snag machine tech to turn a trainer’s Pokémon right back against them.

## **Q.1128. On how rare the starters are.**

- ## *Tags: Gym, League, Pokemon Starter, Pokemon Trainer*


Yeah, the game starters are fairly rare. Not unheard of, but not easy to get either. Most people just get starters from their local Gym, a breeder, or other avenues \- it’s in the League’s best interest to make sure there are as many available to new trainers as possible.

## **Q.1149. What would Ash's journey look like if he wasn't so fate touched, or if the legends weren't waking up, Mewtwo didn't exist, etc.?**

- ## *Tags: , Amelia, Ash, Champion, Conference, Cynthia, Gary, Jessica, Jonathan, Lance, Legendary Pokemon, Mewtwo, Professor Oak, Steven*


Interesting question\! So, if we say he’s avoided all that stuff and either Legendary events aren’t happening or whatever, I think he’d be on a similar track as Lance, Steven, and Cynthia at that age.

I still see him traveling with Amelia and Jonathan unless there’s a good reason not to. Assuming through some bizarre twist he still gets the same teammates, I’d say he ends up at the Conference and makes it to either Top 8 or Top 4\.

That said, it’s a MUCH harder fight. He would still do extremely well in the earliest, but would never dominate like he did.

He’d still solidly beat Jon, and scrape out a win against Jessica. Gary would beat him if Gary got training from Professor Oak like in Traveler proper, but I think Oak wouldn’t help Gary if Ash weren’t also getting Champion-level assistance. Or else he’d take them both on and try to heal their rift.

League would be very interested since Ash would still have been marked down as a very talented rookie, and I think they’d not make a trainee offer but would try to build some kind of relationship with him.

His trauma pushed him farther than he would have otherwise, and his Legendary experiences and other adventures have both shaped him as a trainer and earned him the confidence of many people who can help him grow beyond what he would be by himself.

More likely a match with him would end up being a prize of sorts \- I can see the tournament organizers paying Ash a nice chunk just to be present and do something with the winners.

## **Q.1158. Infernus was able to contain the fire sphere power, why can't Oz do the same to some of Zapdos's electricity?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Concept, Fire Sphere, Infernus, Legendary Pokemon, Oz, Zapdos*


Yeah, with Infernus it more came down to willpower. Ash could conquer the Fire Sphere without being burnt to a crisp \- the Concept dominates you, or you dominate the Concept. There’s no in between, more a metaphysical and battle of wills than just a battle of strength. Course, most mortals would be utterly subsumed and burnt out by the Fire Sphere. Ash and Infernus both have massive willpower, however, and also some familiarity with the Concept already \- Ash had been tempered by Legendary contact, and Infernus had been remade with Fire.

Trying to tank an attack is a bit different. That’s a pure physical expression of the Legend’s power, and physical limits come into play there.

## **Q.1159. On what Amelia is currently working on.**

- ## *Tags: Amelia, Grey, Pokemon Battle*


One good thing to remember is that Amelia’s specifically trying to compensate for her weakness to raw power \- she’s not eager to get bodied by another Grey\!

## **Q.1160. Does the Ever Grande league contact known Masters like Kapono Paewei for help with security threats since they aren’t as equipped with powerful trainers like Indigo?**

- ## *Tags: Ever Grande League, League, Master Trainer*


For Masters, they tend to be two things that make them unappealing for the League to contract:

1\. They’re a huge pain to deal with 99% of the time if they’re not already with the League.

2\. They’re very, very expensive.

For the resources and favors that go into hiring one Master, the Ever Grande League could hire a dozen or more mid to high-level trainers. The Ever Grande League’s main problem tends to be coverage, not firepower.

I am excited to show Dazed’s growth\! She’s kind of in a weird boat where her raw power is as high as it needs to be, and now most of her big strides will be based around learning new skills and techniques.

## **Q.1164. On Michael’s and Giovanni’s training strategy.**

## **Q.1165. Is air lens a very well known technique?**

- ## *Tags: Air Lens, Blaine, Gym Leader, Magmar, Pokemon Trainer, Slugma*


The average (or even above average) trainer wouldn’t know about it in any detail unless they’re familiar with Blaine. It’s not casual knowledge, but if you read up on the Magmar or Slugma line it’ll pop up.

## **Q.1166. Is that one of the defining marks \[of a Champion\]? That no matter how good a master plans there is just too much raw power and skill to overcome?**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Master Trainer, Pokemon Battle, Pokemon Trainer*


Sort of\! Champions tend to be pretty maxed out in all respects, but always have a particular specialty.

By the time you’re high Master-level it’s really tough to physically improve your Pokémon. They’re hitting their physiological limits \- incremental growth is there, but from there it’s all about experience, tactics, and technique.

Every Champion-level fighter is a work of art, trained to perfection to counter literally anything, usually developing entirely unique skills or taking standard skills beyond what’s ever been seen before. And more than that, the team ends up as greater than the sum of its parts as each teammate can complement one another and set the others up for success.

There’s no ironclad mark for Champions other than just being more than even the strongest standard Masters. More skilled, more intelligent, and trained past the barriers most Masters fail to break through.

## **Q.1167. On Mamoru’s power level.**

- ## *Tags: Aura, Ghost of Lavender, Legendary Pokemon, Mamoru, Master Trainer, Pseudo Legendary*


I will say power was 95% figured out by Chapter 17, so the Mamoru fight is mostly valid\!

Also, for the pseudos I will say there’s a spectrum, similar to Masters. Any Pokémon that’s transcended normal limits \- whether through Legendary influence, raw physical might, technique, or Aura mastery is considered a pseudo, although some (such as Lavender) stand out as especially potent.

## **Q.1168. Has anyone taken over the viridian gym yet?**

## **Q.1170. Has Ash met any of the other game protagonists?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Brendan, Leaf, May, Meta*


This could always be where Leaf comes in. But he has met Brendan and May.

## **Q.1171. What were the main powers in Johto that Drake Ryoto had to conquer/ally with?**

- ## *Tags: Azalea Town, Cherrygrove City, Cianwood City, Dragonite, Ecruteak City, Flying type, Goldenrod City, Johto, Mahogany Town, Olivine City, Ryoto, Taiyo, Tsuki, Violet City, Wataru Clan*


Good question\! I’ve gone back and forth on the Tsuki and Taiyo’s timelines \- beginning anywhere from 1,200 years before Traveler to around 700\. Pretty sure canonically in the games the towers were built 700 years ago, so let’s roll with that.

For now I’ll say that they came into existence afterward and ruled for roughly 550 years. A successful dynasty by any measure.

Violet City was a powerful force at the time, maintaining a strong central presence and specializing in flying-types. This specialization gave incredible advantages in logistics  \- they were able to respond to new situations and deliver messages extremely fast, and were only second to the Wataru in tactical flexibility \- and also gave them a fighting chance against Wataru raids, although a single Dragonite was still a terror. They were wealthy due to so much inland trade passing through, and were a key ally for Ryoto to gain.

Otherwise, the main contender was Goldenrod. It was immensely wealthy and powerful, generally exerting large amounts of influence over Azalea, Olivine, Cianwood, and Cherrygrove (which was frequently shifting between the naval power of Goldenrod and Violet’s Influence).

In the time of Ryoto, it still held immense power over Ecruteak as well, although that swiftly changed with the advent of the Tsuki and Taiyo dynasties.

Goldenrod was the true power, and for much of Johto’s history maintained a status as the de facto capitol. It often shaped alliances and conquered other cities, though with the Wataru entering the field around five hundred years before that changed. The Wataru weren’t able to actually conquer it due to their small numbers, but the fear of a Wataru strike force coming down with dragon fire ensured regular tribute and great respect even from Goldenrod.

Ryoto in particular had built strong relationships with the leaders of Mahogany (a sharp change from the normal hostility) which offered a huge advantage in safeguarding Blackthorn’s borders.

His most important early alliance was with the leaders of Violet City, who he’d recognized as a particular thorn in his side if it came to combat \- the Wataru would be safe no matter what, but their ability to project power would be seriously hampered if Violet’s Skyguard specifically allied with any other cities. He’d spent years before he was even the Drake making inroads there.

Once Violet officially joined the Joh Union, the rest of the pieces Ryoto had set up fell into place rather quickly with minimal bloodshed \- nobody wanted to fight a long, bloody losing battle, and Ryoto had made allies in key places during his time as a Wataru emissary.

He was a great warrior and fighter \- he became Drake, after all \- but Ryoto had a very keen mind for politics and insight into the desires of others. His grand plans and charisma earned him many, many supporters, as did his genuine appreciation and respect for the other cities and cultures of Johto… which, believe me, was very rare amongst the Wataru of the time.

## **Q.1181. If Bruno did evolve him \[King of the Mountain\], what would happen?** 

- ## *Tags: Bruno, Elite Four, Evolution, King of the Mountain, Pokemon Biology, Steelix*

If Bruno evolved the King it would basically be ridiculously powerful. It would basically be utterly invincible physically, and its armor would be so thick the normal Steelix weaknesses to elemental attacks and temperature changes would be completely gone. 

That said, I imagine that it would take several years for the King’s body to fully adapt and reach his full power as a Steelix.

It would really depend on the King, who’s content in his current form. You never know what might happen though\!

## **Q.1182. How does Cynthia fare against Steven in a 6v6 match?**

- ## *Tags: Aerodactyl, Champion, Cynthia, Dov, Dragonite, Gabite, Lance, Lev, Mael, Magnus, Metagross, Pokemon Battle, Princess, Saph, Shelgon, Spiritomb, Steven, Vibrava*


Cynthia is special because her team is especially well-balanced. She’s adapted her team to fill unique roles, and all are extremely powerful in their own right \- I’d say Princess is the best fighter, but then others aren’t far behind. Cynthia just uses them to their maximum potential in combat. 

Common misconception that Spiritomb is getting weaker in every way, which isn’t true. Its offensive abilities are decreasing as it heals, but Spiritomb is growing in other ways.

For Lance…

Dragonite \- Dov \- Magnus \- Aerodactyl \- Lev \- Mael \- Saph \- Gabite \- Vibrava \- Shelgon. 

Aerodactyl, Lev, Mael are in no particular order. 

Steven: Metagross \- Everyone else.

## **Q.1183. On whether you can refuse being a Champion.** 

- ## *Tags: Champion*


I will say that you can always decline the position if you beat Elite Four/Champion \- it’s rare, but happens. Some people don’t want to be tied down, or would prefer to work with the League in a less visible position.

## **Q.1184. On why Steven stopped being a Champion.**

- ## *Tags: ACE Trainer, Champion, Pierce, Steven*


Yep \[To deal with Pierce\]. He did it because he wanted revenge. Pierce’s betrayal hurt and damaged the colony horribly, and Steven was ruled by his heart rather than his head. The idea of letting the ACE trainers hunt Pierce felt too impersonal to him \- he wanted to hunt him down himself.

## **Q.1185. Is Lance the current Drake of Wataru?**

- ## *Tags: Drake, Lance*


Yep, Lance is the current Drake.

## **Q.1186. Are there any other runaway Watarus that hold positions of power elsewhere?**

- ## *Tags: Drake, Lance, Pike, Shamouti Incident*


Yeah, Lance and Pike/Drake had a very awkward meeting regarding the Shamouti Incident. Lance came very close to ending that man’s whole career.

## **Q.1187. Actually do psychics strictly converse through words? Would the more isolated psychics communicate through knowledge? Or feelings or something?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Psychic type*


So, in general psychics communicate mind-to-mind and don’t use words. Thoughts, impressions, concepts, etc. can be filtered directly into another’s mind which is much more efficient and allows for more intimate communication. 

Words are useful, but normally something used with humans. Psychics rarely bother with them otherwise.

## **Q.1188. How does Zoroark work? Can it use its illusion ability before it gets sent out into battle?**

- ## *Tags: Distortion, Flash, Pokemon Biology, Sidney, Zoroark*


Yeah, Zoroark do need a few seconds to interpret their surroundings, but Sidney’s has been trained to go invisible/other illusory effects essentially the moment it’s released.

The good thing is there’s still countless ways to detect a Zoroark. Vibrations, air currents, sound, psychic sense, sensitivity to Distortion \- all things a skilled Zoroark can somewhat account for, but there’s always a limit.

Plus there’s plenty you can do against an invisible opponent \- AoE attacks, for one. Something like Flash. Anything to break their focus and drop the illusions, or make them incapable of fighting in that state.

A well-trained Zoroark is limited pretty much only by its imagination, attention to detail, and the capabilities of its opponent\!

## **Q.1189. Do Zoroark use their illusions as their primary communication?**

- ## *Tags: Pokemon Behaviour, Pokemon Biology, Zoroark*


Yep\! Many of the hidden colonies (I like to think of it as a mirage of Zoroark) have their own distinct languages from manipulating illusions. They can mimic sight and sound \- truly advanced Zoroark can affect other senses to an extent, though it’s difficult \- so the language tends to rely on a complex interplay between the two.

## **Q.1190. What is tragedy?**

- ## *Tags: Ash, Champion, Lance, Meta, Pokemon Battle*


One of my saddest moments was when I lost a massive chunk of Chapter 42 that showed Lance corrupted by the crystal and kicking ass \- he was ripping through the Elite Four and absolutely annihilated Ash. I ended up just writing around the loss unfortunately.

## **Q.1191. Was the King vs Entei scene what replaced that? \[See question \#1190\]**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Crystal Entei, King of the Mountain, Lance, Meta*


Not quite \- I planned on a King vs. Entei scene regardless, but I have it more attention and expanded on it after the Lance scene was wiped.

It also changed the dynamic of the battle against Crystal Entei. I had that image of the team managing to ‘kill’ it for a long team, then the scene with the Beasts arriving and Suicune impaling it, but it was definitely influenced by the removal of Lance’s rampage.

## **Q.1192. Is Lance’s gap exaggerated because it's Lance or is it about that much with every region and their champ.**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Drake, Elite Four, Lance, Pokemon Battle, Steven, Wallace*


Lance has a unique advantage with his focus on flight, but pretty much any Champion would tear through their Elite Four… except for Steven and Wallace, but that’s just because Drake is that much of a badass.

## **Q.1193. Isn't fossil pokemon like, kind of a well-kept secret?**

- ## *Tags: Fossil Pokemon*


Fossils are rare, but common knowledge\!

## **Q.1194. Did names for Pokémon already exist way back? As in, did people 2000 years back, for example, already call Pidgeot such?**

- ## *Tags: Meta*


I’m going to say sort of. Absolutely different names across different areas, but you would probably be able to at least see the roots of the modern names.

## **Q.1195. Is Champion accurate for that, or is it "translated" for current times? \[see question \#1194\]**

- ## *Tags: Champion, Indigo, Mamoru, Meta*


Yep\! Current ones are relatively close. We definitely see some minor ‘translation’ in Champion, but not too much.

The good thing for Pokémon is that they get a good bit of their understanding from their minor psychic abilities \- it lets them learn the language much faster.

But yeah, Mamoru’s only real human connection has been when the Indigo Champions challenge him \- which is kind of sad, really.

## **Q.1196. Is everything on there \[League Move Repository\] official/by the League, or are trainers able to contribute things?**

- ## *Tags: League, Professor Oak, Technology*


Yep\! In Traveler it’s basically a massive repository of information on Pokémon and techniques. Videos, scientific articles, pictures, geographic information \- pretty much anything you can think of.

I’d say it’s mostly coming through and being updated by Professor Oak and his team \- the League is in partnership, but their contributions and the contributions of trusted trainers and other researchers are filtered by Oak.

## **Q.1197. Who was Lance's closest challenger/battle?**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Champion, Dov, Lance, Lorelei, Pokemon Battle*


To be honest, Lance hasn’t had any serious challengers. The few that make it to him rarely get past Dov.

The only real challengers for his position have been internal. Agatha every year or two \- not because she wanted the Mantle by then, but just to keep Lance on his toes \- and Lorelei also attempted challenges against him.

## **Q.1198. Wouldn't anyone that \-got- to him have been more of a serious contender than either by sheer virtue of having beaten the rest of the Elite Four, or is it much more so of a "bad matchup vs Flight Spam" thing there? \[see question \#1197\]**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Champion, Elite Four, Lance, Master Trainer, Pokemon Battle*


Well, to be fair my head canon is only that one or two made it to him in ten years, and the Indigo Elite Four was slightly easier than others, strictly because there was only three Masters to go through before you reached the Champion.

But yeah, with his flight there was pretty much nothing these challengers could do. The jump from Agatha to Lance is a massive one, and you have to adjust to extremely different styles.

They absolutely wouldn’t be making challenges during the last year since stability was needed, but anyone on the Elite Four is extremely competitive. If they thought they had a good shot, they’ll normally take it.

## **Q.1199. The Elite 4 of the Indigo League are getting 2 challengers a year?**

- ## *Tags: Elite Four, Pokemon Battle, Sinnoh*


Yep\! Two potential challengers each year.

See, Sinnoh’s real strategy is exporting Elite Four members to spread their agenda.

## **Q.1200. On Indigo’s Elite Four.**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Elite Four, Indigo, Karen, Lance, Lorelei, Will*


Yep, the gap between the Elite Four was something I took into account. There’s a three year gap in the games, so I introduced Will and Karen early and had them take the place of Lorelei and Agatha… who conveniently left to conquer a region and on a vacation, respectively.

## **Q.1197. Who was Lance's closest challenger/battle?**

- ## *Tags: Agatha, Champion, Dov, Lance, Loelei, Pokemon Battle*


To be honest, Lance hasn’t had any serious challengers. The few that make it to him rarely get past Dov.
